- **T-ENV-12**: No escape sequences → literal `hello\nworld`. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-13**: Inline `#` is part of value. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-14**: Trailing whitespace on value trimmed. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-15**: `KEY = value` → invalid key (space before `=`). Warning on stderr. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-15f**: `KEY= value` → leading space in value preserved. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-15a**: `KEY=` → empty value. Variable is present with empty string. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-15b**: `KEY=a=b=c` → split on first `=`. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-15c**: `1BAD=val` → invalid key, line ignored with warning. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-15d**: `justtext` → malformed line, ignored with warning. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-15e**: Unmatched quotes → literal preserved. *(Spec 8.1)*

#### Local Env Override (`-e`)

- **T-ENV-16**: `-e local.env` loads variables into script. *(Spec 8.2)*
- **T-ENV-17**: `-e nonexistent.env` → error, exit 1. *(Spec 8.2)*
- **T-ENV-17a**: `-e unreadable.env` → error, exit 1. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 8.2)*
- **T-ENV-18**: Global has `X=global`, local has `X=local`. Script sees `local`. *(Spec 8.2)*
- **T-ENV-19**: Global has `A=1`, local has `B=2`. Both present. *(Spec 8.2)*

#### Injection Precedence

- **T-ENV-20**: `LOOPX_BIN` is always set, overrides user values. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-20a**: `LOOPX_BIN` overrides inherited system environment. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-20b**: `LOOPX_BIN` overrides local env file (`-e`) value. Create a local env file containing `LOOPX_BIN=/tmp/fake-binary`. Run with `-e <envfile>`. Script writes `$LOOPX_BIN` to a marker file. Assert marker contains the real injected binary path (a valid executable path that is not `/tmp/fake-binary`). This explicitly tests the highest-precedence layer (loopx-injected) against the second-highest layer (local `-e`) for `LOOPX_BIN`, completing the SPEC 8.3 precedence coverage pattern established by T-ENV-21c for `LOOPX_WORKFLOW`. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-21**: `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` always set, overrides user-supplied value. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-21a**: `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` overrides inherited system environment. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-21b**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW` always set, overrides user-supplied value. Script writes `$LOOPX_WORKFLOW` to a marker file. Set `LOOPX_WORKFLOW=fake` in global env. Assert marker contains the real workflow name. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-21c**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW` overrides local env file (`-e`) value. Create a local env file containing `LOOPX_WORKFLOW=fake`. Run with `-e <envfile>`. Script writes `$LOOPX_WORKFLOW` to a marker file. Assert marker contains the real workflow name, not `"fake"`. This explicitly tests the highest-precedence layer (loopx-injected) against the second-highest layer (local `-e`). *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-21d**: `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` overrides local env file (`-e`) value. Create a local env file containing `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT=/tmp/fake-project-root`. Run with `-e <envfile>`. Script writes `$LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` to a marker file. Assert marker contains the real project root (the invocation cwd), not `/tmp/fake-project-root`. This explicitly tests the highest-precedence layer (loopx-injected) against the second-highest layer (local `-e`) for `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT`, completing the SPEC 8.3 precedence coverage pattern alongside T-ENV-20b (`LOOPX_BIN`) and T-ENV-21c (`LOOPX_WORKFLOW`). *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-21e**: `LOOPX_BIN` overrides global env-file value. Set up a global env file (via `withGlobalEnv`) containing `LOOPX_BIN=/tmp/fake-binary`. Script observes `LOOPX_BIN` via `observe-env`. Assert the marker records the real injected binary path (a valid executable path that is not `/tmp/fake-binary`). T-ENV-20b covers the local `-e` tier for `LOOPX_BIN`; this test closes the global-env-file tier gap, bringing `LOOPX_BIN` precedence coverage up to the same three-tier pattern as `LOOPX_WORKFLOW` (T-ENV-21b / T-ENV-21c / T-ENV-21e-equivalent). *(Spec 8.1, 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-21f**: `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` overrides global env-file value. Set up a global env file containing `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT=/tmp/fake-project-root`. Script observes `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` via `observe-env`. Assert the marker contains the real project root (the invocation cwd), not `/tmp/fake-project-root`. T-ENV-21a covers the inherited-env tier, T-ENV-21d covers the local `-e` tier; this test closes the global-env-file tier gap for `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT`. *(Spec 8.1, 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-21g**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` overrides global env-file value. Set up a global env file containing `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR=/tmp/fake-dir`. Script observes `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` via `observe-env`. Assert the marker contains the real injected workflow directory path, not `/tmp/fake-dir`. T-WFDIR-06 covers the inherited-env tier, T-WFDIR-07 covers the local `-e` tier, T-WFDIR-08 covers the `RunOptions.env` tier; this test closes the global-env-file tier gap for `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. *(Spec 8.1, 8.3, 6.1)*
- **T-ENV-21h**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` overrides global env-file value. Set up a global env file containing `LOOPX_TMPDIR=/tmp/fake-loopx-tmp`. Script observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` via `observe-env`. Assert the marker records the real injected tmpdir path (under `os.tmpdir()`, matching the `loopx-*` naming pattern), **not** `/tmp/fake-loopx-tmp`. Additionally assert the observed path exists as a directory on disk — proving it is the real loopx-created tmpdir, not merely a substitution. T-TMP-30 covers the inherited-env tier and T-TMP-31 covers the local `-e` tier; this test closes the global-env-file tier gap for `LOOPX_TMPDIR`, bringing the precedence-coverage pattern for `LOOPX_TMPDIR` in line with `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`'s full four-tier coverage. *(Spec 8.1, 8.3, 7.4)*
- **T-ENV-22**: System env has `SYS_VAR=sys`, global env has `SYS_VAR=global`. Script sees `global`. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-23**: System env has `SYS_VAR=sys`, no loopx override. Script sees `sys`. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-24**: Full precedence chain. Assert local wins over global over system. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-24a**: `LOOPX_DELEGATED` is visible in script execution environments when inherited. Spawn loopx with `LOOPX_DELEGATED=1` in the inherited process environment. Script uses `observe-env` fixture for `LOOPX_DELEGATED`. Assert marker contains `{ "present": true, "value": "1" }`. The spec does not require loopx to scrub this variable before spawning scripts — it is part of the inherited system environment. *(Spec 8.3, 3.2)*
- **T-ENV-24a2**: `LOOPX_DELEGATED` from the **global** env file reaches spawned scripts. Per SPEC 9.5 / 13, `LOOPX_DELEGATED` is startup-reserved only — **not** script-protocol-protected at tier 1. Env files may supply it to spawned scripts. Set up a global env file (via `withGlobalEnv`) containing `LOOPX_DELEGATED=from-global`. Do **not** set `LOOPX_DELEGATED` in loopx's inherited environment. Script observes `LOOPX_DELEGATED` via `observe-env`. Assert marker records `{ "present": true, "value": "from-global" }`. T-ENV-24a covers the inherited-env tier and T-API-58a covers `RunOptions.env`; this test closes the global-env-file gap so all three supply tiers are covered. *(Spec 8.3, 3.2, 9.5, 13)*
- **T-ENV-24a3**: `LOOPX_DELEGATED` from the **local** env file (`-e`) reaches spawned scripts. Same structure as T-ENV-24a2 but via a local env file: create a local env file containing `LOOPX_DELEGATED=from-local`. Run `loopx run -e <envfile> -n 1 ralph`. Script observes `LOOPX_DELEGATED`. Assert marker records `{ "present": true, "value": "from-local" }`. Completes local-env-file parity alongside T-ENV-24a (inherited), T-ENV-24a2 (global env file), and T-API-58a (`RunOptions.env`). *(Spec 8.3, 3.2, 9.5, 13)*
- **T-ENV-24b**: Empty-string value in local env file overrides non-empty global/system value. *(Spec 8.3)*

#### Env-File Embedded NUL → Spawn Failure

SPEC 7.2 / 9.5 state that runtime rejection of a child environment entry can come from **any env tier** and surfaces as a child launch / spawn failure — "the runtime does not distinguish tiers." The `RunOptions.env` tier is covered (T-API-57 / T-API-57a); these tests close the gap for the local env-file (`-e` / `envFile`) and global env-file tiers.

The spec's env-file parser (SPEC 8.1) rejects keys that do not match `[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*` (so a NUL in a **key** is parser-rejected as a line with an invalid key name, emitting a stderr warning and dropping the line — this path is parser-level, not spawn-level, and already covered by T-ENV-15c for the generic invalid-key case). The spec does not validate NUL in **values** at parse time — values are single-line strings with no escape interpretation, so a literal NUL byte in a value survives parsing. That survived entry reaches the child-spawn step, where the runtime rejects it. Both tests use `writeEnvFileRaw` to write the literal NUL byte into the value.

- **T-ENV-26**: Local env-file (`-e`) with a literal NUL byte in a value surfaces as a spawn failure, not a parser-shape error. Create a local env file at `./.env` via `writeEnvFileRaw(path, "MYVAR=bad\x00val\n")` (a line whose value contains an embedded NUL byte after parsing). Create a valid workflow `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Run `loopx run -e .env -n 1 ralph` via the CLI. Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) stderr contains a child-launch / spawn-failure error referencing the environment-entry rejection (not a parser warning about an invalid key shape), (c) the script did not run (no marker file from `ralph:index`). Per SPEC 7.2, the rejection surfaces as "child launch / spawn failure after tmpdir creation" — `LOOPX_TMPDIR` is created before the spawn step, and its best-effort cleanup runs before the CLI exits with code 1 (assert no `loopx-*` dir remains under `os.tmpdir()`). The failure is distinguishable from parser-level failures (e.g., T-ENV-15c, where the line would be dropped with a parser warning and the loop would still attempt to run). *(Spec 7.2, 8.2, 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-27**: Global env-file with a literal NUL byte in a value surfaces as a spawn failure, not a parser-shape error. Use `withGlobalEnv` to place a global env file containing `MYVAR=bad\x00val` (written via `writeEnvFileRaw` to preserve the literal NUL). Create a valid workflow `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph` via the CLI (no local `-e`). Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) stderr contains a child-launch / spawn-failure error (not a parser warning), (c) the script did not run (no marker file), and (d) `LOOPX_TMPDIR` cleanup ran (no lingering `loopx-*` dir under `os.tmpdir()`). This is the global-env-file tier counterpart to T-ENV-26 (local `-e`) and T-API-57 (`RunOptions.env`), completing the "any env tier can raise a spawn failure" coverage pattern from SPEC 7.2 / 9.5. *(Spec 7.2, 8.1, 8.3)*
- **T-ENV-26a**: Local env-file (`-e`) with a literal NUL byte in a value under the programmatic API surfaces as a spawn failure. Create a local env file at `./.env` via `writeEnvFileRaw(path, "MYVAR=bad\x00val\n")`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { envFile: ".env", maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: the promise rejects with a spawn-failure error (not an `envFile` shape-validation error — the file exists and is readable, and the parser accepts the value). The script did not run. This is the programmatic-API counterpart to T-ENV-26. *(Spec 7.2, 8.2, 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-ENV-27a**: Global env-file with a literal NUL byte in a value under the programmatic API surfaces as a spawn failure. Use `withGlobalEnv` to place a global env file containing `MYVAR=bad\x00val`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: the promise rejects with a spawn-failure error, and the script did not run. This is the programmatic-API counterpart to T-ENV-27 and closes global-env-file NUL-in-value coverage on both run surfaces. *(Spec 7.2, 8.1, 9.3)*

#### Env Caching

- **T-ENV-25**: During a multi-iteration loop, modify the global env file between iterations. Assert the marker contains the original value. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-25a**: During a multi-iteration loop with `-e`, modify the local env file between iterations. Assert original value persists. *(Spec 8.2)*
- **T-ENV-25b**: `loopx run -n 0 ralph` with an unreadable global env file → exits with code 1. Global env loading and validation happens before the `-n 0` short-circuit. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 4.2, 8.1)*
- **T-ENV-25c**: `loopx run -n 0 ralph` with a malformed-but-readable global env file (e.g., containing `1BAD=val`) → exits with code 0, stderr contains a parser warning for the invalid key. Proves global env files are actually parsed under `-n 0`, not just existence/readability checked. This is the global-env counterpart to T-CLI-22c (which covers the local `-e` file under `-n 0`). *(Spec 4.2, 8.1)*

#### `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`

Spec 6.1 and 8.3 make `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` a script-protocol-protected variable derived from the cached discovery-time path of the currently-spawned script. These tests pin down its lifecycle and precedence semantics.

- **T-WFDIR-01**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` is injected into every script spawn. `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` uses `observe-env` on `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. Assert the marker records `{ "present": true, "value": "<abs path>/.loopx/ralph" }` where the value is the absolute path to the workflow directory (no trailing slash, per implementation — or with a trailing slash, per implementation; the assertion treats the two as equivalent if the implementation is consistent across calls). Exit 0. *(Spec 6.1, 8.3)*
- **T-WFDIR-02**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` equals the discovered workflow directory path. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Observe `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` and also record the project root via `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT`. Assert that `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR === path.join(LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT, ".loopx", "ralph")` in the v1 layout. The injected form is derived from the cached discovery path, not recomposed. *(Spec 6.1)*
- **T-WFDIR-03**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` is refreshed per-spawn on intra-workflow goto. `ralph:index` outputs `goto:"check"`, and `ralph:check` observes `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. Both `ralph:index` and `ralph:check` record markers (distinct files keyed by script name). Assert: both markers record `<abs>/.loopx/ralph` — intra-workflow goto preserves the workflow dir. *(Spec 6.1, 8.3)*
- **T-WFDIR-04**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` changes on cross-workflow goto. `ralph:index` outputs `goto:"other:check"`; `other:check` observes `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` into a distinct marker file. Also observe `LOOPX_WORKFLOW` to cross-check. Assert: `ralph:index`'s marker has value `<abs>/.loopx/ralph` and `other:check`'s marker has value `<abs>/.loopx/other` — `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` is refreshed before the B-side spawn. Additionally, cwd remains the project root across the transition (T-EXEC-16b) — `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` is the per-spawn workflow-relative surface, cwd is not. *(Spec 6.1, 8.3)*
- **T-WFDIR-04a**: Deeper cross-workflow chain (A → B → C) observes each workflow's own directory. Three workflows, each with a script that observes `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` into its own marker file before emitting goto to the next. Assert the three markers contain `.loopx/alpha`, `.loopx/beta`, `.loopx/gamma` respectively. *(Spec 6.1)*
- **T-WFDIR-05**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` resets correctly when the loop returns to the starting target. `alpha:index` outputs `goto:"beta:step"`. `beta:step` outputs no goto (loop resets). Both scripts observe `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` appending to a markers log keyed by iteration. Run with `-n 3`. Assert: alpha's log shows `.loopx/alpha` on both its first and third iterations, and beta's log shows `.loopx/beta` on the second iteration — the reset iteration sees `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` set back to the starting workflow's directory. *(Spec 6.1, 2.2)*
- **T-WFDIR-06**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` overrides inherited system-env values of the same name. Spawn loopx with `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR=/tmp/fake-dir` in the inherited process environment. Script observes `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. Assert the marker contains the real injected workflow directory path, not `/tmp/fake-dir`. Protocol variables win at tier 1 (Spec 8.3). *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-WFDIR-07**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` overrides local env file (`-e`) value. Create a local env file containing `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR=/tmp/fake-dir`. Run with `-e <envfile>`. Script observes `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. Assert the marker contains the real injected path, not `/tmp/fake-dir`. This explicitly tests the highest-precedence layer (loopx-injected) against the second-highest layer (local `-e`) for `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`, completing the Spec 8.3 precedence coverage pattern established by T-ENV-20b / T-ENV-21c / T-ENV-21d. *(Spec 8.3)*
- **T-WFDIR-08**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` overrides `RunOptions.env` value. Call `run("ralph", { env: { LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR: "/tmp/fake-dir" } })`. Script observes `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. Assert the marker contains the real injected path, not `/tmp/fake-dir`. Per Spec 8.3, protocol-variable injection is tier 1 and `RunOptions.env` is tier 2 — `RunOptions.env` entries for `LOOPX_*` keys are silently overridden. *(Spec 8.3, 9.5)*
- **T-WFDIR-09**: Bash execution path — `$(dirname "$0") == LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` byte-for-byte, regardless of symlinks. `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` performs: `write-value-to-file "$LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR" <wfdirMarkerPath>` and `write-value-to-file "$(dirname "$0")" <dirnameMarkerPath>`. Both markers are written via the `write-value-to-file` fixture (`printf '%s'`, exact-byte safe, no trailing newline). Assert the two marker files' byte contents are equal. This is a normative Bash invariant per Spec 6.1 "Invocation path" / 6.2 — loopx invokes Bash with the absolute discovery-time path, and Bash does not canonicalize `$0`. *(Spec 6.1, 6.2)*
- **T-WFDIR-10**: Symlinked workflow directory — discovery-time spelling is preserved. Create a real workflow directory at `/tmp/real-workflows/ralph/` (containing `index.sh` that observes `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`). Symlink `<project>/.loopx/ralph → /tmp/real-workflows/ralph`. Run `loopx run ralph`. Assert the marker value includes the symlinked spelling (`<project>/.loopx/ralph`), **not** the realpath (`/tmp/real-workflows/ralph`). Per Spec 6.1, `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` is derived from the discovery-time path and does not apply `realpath`. *(Spec 6.1)*
- **T-WFDIR-11**: Symlinked `.loopx` directory — discovery-time spelling is preserved. Create real workflows at `/tmp/real-loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Symlink `<project>/.loopx → /tmp/real-loopx`. Run `loopx run ralph`. Assert `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` uses the symlinked spelling (`<project>/.loopx/ralph`), not `/tmp/real-loopx/ralph`. *(Spec 6.1)*
- **T-WFDIR-12**: Symlinked entry script file — discovery-time spelling is preserved. Create a real script at `/tmp/real-script.sh`. Symlink `<project>/.loopx/ralph/index.sh → /tmp/real-script.sh`. Run `loopx run ralph`. Assert `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` is the symlinked workflow directory (`<project>/.loopx/ralph`), independent of the entry-script symlink target. Additionally (from T-WFDIR-09's normative Bash equality), `$(dirname "$0")` must equal `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. *(Spec 6.1)*
- **T-WFDIR-13**: Top-level script and a sourced helper both observe the same `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` sources `.loopx/ralph/lib/helper.sh`. Both the top-level script and the helper (sourced into the same process) write `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` to separate marker files. Assert both markers contain identical values. Env vars are injected once per child spawn and inherited by the whole process. *(Spec 6.1)*
- **T-WFDIR-14**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` is a cross-workflow rendezvous anti-pattern sanity check. `alpha:index` writes a file `<LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR>/shared.tmp` then gotos `beta:index`. `beta:index` reads from its **own** `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR/shared.tmp`. Assert `beta:index` reports file-not-found — `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` always points at the currently-spawned script's own workflow and is not a rendezvous point. Documents Spec 6.1's "Cross-workflow rendezvous" clarification that `$LOOPX_TMPDIR` (or a shared fixed location) is the correct rendezvous surface. *(Spec 6.1)*

#### `LOOPX_TMPDIR` (Run-Scoped Temporary Directory)

Spec 7.4 describes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` lifecycle, cleanup, and snapshot semantics. This block is a full coverage pass. All tests use `observe-env` to capture `LOOPX_TMPDIR` into marker files, plus direct filesystem inspection where needed (identity checks, mode, file persistence).

##### Creation and Scope

- **T-TMP-01**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` is created once per run and injected into every script spawn. Run a two-iteration loop where both iterations observe `LOOPX_TMPDIR`. Assert: (a) both markers contain the same absolute path, and (b) the path exists, is a directory, and is non-empty-parented under `os.tmpdir()`. *(Spec 7.4, 8.3)*
- **T-TMP-02**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` is an absolute path. Observe `LOOPX_TMPDIR` in a script. Assert the marker value starts with `/` (POSIX) and equals its own `path.resolve()`. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-03**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` shared across iterations. `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` on each iteration and appends to a log. Run with `-n 3`. Assert all three entries are identical — the tmpdir is stable for the lifetime of the run. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-04**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` shared across intra-workflow goto. `ralph:index` outputs `goto:"check"`; `ralph:check` outputs `stop:true`. Both observe `LOOPX_TMPDIR` into separate markers. Assert identical values. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-05**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` shared across cross-workflow goto. `alpha:index` outputs `goto:"beta:step"`; `beta:step` outputs `stop:true`. Both observe `LOOPX_TMPDIR`. Assert identical values — cross-workflow transitions do not refresh the tmpdir. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-06**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` preserved across loop reset. `alpha:index` outputs `goto:"beta:step"`; `beta:step` outputs no goto (loop resets to `alpha:index`). Both observe `LOOPX_TMPDIR` on each iteration. Run with `-n 3`. Assert all three observations are identical. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-07**: Files written to `LOOPX_TMPDIR` persist within a run. `ralph:index` writes `"hello"` to `$LOOPX_TMPDIR/state.txt` then gotos `ralph:check`. `ralph:check` reads `$LOOPX_TMPDIR/state.txt` and outputs it as `result`. Observe via `runPromise`. Assert the second yielded output's `result` is `"hello"`. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-08**: Concurrent runs get distinct tmpdirs. Launch two `runPromise` invocations in parallel (or two CLI runs) against independent projects. Each records its `LOOPX_TMPDIR` via `observe-env`. Assert the two recorded paths differ. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-09**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` mode is `0700`. After a run starts (and before cleanup), capture the tmpdir path from `observe-env` and `stat` it. Assert the mode bits are exactly `0o700` (owner-only rwx). Use a fixture that records the tmpdir into a marker file but does not remove it before the test's mode check can run — e.g., spawn loopx as a background process, wait for the marker, read tmpdir from it, stat the tmpdir, then allow loopx to complete. *(Spec 7.4)*

##### Not-Created Cases

- **T-TMP-10**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` is **not** created under CLI `-n 0`. Run `loopx run -n 0 ralph`. Script must not spawn (zero iterations), so observing `LOOPX_TMPDIR` inside a script is impossible — instead, snapshot the set of directories in `os.tmpdir()` matching `loopx-*` before and after the run. Assert: no new `loopx-*` directory was created during the `-n 0` run. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-11**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` is **not** created under programmatic `maxIterations: 0`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })`. Snapshot `os.tmpdir()` before and after. Assert no new `loopx-*` directory. Mirrors T-TMP-10 on the programmatic surface. *(Spec 7.4, 9.5)*
- **T-TMP-12**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` is **not** created when pre-iteration failures fire before tmpdir creation. `runPromise("ralph", { envFile: "nonexistent.env" })` — the env-file failure surfaces before tmpdir creation per Spec 7.1 ordering. Snapshot `os.tmpdir()` before and after. Assert no new `loopx-*` directory. Repeat for: missing-workflow, target-validation, invalid-options-shape, and invalid-signal failures. *(Spec 7.4, 7.1, 9.5)*

##### Tmpdir Creation Failure

SPEC 7.2 / 7.4 define behavior when any step of the tmpdir creation sequence fails: loopx does not spawn any child, the CLI exits with code 1, `run()` throws on first `next()`, and `runPromise()` rejects. Best-effort cleanup runs on any partial directory. These tests exercise a real `mkdtemp` failure by setting the tmpdir parent (`TMPDIR`) to a path whose parent directory is unwritable.

- **T-TMP-12a**: CLI — tmpdir creation failure causes exit 1 with no child spawned. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` that writes a marker file on execution. Create an unwritable directory (e.g., `/tmp/loopx-unwritable-parent/` with mode `0500` under non-root). Set `TMPDIR=/tmp/loopx-unwritable-parent/nonexistent` in the CLI's inherited environment (the parent is unwritable, so `mkdtemp` will fail). Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph`. Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) stderr contains a tmpdir-creation-failure error message, (c) the `ralph:index` marker file does **not** exist (no child was spawned), and (d) no `loopx-*` directory was created under the unwritable parent. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 7.2, 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-12b**: `run()` — tmpdir creation failure throws on first `next()`. Same unwritable-parent setup as T-TMP-12a. Call `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` from a driver whose inherited `process.env.TMPDIR` points at the unwritable path. Await `gen.next()`. Assert: the generator throws with a tmpdir-creation-failure error, and the `ralph:index` marker file does not exist. Snapshot `os.tmpdir()` before/after — no `loopx-*` directory created. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 7.2, 7.4, 9.1)*
- **T-TMP-12c**: `runPromise()` — tmpdir creation failure rejects. Same unwritable-parent setup. Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: the promise rejects with a tmpdir-creation-failure error, and no child was spawned (marker file absent). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 7.2, 7.4, 9.2)*

##### Tmpdir Creation Sub-step Coverage Gaps (Not Directly Covered)

SPEC 7.4 "Creation order" normatively specifies three sub-steps and distinct behavior when each one fails:

1. `mkdtemp` itself fails → no path exists, no cleanup needed.
2. Identity capture fails (after `mkdtemp` succeeded) → loopx attempts a single non-recursive `rmdir` on the path, outside the race-resistant guarantee.
3. Mode-securing fails (after `mkdtemp` and identity capture succeeded) → full identity-fingerprint cleanup-safety routine runs.

T-TMP-12a / T-TMP-12b / T-TMP-12c cover sub-step 1 (`mkdtemp` failure) by configuring an unwritable parent. **Sub-steps 2 and 3 are not directly covered by the current test suite.**

- **T-TMP-12d (not yet directly covered)**: Identity capture failure (sub-step 2 of SPEC 7.4's creation order). Forcing `mkdtemp` to succeed while `stat` on the created directory fails is not reliably reproducible black-box under POSIX semantics — the operation is path-based on a directory that was just created by the same process. A fault-injection seam analogous to the install-fault seams in section 1.4 (e.g., `LOOPX_TEST_TMPDIR_FAULT=identity-capture-fail`) would make this deterministically testable; without that seam, this sub-path is only exercised via incidental filesystem races. This gap is tracked as a known coverage limitation of SPEC 7.4 rather than claimed as covered.
- **T-TMP-12e (not yet directly covered)**: Mode-securing failure (sub-step 3 of SPEC 7.4's creation order). Forcing `mkdtemp` + identity capture to succeed while `chmod` / mode-verification fails is similarly not reliably reproducible black-box — the same process owns the directory it just created. A fault-injection seam (e.g., `LOOPX_TEST_TMPDIR_FAULT=mode-secure-fail`) would make this deterministically testable, including the "full identity-fingerprint cleanup-safety routine runs" contract. Until such a seam is declared in section 1.4, this sub-path is tracked as a known coverage limitation of SPEC 7.4.

**Implementer note.** If coverage of sub-steps 2 and 3 is required for acceptance, the recommendation is to add a `LOOPX_TEST_TMPDIR_FAULT` env-var test-only seam to section 1.4 (gated on `NODE_ENV=test`, same pattern as `LOOPX_TEST_INSTALL_FAULT` and `LOOPX_TEST_AUTOINSTALL_FAULT`) accepting values `identity-capture-fail` and `mode-secure-fail`, and convert the two tests above into executable entries. Without the seam, the traceability matrix for SPEC 7.4 should not claim these sub-paths as directly covered.

##### Cleanup Triggers

- **T-TMP-13**: Cleanup on normal completion (`stop:true`). `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`, writes `$LOOPX_TMPDIR/file.txt`, then outputs `stop:true`. Run CLI. Parse the tmpdir path from the marker. Assert: after loopx exits (exit 0), the tmpdir no longer exists. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-14**: Cleanup on normal completion (`-n` reached). Same fixture but no `stop:true`; run with `-n 1`. Assert the tmpdir is removed after loopx exits 0. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-15**: Cleanup on non-zero script exit. Script observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` into a marker, then `exit 1`. Assert: loopx exits 1, and the tmpdir captured in the marker no longer exists. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-16**: Cleanup on invalid goto. Script emits `goto:"nonexistent-workflow:script"`. Assert: loopx exits 1, tmpdir (captured from a prior `LOOPX_TMPDIR` observation) removed. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-17**: Cleanup on SIGINT. Use `runCLIWithSignal`. Fixture observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` into marker, writes "ready" to stderr, then sleeps. Harness `waitForStderr("ready")`, reads tmpdir from marker, sends SIGINT. Assert: loopx exits 130, and the tmpdir is removed. *(Spec 7.4, 7.3)*
- **T-TMP-18**: Cleanup on SIGTERM. Same as T-TMP-17 but SIGTERM and exit 143. *(Spec 7.4, 7.3)*
- **T-TMP-19**: Cleanup on programmatic `AbortSignal` abort. `const c = new AbortController(); const gen = run("ralph", { signal: c.signal }); const out = await gen.next(); c.abort();` where the script observed `LOOPX_TMPDIR` during its first iteration. Await the next `gen.next()` (expected to throw the abort error). Assert: tmpdir is removed before the thrown error surfaces — read the tmpdir path from the marker *after* the throw to confirm, or check during a `try { await gen.next() } catch {}` block followed by a `fs.existsSync(tmpdir)` check. *(Spec 7.4, 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-TMP-20**: Cleanup on generator cancellation via `.return()` after first `next()`. Script observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`, then blocks (long-running). `const gen = run("ralph"); const first = await gen.next(); await gen.return(undefined);` — generator settles. Assert: tmpdir (from `first.value`'s side-effect marker) is removed. *(Spec 7.4, 9.1)*
- **T-TMP-21**: Cleanup on generator cancellation via `.throw()` after first `next()`. Same fixture as T-TMP-20 but uses `gen.throw(new Error("bye"))`. Catch the thrown error. Assert the tmpdir is removed. *(Spec 7.4, 9.1)*
- **T-TMP-22**: Cleanup on `break` after yield. `for await (const o of run("ralph")) { break; }`. The fixture yielded `LOOPX_TMPDIR` via observation into a marker. Assert tmpdir removed after the `for await` block exits. *(Spec 7.4, 9.1)*

##### Final-Yield-vs-Settlement Carve-out

- **T-TMP-23**: After the final yield, cleanup is guaranteed only once the generator settles. `const gen = run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 });` with fixture that observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`. Do `const { value } = await gen.next();` — this is the first and final yield. Read tmpdir from marker. Without calling `gen.next()` / `.return()` / `.throw()` again, assert: tmpdir may still exist at this observation point (implementation-defined). Then call `await gen.next()` (expecting `{ done: true }`). After settlement, assert tmpdir is removed. This documents Spec 7.4's nuance that abandoning the generator after the final yielded value may leak the tmpdir. *(Spec 7.4, 9.1)*
- **T-TMP-24**: Cleanup via full `for await` completion. Same fixture as T-TMP-23 but consume via `for await` until the generator completes naturally. Assert tmpdir is removed after the `for await` loop exits — `for await` drives settlement automatically. *(Spec 7.4, 9.1)*

##### Tmpdir Parent Snapshot Timing

- **T-TMP-25**: CLI — tmpdir parent determined pre-iteration. Set `TMPDIR=/tmp/loopx-test-parent-A` in the CLI environment. Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph` with fixture observing `LOOPX_TMPDIR`. Assert the tmpdir lives under `/tmp/loopx-test-parent-A/` — the parent was captured at pre-iteration time from loopx's own inherited env. *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-26**: `run()` — tmpdir parent captured lazily on first `next()`. `process.env.TMPDIR = "/tmp/loopx-parent-A"; const gen = run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 }); process.env.TMPDIR = "/tmp/loopx-parent-B"; await gen.next();` (script observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`). Assert: the tmpdir lives under `/tmp/loopx-parent-B` — the mutation between `run()` returning and first `next()` does affect the parent (the snapshot is lazy). *(Spec 7.4, 9.1)*
- **T-TMP-27**: `runPromise()` — tmpdir parent captured eagerly at call site. `process.env.TMPDIR = "/tmp/loopx-parent-A"; const p = runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 }); process.env.TMPDIR = "/tmp/loopx-parent-B"; await p;` (script observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`). Assert: the tmpdir lives under `/tmp/loopx-parent-A` — the mutation *after* `runPromise()` returned did not redirect the parent (eager snapshot at call site). *(Spec 7.4, 9.2)*
- **T-TMP-28**: `TMPDIR` from env files does **not** redirect loopx's own tmpdir parent. Place `TMPDIR=/tmp/wrong-parent` in a global env file. Set the loopx inherited `TMPDIR=/tmp/right-parent`. Run loopx; fixture observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`. Assert the tmpdir lives under `/tmp/right-parent`. Env-file entries reach spawned scripts but do not mutate loopx's own `process.env` and so do not redirect `os.tmpdir()`. *(Spec 7.4, 8.3)*
- **T-TMP-29**: `TMPDIR` from `RunOptions.env` does **not** redirect loopx's own tmpdir parent. Set loopx inherited `TMPDIR=/tmp/right-parent`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { env: { TMPDIR: "/tmp/wrong-parent" } })`. Script observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`. Assert tmpdir lives under `/tmp/right-parent`. `RunOptions.env` merges into the child environment; it does not mutate loopx's own `process.env`. *(Spec 7.4, 9.5)*

##### Cleanup Safety (Identity-Fingerprint, Symlink / Non-Directory / Mismatched Directory)

SPEC 7.4 "Identity-fingerprint cleanup safety" defines normative rules for cleanup dispatch: symlinks are unlinked without following, regular files and mismatched directories are left with a warning, and nested symlink entries are unlinked but not traversed. SPEC 7.4 also specifies that **loopx does not reap stale tmpdirs at startup** and **does not chase renamed-away tmpdirs**. These rules are black-box testable and must be covered.

All tests in this block use a fixture that observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` into a marker, then performs the relevant filesystem manipulation on the reported path (rename, replacement with symlink, replacement with regular file, or nested symlink creation) before loopx exits. Tests inspect the filesystem after loopx exits to verify the safety rules held.

- **T-TMP-32**: No stale-tmpdir reaping at startup. Before running loopx, pre-create a directory matching the `loopx-*` naming pattern directly under `os.tmpdir()` (e.g., `<os.tmpdir()>/loopx-stale-xyz/`) with a marker file inside. Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph` against a normal fixture. After loopx exits 0, assert: (a) the pre-created `loopx-stale-xyz/` directory still exists with its marker file intact, and (b) loopx's own freshly-created `loopx-*` directory (observed via `observe-env` on `LOOPX_TMPDIR`) has been cleaned up. Per SPEC 7.4 "loopx does not reap stale tmpdirs at startup". *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-33**: Renamed-away tmpdir is not chased. Fixture observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`, writes a marker `initialized` into it, then renames the tmpdir directory itself (e.g., `mv "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" "$LOOPX_TMPDIR-renamed"` — performed before the script exits), then emits `stop:true`. After loopx exits 0, assert: (a) the original tmpdir path (which is now gone due to the rename) does not exist, (b) the renamed path (`-renamed` suffix) **still exists** with the `initialized` marker intact — loopx did not chase the renamed directory and did not remove it. Per SPEC 7.4 "A script that removes or renames its tmpdir during the run defeats automatic cleanup of the moved directory; loopx does not chase renamed tmpdirs." *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-34**: Cleanup of a symlink replacement removes the symlink entry only, not the target. Fixture observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`, writes a marker `target-marker` inside an external directory (e.g., `$LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT/target-survives/target-marker`), then `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` and `ln -s "$LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT/target-survives" "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"`, then emits `stop:true`. After loopx exits 0, assert: (a) the `$LOOPX_TMPDIR` path no longer exists (loopx unlinked the symlink entry), (b) the external `target-survives/` directory still exists with `target-marker` intact (loopx did not follow the symlink target). Per SPEC 7.4 cleanup-safety rule 2: "Path is a symlink: unlink the symlink entry; do not follow the target." *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-35**: Cleanup leaves a regular-file replacement in place with a warning. Fixture observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`, then `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` and `printf '%s' "regular-file-replacement" > "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` (tmpdir path is now a regular file), then emits `stop:true`. After loopx exits 0, assert: (a) the `$LOOPX_TMPDIR` path exists and is a regular file with content `regular-file-replacement`, (b) stderr contains a single cleanup warning mentioning the non-directory path, (c) the CLI exit code is unaffected (still 0). Per SPEC 7.4 cleanup-safety rule 3: "Path is a regular file ... : leave in place with a stderr warning." *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-36**: Cleanup leaves a mismatched-directory replacement in place with a warning. Fixture observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`, then `rm -rf "$LOOPX_TMPDIR"` and creates a **different** directory at the same path (e.g., `mkdir "$LOOPX_TMPDIR" && touch "$LOOPX_TMPDIR/mismatched-marker"`). Because the new directory's device/inode differs from the identity fingerprint loopx captured at tmpdir creation, it is a mismatched directory per SPEC 7.4 rule 5. Script emits `stop:true`. After loopx exits 0, assert: (a) the `$LOOPX_TMPDIR` path exists and is a directory, (b) the `mismatched-marker` file inside still exists — loopx did not recursively remove it, (c) stderr contains a single cleanup warning mentioning the mismatched directory. Per SPEC 7.4 rule 5: "Path is a directory whose identity does not match: leave in place with a stderr warning." *(Spec 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-37**: Recursive cleanup unlinks nested symlink entries without traversing targets. Fixture observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`, creates an external target (e.g., `$LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT/external-target-dir/` containing `external-file`), then creates a nested symlink `$LOOPX_TMPDIR/nested-link -> $LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT/external-target-dir`, emits `stop:true`. After loopx exits 0, assert: (a) `$LOOPX_TMPDIR` has been removed (recursive cleanup ran, matching identity), (b) `$LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT/external-target-dir/` still exists with `external-file` intact — the recursive walk unlinked the nested symlink entry but did not follow through to delete its target contents. Per SPEC 7.4 rule 4: "Symlink entries encountered during the walk are unlinked but not traversed, so symlinks pointing outside the tmpdir do not collateral-delete their targets." *(Spec 7.4)*

##### Cleanup Idempotence and Warning Cardinality (Not Directly Covered)

SPEC 7.2 / 7.4 specify strong guarantees around cleanup that are difficult to force deterministically in black-box tests:

- **At most one cleanup attempt per created `LOOPX_TMPDIR`** over the lifetime of the run — racing terminal triggers (SIGTERM during cleanup of a prior SIGINT; abort concurrent with consumer `.return()` / `.throw()`; non-zero exit concurrent with abort; abort after final yield concurrent with a consumer `.throw()`; child spawn failure concurrent with abort; abort concurrent with tmpdir creation failure) do not start a second cleanup attempt.
- **At most one cleanup-related stderr warning per run.** Combined with the idempotence rule, every run emits at most one cleanup warning regardless of how many concurrent terminal triggers or cleanup-safety rules fire.

Existing T-TMP-35 / T-TMP-36 assert "a single cleanup warning" for the regular-file-replacement and mismatched-directory-replacement cases respectively, which are the two normatively-warning cleanup-safety branches. But the **racing-trigger idempotence** and **at-most-one-warning across racing triggers** guarantees are not directly covered — those require deterministic coordination of two terminal triggers (e.g., SIGINT then SIGTERM during the post-SIGINT cleanup window) that black-box tests cannot reliably produce without a fault-injection or coordination seam.

- **T-TMP-38 (not yet directly covered)**: Cleanup idempotence under racing SIGINT → SIGTERM (terminal trigger during cleanup of a prior terminal trigger). Deterministically reproducing "SIGTERM during cleanup of a prior SIGINT" requires either (a) an injection seam that pauses loopx in the middle of cleanup so the harness can send the second signal, or (b) a timing-fragile coordination that races the child process group's exit against the cleanup routine. Neither is reliably reproducible black-box without a new test-only seam (e.g., `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_DELAY_MS=500` to widen the in-cleanup window, or a sentinel stderr marker emitted at cleanup start analogous to the pre-iteration sentinel in section 1.4). This gap is tracked as a known coverage limitation of SPEC 7.2's "at most one cleanup attempt" guarantee.
- **T-TMP-39 (not yet directly covered)**: At-most-one-warning cardinality across racing terminal triggers. Same reproducibility problem as T-TMP-38 — two cleanup-warning-emitting branches (e.g., racing mismatched-directory and symlink-replacement states, or racing SIGINT during a post-SIGINT mismatched-dir cleanup) cannot be deterministically driven black-box without a coordination seam. Tracked as a known coverage limitation of SPEC 7.4's "at most one cleanup warning per run" guarantee.

**Implementer note.** If coverage of these invariants is required for acceptance, the recommendation is to add a `LOOPX_TEST_CLEANUP_DELAY_MS` env-var seam to section 1.4 (gated on `NODE_ENV=test`) plus a cleanup-start sentinel stderr marker (same pattern as the pre-iteration sentinel in section 1.4). The seam would let the harness observe "cleanup has begun" and deliver a second terminal trigger inside the widened cleanup window; tests could then assert warning cardinality and idempotence deterministically. Without the seam, the traceability matrix for SPEC 7.2 / 7.4 should not claim these invariants as directly covered.

##### `LOOPX_TMPDIR` Protocol-Variable Precedence

Spec 8.3 makes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` a **script-protocol-protected variable** that must override user-supplied values from every lower tier. These tests complete the precedence-coverage pattern established by `LOOPX_BIN` / `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` / `LOOPX_WORKFLOW` / `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` (T-ENV-20b / T-ENV-21a–21d / T-WFDIR-06–08), which each have symmetric inherited-env and env-file precedence tests. Without these, a buggy implementation could special-case `LOOPX_TMPDIR` to be read from inherited env or an env file instead of freshly injected from its own tmpdir-creation step.

- **T-TMP-30**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` overrides inherited-env values of the same name. Spawn loopx with `LOOPX_TMPDIR=/tmp/fake-loopx-tmp` in the inherited process environment. Script observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR` via `observe-env`. Assert the marker records the real injected tmpdir path (under `os.tmpdir()`, matching the `loopx-*` naming pattern), **not** `/tmp/fake-loopx-tmp`. Additionally assert the observed path exists as a directory on disk — proving it is the real loopx-created tmpdir, not merely a substitution. Protocol variables win at tier 1 (SPEC 8.3). This is the `LOOPX_TMPDIR` counterpart to T-WFDIR-06 (`LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` override) and T-ENV-21a (`LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` override). *(Spec 8.3, 7.4)*
- **T-TMP-31**: `LOOPX_TMPDIR` overrides local env file (`-e`) value. Create a local env file containing `LOOPX_TMPDIR=/tmp/fake-loopx-tmp`. Run `loopx run -e <envfile> -n 1 ralph`. Script observes `LOOPX_TMPDIR`. Assert the marker contains the real injected tmpdir path, not `/tmp/fake-loopx-tmp`. This is the `-e` local env-file counterpart to T-TMP-30. Completes the SPEC 8.3 precedence coverage for `LOOPX_TMPDIR` alongside the inherited-env tier (T-TMP-30) and the global env-file tier (which loopx treats identically to the local `-e` tier for protocol-variable override — any env-file value is below the tier-1 protocol injection). Mirrors T-WFDIR-07 (`LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` vs `-e`) and T-ENV-21c (`LOOPX_WORKFLOW` vs `-e`). *(Spec 8.3, 7.4)*

#### `PWD` Non-Protocol Behavior

Spec 6.1 / 8.3 / 13 explicitly declare `PWD` to be **outside** the script-protocol-protected tier. These tests pin down that `PWD` is not reserved or protected by loopx.

**Fixture note.** Exact-value `PWD` passthrough assertions use a **TS fixture reading `process.env.PWD`** (via the existing `observe-env` fixture with variable name `PWD`), not Bash `$PWD`. Per SPEC 6.1 / 8.3 / 13, Bash `$PWD` is shell-maintained and subject to normal POSIX / Bash semantics — Bash may rewrite `$PWD` during shell startup, so exact byte-for-byte equality between Bash `$PWD` and a caller-supplied value is not a loopx guarantee. The TS `observe-env` fixture reads `process.env.PWD` directly via Node / Bun's env-map accessor, which preserves the inherited value byte-for-byte and does not apply shell-level PWD semantics. The Bash `observe-pwd` fixture is retained only for tests that specifically want to observe Bash's shell-managed `$PWD` variable (none of the T-PWD-* exact-value tests below).

- **T-PWD-01**: loopx does not reserve/protect `PWD`. TS script observes `PWD` via `observe-env` (reading `process.env.PWD` directly, not Bash `$PWD` — see fixture note above). Spawn loopx with a specific `PWD=/some/inherited/value` in the inherited environment (using `execa`'s `env` option). Assert the marker records `{ "present": true, "value": "/some/inherited/value" }` — loopx did not unset, override, or rewrite `PWD`. Using `process.env.PWD` (not Bash `$PWD`) ensures the assertion is against the byte-for-byte inherited value rather than Bash's shell-level POSIX rewrite. *(Spec 6.1, 8.3, 13)*
- **T-PWD-02**: `RunOptions.env.PWD` reaches spawned scripts. Call `runPromise("ralph", { env: { PWD: "/value-from-run-options" } })`. TS script observes `PWD` via `observe-env`. Assert marker records `{ "present": true, "value": "/value-from-run-options" }` — `RunOptions.env` (tier 2, Spec 8.3) supplies `PWD` unchanged because `PWD` is not at tier 1. The TS fixture is used so the assertion is against the env-map value, bypassing Bash's shell-level PWD rewrite. *(Spec 6.1, 8.3, 9.5)*
- **T-PWD-03**: Inherited `PWD` propagates unchanged when neither env file nor `RunOptions.env` sets it. Spawn with `PWD=/inherited`. TS script observes `PWD` via `observe-env`. Assert marker records `{ "present": true, "value": "/inherited" }`. TS fixture used for the same reason as T-PWD-01/02. *(Spec 6.1, 8.3)*
- **T-PWD-04**: Protocol variables (Spec 8.3 table) do **not** include `PWD`. A TS script enumerates `process.env` and writes the keys as JSON via `fs.writeFileSync`. Assert: (a) `LOOPX_BIN`, `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT`, `LOOPX_WORKFLOW`, `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`, and `LOOPX_TMPDIR` are all present; (b) `PWD` is either present (with the inherited value) or absent (if not in the loopx parent's env) — it is not forcibly injected. More importantly: when loopx is spawned without `PWD` in its own environment (e.g., `env -i node cli.js run ralph`), the script's `PWD` must **not** be present — proving loopx does not synthesize a `PWD` value when none is inherited. *(Spec 6.1, 8.3, 13)*
- **T-PWD-05 (non-normative)**: *This item is a non-normative reminder, not an executable test.* Run help (Spec 11.2) does not currently document protocol variables, so a literal "`PWD` must not appear in `loopx run -h` stdout" assertion would be vacuous. If a future change introduces a protocol-variables help/docs section to the CLI, the implementer should remember that `PWD` must not be listed as an injected variable per Spec 6.1 / 8.3 / 13 — convert this item back into an executable test at that point. *(Spec 6.1, 11.2)*
- **T-PWD-06**: CLI project root uses `process.cwd()`, not inherited `PWD`. SPEC 3.2 / 6.1 explicitly say "loopx does not consult `$PWD`" for project-root derivation — the CLI reads loopx's own `process.cwd()`. Spawn loopx with `PWD=/bogus-value-that-does-not-exist` in the inherited environment, while the actual kernel cwd (via the child-spawn's `cwd` option) is a real project directory (e.g., `/tmp/real-project/` containing `.loopx/ralph/index.ts`). TS fixture writes `$LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` via `observe-env` to a marker, also writes `process.cwd()` via `observe-cwd-ts`, and also writes the inherited `PWD` via `observe-env` with variable name `PWD` (reading `process.env.PWD` — not Bash `$PWD`, per the fixture note above). Assert: (a) `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` equals the kernel cwd (something like `/tmp/real-project`), **not** `/bogus-value-that-does-not-exist`, (b) `process.cwd()` likewise reports the real cwd (directory identity matches; exact string spelling may be runtime-canonicalized), and (c) the `PWD`-via-`observe-env` marker records `{ "present": true, "value": "/bogus-value-that-does-not-exist" }` (inherited `PWD` passed through unchanged to the child per T-PWD-01, but loopx itself did not use it). This pins down the "loopx does not consult `$PWD`" rule concretely on the CLI project-root path — the existing T-PWD-* tests cover `PWD` passthrough but not that loopx ignores `PWD` for its own purposes. The TS fixture is used for the `PWD`-passthrough assertion so the comparison is against the env-map value rather than Bash's shell-level rewrite. *(Spec 3.2, 6.1, 13)*

#### Symlink / Project-Root Spelling

Spec 3.2 / 6.1 declare loopx preserves discovery-time and caller-supplied spellings rather than canonicalizing via `realpath`. These tests close coverage gaps around symlinks on the project root and `.loopx/` layout.

- **T-SYM-01**: Symlinked `.loopx` directory works end-to-end. Real workflows at `/tmp/real-loopx/ralph/index.sh` (outputs `stop:true`). Symlink `<project>/.loopx → /tmp/real-loopx`. `loopx run ralph` → exits 0, script executed. (Paired with T-WFDIR-11 which adds the env-var spelling assertion.) *(Spec 5.1, 6.1)*
- **T-SYM-02**: CLI invocation from a symlinked project-root spelling — `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` is loopx's own `process.cwd()`. Real project at `/tmp/real-project/`. Symlink `/tmp/link-project → /tmp/real-project`. `cd /tmp/link-project && loopx run ralph`. Under POSIX, `getcwd(3)` typically canonicalizes, so loopx's `process.cwd()` is `/tmp/real-project`; `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` is that canonical string. Fixture observes `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT`. Assert marker matches `/tmp/real-project` (the canonicalized form), not `/tmp/link-project`. Spec 6.1 "Directory identity vs. string spelling" — CLI `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` is the `process.cwd()` spelling, which under POSIX is canonical. *(Spec 3.2, 6.1)*
- **T-SYM-03**: Programmatic `cwd` preserves symlink spelling (no `realpath`). Real project at `/tmp/real-project/`. Symlink `/tmp/link-project → /tmp/real-project`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { cwd: "/tmp/link-project", maxIterations: 1 })`. Fixture observes `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT`. Assert marker is `/tmp/link-project` — the symlink spelling supplied via `RunOptions.cwd` is preserved verbatim, not canonicalized. *(Spec 3.2, 6.1, 9.5)*
- **T-SYM-04**: Programmatic `cwd` under a symlinked ancestor is preserved verbatim. Real project at `/tmp/real-outer/proj/`. Symlink `/tmp/link-outer → /tmp/real-outer`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { cwd: "/tmp/link-outer/proj", maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` is `/tmp/link-outer/proj` — lexical resolution via `path.resolve` only, no `realpath`. *(Spec 3.2, 6.1, 9.5)*
- **T-SYM-05**: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` uses cached discovery-time spelling, not recomposition. `<project>/.loopx` is a real directory; `<project>/.loopx/ralph` is a symlink to `/tmp/real-ralph/` (where `/tmp/real-ralph/index.sh` lives). Run `loopx run ralph`. Observe `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` and `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`. Assert: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR == "<project>/.loopx/ralph"` (the discovered, symlinked spelling) — **not** `/tmp/real-ralph`, and **not** the lexically-recomposed `path.join(LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT, ".loopx", "ralph")` if lexical recomposition would diverge from the cached discovery path. For the symlink-on-`.loopx/<workflow>` case those happen to coincide, so this test uses a second project where `<project>/.loopx` itself is a symlink to `/tmp/real-loopx`, and `<project>/.loopx/ralph` is a plain directory underneath — then `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` must be `<project>/.loopx/ralph` (the cached path at discovery time), not `/tmp/real-loopx/ralph` (the realpath-canonicalized form). *(Spec 6.1)*

### 4.8 Module Resolution & Script Helpers

**Spec refs:** 3.3, 3.4, 6.4, 6.5

#### `import from "loopx"` Resolution

- **T-MOD-01**: A TS script in a workflow with `import { output } from "loopx"` runs successfully under Node.js. `[Node]` *(Spec 3.3)*
- **T-MOD-02**: Same import works under Bun. `[Bun]` *(Spec 3.3)*
- **T-MOD-03**: A JS script with `import { output } from "loopx"` also works. *(Spec 3.3)*
- **T-MOD-03a**: A workflow that has its own `node_modules/loopx` (a different version) resolves `import from "loopx"` to the **local** package, not the running CLI's package. Standard module resolution applies — the closest `node_modules` wins. The workflow-local `node_modules/loopx` package must export a sentinel value (e.g., a unique marker string from a custom `output()` or an additional export) that differs from the CLI-provided package. The test script imports from `"loopx"` and writes the sentinel to a marker file. Assert: (a) the marker file contains the workflow-local sentinel, proving the local package was actually loaded (not just that the CLI didn't warn), and (b) **no warning is emitted on stderr** — per Spec 3.3, no warning is emitted for workflow-local `node_modules/loopx` resolution in v1. *(Spec 3.3, 2.1)*
- **T-MOD-03b**: Combined precedence: project-root delegation is active (project-root `package.json` declares `loopx`, `node_modules/.bin/loopx` exists) **and** the target workflow has its own `node_modules/loopx` with a different sentinel export. The test script imports from `"loopx"` and writes the resolved sentinel to a marker file. Assert: the marker file contains the **workflow-local** sentinel, not the project-root delegated package's sentinel. This tests the full Spec 3.3 precedence chain — delegation determines which CLI binary runs, but `import "loopx"` within a script resolves to the closest `node_modules/loopx` (the workflow-local one), not the delegated project-root one. T-MOD-03a tests workflow-local vs. CLI without delegation; T-DEL-06 tests delegation without workflow-local; this test combines both and asserts the workflow-local package wins. *(Spec 3.3, 3.2)*
- **T-MOD-03c**: Workflow-level `package.json` `type` field is respected for intra-workflow `.js` module resolution. Create `.loopx/ralph/package.json` with `{ "type": "module" }`, `.loopx/ralph/lib/helper.js` containing `export const value = "esm-resolved";` (ESM named export), and `.loopx/ralph/index.ts` that does `import { value } from "./lib/helper.js"; import { output } from "loopx"; output({ result: value });`. Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph` under Node.js. Assert: (a) exit code 0, and (b) output result is `"esm-resolved"`. The `.ts` entry point is executed via tsx, but the imported `.js` helper in `lib/` is resolved through Node.js's standard module system, where the nearest `package.json` `type` field determines whether `.js` files are treated as ESM. This verifies that loopx's execution model (workflow directory as cwd, per Spec 6.1) correctly exposes the workflow's `package.json` `type` field to Node.js module resolution for intra-workflow imports. `[Node]` *(Spec 2.1, 3.3)*
- **T-MOD-03d**: Symlink caveat for JS/TS entry paths — under a symlinked entry path, a workflow-local `node_modules/loopx` on the **logical** path may not win, and loopx emits no warning. `[Node]` SPEC 3.3's "Symlink caveat for JS/TS entry paths" clarifies that Node's default main-module handling applies `realpath` to the main module's file path, so when the absolute discovery-time entry path traverses any symlink, the resolver walks up from the canonical target rather than the symlink-preserving spelling. Set up: a real workflow directory at `/tmp/real-workflow/` with `index.ts` containing `import { output } from "loopx"; output({ result: globalThis.__LOOPX_SENTINEL ?? "from-global" });` (or equivalent sentinel-reading import). Do **not** install a `node_modules/loopx` at `/tmp/real-workflow/`. Create a project at `/tmp/project/` and symlink `/tmp/project/.loopx/ralph -> /tmp/real-workflow/`. Install a workflow-local `node_modules/loopx` at `/tmp/project/.loopx/ralph/node_modules/loopx/` (on the *logical* path) whose exported `output()` writes a sentinel distinguishable from the global/CLI version (e.g., the exported `output()` sets `globalThis.__LOOPX_SENTINEL = "from-workflow-local"` before serializing, or the package's sentinel export is importable and differs). Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph` under Node.js from `/tmp/project/`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, and (b) the output result is `"from-global"` (or the CLI-provided sentinel), **not** `"from-workflow-local"` — Node's main-module `realpath` resolved the entry to `/tmp/real-workflow/index.ts`, and the resolver walked up from `/tmp/real-workflow/` rather than the symlink-preserving `/tmp/project/.loopx/ralph/`, so the workflow-local `node_modules/loopx` is not on the resolved module-resolution path. Additionally assert (c): stderr contains **no warning** about the workflow-local `node_modules/loopx` being bypassed — per SPEC 3.3 "No warning is emitted for this scenario in v1." T-MOD-03a covers the normal (non-symlinked) precedence where workflow-local wins; this test is the symlink-caveat counterpart and locks down the documented exception. `[Node]` *(Spec 3.3)*

#### `output()` Function

- **T-MOD-04**: `output({ result: "hello" })`. Observe via `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`: yielded Output has `result: "hello"`. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-05**: `output({ result: "x", goto: "check" })`. Observe via `run("ralph")`: yielded Output has both fields, and loopx transitions. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-05a**: TS/JS script `alpha:index` calls `output({ goto: "beta:index" })`; `beta:index` writes a marker file and then calls `output({ stop: true })`. Assert `beta:index` executed (marker file exists). This is a positive end-to-end test for a JS/TS `output()` cross-workflow goto: T-MOD-05 covers intra-workflow goto and T-LOOP-05 covers cross-workflow goto generally, but no existing test exercises a JS/TS `output()` emitting a qualified `workflow:script` target that the loop follows. *(Spec 6.4, 2.2)*
- **T-MOD-06**: `output({ stop: true })`. Loop completes after one iteration. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-07**: `output({})` (no known fields). Script crashes with non-zero exit code. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-08**: `output(null)`. Script crashes. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-09**: `output(undefined)`. Script crashes. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-10**: `output("string")`. Yielded Output has `result: "string"`. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-11**: `output(42)`. Yielded Output has `result: "42"`. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-12**: `output(true)`. Yielded Output has `result: "true"`. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13**: `output({ result: "x", goto: undefined })`. Yielded Output has `result: "x"` and no `goto` property. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13a**: `output([1, 2, 3])` (array, no known fields). Script crashes. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13b**: `output({ result: undefined, goto: undefined, stop: undefined })`. Equivalent to `output({})`. Script crashes. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13c**: `output({ foo: "bar" })`. Script crashes (no known fields). *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13d**: `output({ stop: false })`. Output accepted, but parsed as `{}` (stop must be exactly true). Loop continues. *(Spec 6.4, 2.3)*
- **T-MOD-13e**: `output({ goto: 42 })`. Output accepted, but parsed as `{}` (goto must be string). Loop resets. *(Spec 6.4, 2.3)*
- **T-MOD-13f**: `output({ result: null })`. Coerced to `"null"`. *(Spec 6.4, 2.3)*
- **T-MOD-13g**: `output({ goto: null })`. Parsed as `{}`. Loop resets. *(Spec 6.4, 2.3)*
- **T-MOD-13h**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate goto targets. Script calls `output({ goto: "a:b:c" })`. The script exits 0 (`output()` serializes the value without validation). Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: "a:b:c"`, then the generator throws an error at transition time (malformed goto target — multiple colons). This mirrors the CLI-helper non-validation behavior tested in T-SUB-02d. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13i**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate leading-colon goto targets. Script calls `output({ goto: ":script" })`. The script exits 0. Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: ":script"`, then the generator throws at transition time (leading colon). This mirrors the CLI-helper non-validation behavior tested in T-SUB-02e. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13j**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate trailing-colon goto targets. Script calls `output({ goto: "workflow:" })`. The script exits 0. Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: "workflow:"`, then the generator throws at transition time (trailing colon). This mirrors the CLI-helper non-validation behavior tested in T-SUB-02f. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13k**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate empty-string goto targets. Script calls `output({ goto: "" })`. The script exits 0. Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: ""`, then the generator throws at transition time (empty string). This mirrors the CLI-helper non-validation behavior tested in T-SUB-02c. An implementation that incorrectly rejects falsy `""` at serialization time would fail here. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13l**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate bare-colon goto targets. Script calls `output({ goto: ":" })`. The script exits 0. Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: ":"`, then the generator throws at transition time (bare colon). This mirrors the CLI-helper non-validation behavior tested in T-SUB-02g. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13m**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate goto target existence. Script calls `output({ goto: "missing-workflow:missing-script" })`. The script exits 0. Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: "missing-workflow:missing-script"`, then the generator throws at transition time (nonexistent workflow). The existing non-validation tests (T-MOD-13h–13l) cover syntactically invalid targets; this test covers a syntactically valid but nonexistent target, confirming the helper only serializes and existence validation is deferred to loop execution time. This mirrors CLI-helper T-SUB-02h. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13n**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate name-pattern violations in bare goto targets. Script calls `output({ goto: "bad.name" })`. The script exits 0 (`output()` serializes without validation). Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: "bad.name"`, then the generator throws at transition time (invalid bare target — the dot violates the name restriction `[a-zA-Z0-9_][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*`). T-MOD-13h–13l cover invalid colon shapes and T-MOD-13m covers a syntactically valid but nonexistent target; this test covers name-pattern violations, which are a distinct validation category. A `output()` that incorrectly regex-validates names at serialization time would fail here. This mirrors CLI-helper T-SUB-02i. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13o**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate name-pattern violations in the workflow portion of a qualified goto target. Script calls `output({ goto: "bad.name:index" })`. The script exits 0. Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: "bad.name:index"`, then the generator throws at transition time (workflow-portion name violates the name restriction pattern). This is the qualified-target counterpart to T-MOD-13n and mirrors CLI-helper T-SUB-02j. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-13p**: JS/TS `output()` does not validate name-pattern violations in the script portion of a qualified goto target. Script calls `output({ goto: "ralph:bad.name" })`. The script exits 0. Observe via `run("test")`: the first yielded Output has `goto: "ralph:bad.name"`, then the generator throws at transition time (script-portion name violates the name restriction pattern). Combined with T-MOD-13o, this proves that name-pattern validation is deferred for both portions of qualified targets. This mirrors CLI-helper T-SUB-02k. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-14**: Code after `output()` does not execute. *(Spec 6.4)*
- **T-MOD-14a**: Large-payload flush: `output({ result: "x".repeat(1_000_000) })`. Full 1 MB string preserved. *(Spec 6.4)*

#### `input()` Function

- **T-MOD-15**: `input()` returns empty string on first iteration. *(Spec 6.5)*
- **T-MOD-16**: `ralph:index` → `output({ result: "payload", goto: "reader" })` → `ralph:reader` calls `input()` → receives `"payload"`. *(Spec 6.5)*
- **T-MOD-17**: `input()` called twice returns the same value (cached). *(Spec 6.5)*
- **T-MOD-18**: `input()` returns a Promise. *(Spec 6.5)*

#### ESM-Only Package Contract

- **T-MOD-22**: `[Node]` `require("loopx")` from a CJS consumer fails with ERR_REQUIRE_ESM. *(Spec 1)*

#### `LOOPX_BIN` in Bash Scripts

**These tests use `withDelegationSetup` (or the real executable path), not `runCLI`.**

- **T-MOD-19**: Bash script uses `$LOOPX_BIN output --result "payload" --goto "reader"`. Assert the reader script receives `"payload"` via stdin. *(Spec 3.4)*
- **T-MOD-20**: Bash script writes `$LOOPX_BIN` to a marker file. Assert it contains a valid executable path. *(Spec 3.4)*
- **T-MOD-21**: Bash script runs `$LOOPX_BIN version` and captures stdout. Assert it matches the package version. *(Spec 3.4)*
- **T-MOD-21a**: End-to-end bash cross-workflow goto via `$LOOPX_BIN output`. Create two workflows: `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` (runs `$LOOPX_BIN output --goto "beta:index"`) and `.loopx/beta/index.sh` (writes `"arrived"` to a marker file via `printf '%s' "arrived" > <markerPath>`, then runs `$LOOPX_BIN output --result "arrived" --stop`). Run `loopx run alpha` via CLI. Assert: (a) exit code 0 (stop: true halted the loop cleanly), and (b) the marker file exists and contains `"arrived"` (proving `beta:index` executed after the cross-workflow goto). The CLI never prints structured Output to its own stdout (Spec 7.1), so assertions use marker files and exit code, not stdout parsing. This is a composition test spanning sections 3.4 (LOOPX_BIN), 4.3 (loopx output subcommand), and 2.2 (cross-workflow goto). *(Spec 3.4, 4.3, 2.2)*

### 4.9 Programmatic API

**Spec refs:** 9.1–9.5

**Runtime-matrix methodology:** All programmatic API tests that run under both Node.js and Bun use `runAPIDriver()` to spawn a driver process under the target runtime.

#### `run()` (AsyncGenerator)

- **T-API-01**: `run("ralph")` returns an async generator. Calling `next()` yields an `Output` object. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-02**: Generator yields one `Output` per iteration. With `maxIterations: 3`, collect all yields → array of 3 outputs. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-03**: Generator completes when `stop: true` is output. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-04**: Generator completes when `maxIterations` is reached. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-05**: The output from the final iteration is yielded before the generator completes. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-06**: Breaking out of `for await` loop after the first yield prevents further iterations. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-07**: `run("ralph", { cwd: "/path/to/project" })` resolves workflows relative to the given cwd. `RunOptions.cwd` sets **both** the project root (`LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` and the directory from which `.loopx/` is resolved) **and** the script execution cwd — per Spec 9.5 and 6.1, cwd and project root are unified. The test must assert both: (a) `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` (via `observe-env`) equals the provided `cwd` value, and (b) the script's own `process.cwd()` (via `observe-cwd-ts`) reports the same directory identity (device/inode match; exact string spelling is runtime-canonicalized per Spec 6.1 "Directory identity vs. string spelling"). *(Spec 9.5, 6.1)*
- **T-API-07a**: `RunOptions.cwd` controls script execution cwd (project-root-unified). Create a workflow in project A. Call `run("ralph", { cwd: projectA })`. Script observes its cwd via `observe-cwd-ts` (`process.cwd()`) and its `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` via `observe-env`. Assert: (a) the cwd marker matches `projectA` (not `.loopx/ralph/`) — script execution cwd equals the project root; (b) the `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` marker equals the absolute path of `projectA`'s `.loopx/ralph/` directory — the workflow-relative path is exposed via `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`, not cwd. This pins down Spec 9.5's clarification that `cwd` specifies both the project root **and** the script execution cwd, and that the previous "`cwd` does not control script execution cwd" disclaimer no longer applies. *(Spec 9.5, 6.1)*
- **T-API-07b**: Relative `RunOptions.cwd` is resolved via `path.resolve(process.cwd(), options.cwd)` once at call time — no `realpath` / canonicalization. Per SPEC 3.2 / 9.5, a relative `cwd` is resolved lexically via `path.resolve` only, and `path.resolve` preserves symlink-spelling verbatim. Set up a real project at `/tmp/test-relative-cwd-project/`, with `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` present. From a driver running with `process.cwd() = /tmp/test-relative-cwd-project`, call `runPromise("ralph", { cwd: "./sub/../project", maxIterations: 1 })` (a relative path with a traversal component). The lexical resolution of this should equal `path.resolve("/tmp/test-relative-cwd-project", "./sub/../project")`, which is `/tmp/test-relative-cwd-project/project`. Seed that resolved path with its own `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Script observes `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` via `observe-env`. Assert: (a) the marker equals exactly `/tmp/test-relative-cwd-project/project` (the lexically resolved absolute path), and (b) the marker does not contain any `..` components — resolution happened lexically and was captured at call time. A buggy implementation that canonicalized via `realpath` would still produce the same string here (no symlinks involved) but would fail tests that combine a symlink component (covered by T-SYM-03/T-SYM-04). This test is the relative-path counterpart to T-SYM-03/T-SYM-04 and pins down the "resolved once at call time" rule for the relative-path case specifically. *(Spec 9.5, 3.2, 6.1)*
- **T-API-08**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` → generator completes immediately with no yields. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-08a**: `run("nonexistent", { maxIterations: 0 })` → generator throws on first `next()` (validation runs before zero-iteration short-circuit). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 7.1)*
- **T-API-08b**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` skips workflow-level version checking, mirroring CLI `-n 0`. Set up `.loopx/ralph/` with `package.json` declaring a loopx version range not satisfied by the running version. Assert: (a) resolves with `[]`, and (b) no version mismatch warning on stderr. *(Spec 9.5, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08c**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `ralph` exists but has no `index` script → generator throws on first `next()`. Target resolution validates the default entry point even with `maxIterations: 0`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08d**: `run("ralph:missing", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `ralph` exists but script `missing` does not → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08e**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0, envFile: "missing.env" })` → generator throws on first `next()`. Env file validation fires even with `maxIterations: 0`, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-22a). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 4.2)*
- **T-API-08f**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0, envFile: "missing.env" })` → rejects. Env file validation fires even with `maxIterations: 0`, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 4.2)*
- **T-API-08g**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` skips the entire version-check path, including `package.json` reading. Set up `.loopx/ralph/package.json` with an invalid semver range for `loopx` (e.g., `"loopx": "not-a-range"` in `dependencies`). Assert: generator completes with no yields, and no `package.json` or version-related warnings on stderr. This extends T-API-08b (which tests unsatisfied range via `runPromise`) to prove the entire runtime version-check path is skipped under `maxIterations: 0` — not just the range comparison. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08h**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` with `.loopx/` containing a sibling workflow with a same-base-name collision (e.g., `.loopx/broken/check.sh` and `.loopx/broken/check.ts`) → generator throws on first `next()`. Global discovery validation catches the collision before the zero-iteration short-circuit, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-22b). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 5.2)*
- **T-API-08i**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` with `.loopx/` containing a sibling workflow with an invalid script name (e.g., `.loopx/broken/-bad.sh`) → generator throws on first `next()`. Global discovery validation catches the invalid name before the zero-iteration short-circuit, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-22d). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 5.3)*
- **T-API-08j**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` with `.loopx/` containing a sibling workflow with an invalid workflow name (e.g., `.loopx/-bad-workflow/index.sh`) → generator throws on first `next()`. Global discovery validation catches the invalid workflow name before the zero-iteration short-circuit, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-22e). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 5.3)*
- **T-API-08k**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0, envFile: "malformed.env" })` where `malformed.env` exists and is readable but contains an invalid line (e.g., `1BAD=val`) → generator completes with no yields, stderr contains a parser warning for the invalid key. Env files are parsed under `maxIterations: 0`, not just existence-checked, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-22c). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 8.1)*
- **T-API-08l**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` with an unreadable global env file → generator throws on first `next()`. Global env loading and validation fires before the zero-iteration short-circuit, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-ENV-25b). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 8.1)*
- **T-API-08m**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` with a malformed-but-readable global env file (e.g., containing `1BAD=val`) → generator completes with no yields, stderr contains a parser warning for the invalid key. Global env files are parsed under `maxIterations: 0` in the programmatic API, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-ENV-25c). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 8.1)*
- **T-API-08n**: `runPromise("a:b:c", { maxIterations: 0 })` → rejects. Malformed target strings (multiple colons) are validated before the `maxIterations: 0` short-circuit, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-119d). This extends the `maxIterations: 0` validation coverage (T-API-08a/08c/08d test missing workflow/index/script) to cover target-syntax validation. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08n1**: `run("a:b:c", { maxIterations: 0 })` returns a generator (lazy); on the first `next()`, the generator throws an invalid-target error. Malformed target strings (multiple colons) are validated before the `maxIterations: 0` short-circuit on the generator surface, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-119d) and the `runPromise` surface (T-API-08n). This is the `run()` generator counterpart to T-API-08n, completing target-syntax validation parity under `maxIterations: 0` across all three surfaces (CLI, `run()`, `runPromise()`). ADR-0003 changed target syntax and zero-iteration semantics enough that the ordering rule — validate target syntax before zero-iteration skip — must be pinned down on the generator API independently of the promise API. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08o**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` unreadable (e.g., mode 000) → generator completes with no yields and no `package.json` warning on stderr. This extends T-API-08b (unsatisfied range via `runPromise`) and T-API-08g (invalid semver via `run()`) to the unreadable-file failure path — completing coverage of all three distinct `package.json` failure branches in SPEC 3.2 under `maxIterations: 0`. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119e). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08p**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0, envFile: "unreadable.env" })` where `unreadable.env` exists but is unreadable (e.g., mode 000) → generator throws on first `next()`. Env file readability validation fires even with `maxIterations: 0`, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-22f). This completes the local `envFile` failure coverage under `maxIterations: 0`: T-API-08e covers missing, T-API-08k covers malformed, and this test covers unreadable. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 4.2, 8.2)*
- **T-API-08p2**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0, envFile: "unreadable.env" })` where `unreadable.env` exists but is unreadable (e.g., mode 000) → rejects. This is the `runPromise` twin of T-API-08p, providing generator/promise symmetry for the unreadable local env file case under `maxIterations: 0`. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 4.2, 8.2)*
- **T-API-08q**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`) → generator completes with no yields and no `package.json` warning on stderr. This extends the `maxIterations: 0` version-check skip coverage to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure branch, mirroring CLI `-n 0` behavior (T-CLI-119c). Together with T-API-08b (unsatisfied range), T-API-08g (invalid semver), and T-API-08o (unreadable), this completes coverage of all four distinct workflow `package.json` failure modes under `maxIterations: 0`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08r**: `run("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists and `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not → generator completes with no yields. A workflow without an `index` script is still valid when targeting an explicit script — `maxIterations: 0` validates that the explicit target exists and passes validation. This is the positive counterpart to T-API-08c (bare target without index → throws). Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119g). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08s**: Normal-execution version mismatch warning via `run()`. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` (outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declaring a loopx version range NOT satisfied by the running version (e.g., `"loopx": ">=999.0.0"` in `dependencies`). Call `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) generator yields one output with `result: "ok"` (execution succeeds despite mismatch), and (b) stderr contains a version mismatch warning for `ralph`.
