This is the normal-execution counterpart to T-API-08b (which verifies the warning is *skipped* under `maxIterations: 0`); CLI coverage exists (T-VER-02), but the programmatic API is a separate surface where ADR-0003's runtime version-warning behavior must also hold. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08t**: Cross-workflow first-entry version warning via `run()`. Set up two workflows: `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` (no `package.json`, outputs `{"goto":"beta:index"}`) and `.loopx/beta/index.sh` (with `package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range, outputs `{"stop":true}`). Call `run("alpha")` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) two outputs are yielded (alpha's goto, then beta's stop), (b) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `beta` (emitted on first entry via goto), and (c) no version warning for `alpha`. This is the API counterpart to T-VER-04 (CLI). *(Spec 9.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08t2**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning via `run()` — invalid JSON variant. Set up `.loopx/clean/index.sh` (no `package.json` or a valid one with no loopx declaration, outputs `{"goto":"broken:index"}`) and `.loopx/broken/index.sh` (outputs `{"stop":true}`) with `.loopx/broken/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Call `run("clean")` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) two outputs are yielded (clean's goto, then broken's stop), (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-JSON warning for `broken` (emitted on first entry via goto), (c) no warning is emitted for `clean`, and (d) execution continues normally. This is the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-07d. T-API-08u covers invalid JSON on normal (single-workflow, bare-target) execution; this test pins down the cross-workflow first-entry path on the programmatic API surface. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 2.2)*
- **T-API-08t3**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning via `run()` — unreadable variant. Same structure as T-API-08t2, but `.loopx/broken/package.json` is set to mode 000 (unreadable) instead of containing invalid JSON. Assert: (a) two outputs are yielded, (b) stderr contains exactly one unreadable-file warning for `broken` (emitted on first entry via goto), (c) no warning for `clean`, and (d) execution continues normally. Unreadable-file counterpart to T-API-08t2; API counterpart to CLI T-VER-07e. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 2.2)*
- **T-API-08t4**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning via `run()` — invalid semver range variant. Same structure as T-API-08t2, but `.loopx/broken/package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }` (valid JSON but invalid semver range) instead of invalid JSON. Assert: (a) two outputs are yielded, (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-semver warning for `broken` (emitted on first entry via goto), (c) no warning for `clean`, and (d) execution continues normally. Invalid-semver counterpart to T-API-08t2 (invalid JSON) and T-API-08t3 (unreadable); API counterpart to CLI T-VER-07f. Together with T-API-08t2 and T-API-08t3, this completes API parity for all three cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure branches on the `run()` surface. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 2.2)*
- **T-API-08t5**: Cross-workflow first-entry version warning via `run()` for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Set up `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` (no `package.json`, outputs `{"goto":"beta:check"}`) and `.loopx/beta/check.sh` (no `index` script, outputs `{"stop":true}`) with `.loopx/beta/package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range. Call `run("alpha")` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) two outputs are yielded (alpha's goto, then beta's stop), (b) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `beta` (emitted on first entry via qualified goto), and (c) no version warning for `alpha`. This is the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-27. T-API-08t covers cross-workflow version mismatch into `beta:index` (index present); T-API-08z covers normal-execution version mismatch on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow; this test is the combination — cross-workflow goto into a no-index workflow via qualified `workflow:script` target with version mismatch. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-08t6**: Cross-workflow first-entry invalid-JSON `package.json` warning via `run()` for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Set up `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` (no `package.json`, outputs `{"goto":"beta:check"}`) and `.loopx/beta/check.sh` (no `index` script, outputs `{"stop":true}`) with `.loopx/beta/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Call `run("alpha")` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) two outputs are yielded (alpha's goto, then beta's stop), (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-JSON warning for `beta` (emitted on first entry via qualified goto), (c) no warning is emitted for `alpha`, and (d) execution continues normally. T-API-08t2 covers cross-workflow goto into `broken:index` (index present) with invalid JSON; T-API-08t5 covers cross-workflow goto into a no-index workflow with version mismatch; this test is the combination — cross-workflow goto into a no-index workflow (entered via explicit `workflow:script` qualified goto) with invalid-JSON `package.json`. API counterpart to CLI T-VER-27a. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-08t7**: Cross-workflow first-entry unreadable `package.json` warning via `run()` for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Same structure as T-API-08t6, but `.loopx/beta/package.json` is set to mode 000 (unreadable) instead of containing invalid JSON. Assert: (a) two outputs are yielded, (b) stderr contains exactly one unreadable-file warning for `beta` (emitted on first entry via qualified goto), (c) no warning for `alpha`, and (d) execution continues normally. Unreadable-file counterpart to T-API-08t6 (invalid JSON); T-API-08t3 covers the same `package.json` failure mode on cross-workflow goto into a workflow *with* an `index` script. API counterpart to CLI T-VER-27b. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-08t8**: Cross-workflow first-entry invalid-semver-range `package.json` warning via `run()` for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Same structure as T-API-08t6, but `.loopx/beta/package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }` (valid JSON but invalid semver range) instead of invalid JSON. Assert: (a) two outputs are yielded, (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-semver warning for `beta` (emitted on first entry via qualified goto), (c) no warning for `alpha`, and (d) execution continues normally. Invalid-semver counterpart to T-API-08t6 (invalid JSON) and T-API-08t7 (unreadable); T-API-08t4 covers the same failure mode on cross-workflow goto into a workflow *with* an `index` script. API counterpart to CLI T-VER-27c. Together with T-API-08t5 (unsatisfied range) and T-API-08t6/08t7 (invalid JSON/unreadable), this completes `run()` cross-workflow first-entry parity across all four `package.json` warning branches for qualified goto entry into no-index workflows. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-08u**: Broken workflow `package.json` warning on normal `run()` execution. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` (outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Call `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) generator yields one output with `result: "ok"` (execution succeeds despite broken `package.json`), and (b) stderr contains a `package.json` parse-failure warning. This is the normal-execution counterpart to T-API-08q (which verifies the warning is *suppressed* under `maxIterations: 0`). CLI coverage exists (T-VER-08), but the API surface requires independent verification. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08u2**: Starting-workflow unreadable `package.json` warning on normal `run()` execution. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` (outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` set to mode 000 (unreadable). Call `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) generator yields one output with `result: "ok"` (execution succeeds despite the unreadable `package.json`), and (b) stderr contains an unreadable-file warning for `ralph`. This is the unreadable-file counterpart to T-API-08u (invalid JSON) on the normal-execution path. CLI coverage exists (T-VER-07), but ADR-0003's starting-workflow `package.json` failure-warning branches must be pinned down independently on the programmatic API surface — T-API-08s covers unsatisfied range and T-API-08u covers invalid JSON, but the unreadable branch is not currently covered for `run()`. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08u3**: Starting-workflow invalid-semver-range `package.json` warning on normal `run()` execution. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` (outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }` (valid JSON, invalid semver range). Call `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) generator yields one output with `result: "ok"` (execution succeeds despite the invalid range), and (b) stderr contains an invalid-semver warning for `ralph`. This is the invalid-semver counterpart to T-API-08u (invalid JSON) and T-API-08u2 (unreadable) on the normal-execution path. CLI coverage exists (T-VER-09), but the API surface requires independent verification. Together with T-API-08s (unsatisfied range), T-API-08u (invalid JSON), and T-API-08u2 (unreadable), this completes `run()` normal-execution parity across all four starting-workflow `package.json` warning branches from SPEC 3.2. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08v**: `run("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists, `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not, and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declares an unsatisfied loopx range (e.g., `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }`) → generator completes with no yields and no version mismatch or `package.json` warnings on stderr. Combines T-API-08r (explicit `workflow:script` target under `maxIterations: 0` in a no-index workflow) with T-API-08b (`maxIterations: 0` skips workflow version checking) — proves that the version-check skip applies to explicit `workflow:script` targets in the programmatic API, not just bare workflow targets. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119h). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08w**: `run("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists, `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not, and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`) → generator completes with no yields and no `package.json` warning on stderr. Extends T-API-08v (explicit target under `maxIterations: 0` with unsatisfied range) to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure path — proving the `maxIterations: 0` version-check skip on the explicit-target path in the programmatic API covers all `package.json` failure branches, not just unsatisfied ranges. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119i). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08x**: `run("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists, `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not, and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains a valid JSON object with an invalid semver range for `loopx` (e.g., `"loopx": "not-a-range"` in `dependencies`) → generator completes with no yields and no `package.json` or version-related warning on stderr. Invalid-semver counterpart to T-API-08w (invalid JSON). Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119j). *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08y**: `run("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists, `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not, and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` is unreadable (e.g., mode 000) → generator completes with no yields and no `package.json` warning on stderr. Unreadable-file counterpart to T-API-08w and T-API-08x. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119k). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.1, 9.5, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-08z**: Normal-execution version mismatch warning on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow via `run()`. Set up `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (no `index` script, outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declaring a loopx version range NOT satisfied by the running version (e.g., `"loopx": ">=999.0.0"` in `dependencies`). Call `run("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 1 })` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) generator yields one output with `result: "ok"` (execution succeeds despite the mismatch), and (b) stderr contains a version mismatch warning for `ralph`. This is the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-26. T-API-08s covers the bare-target normal-execution warning path; T-API-36a covers explicit `workflow:script` targeting of a no-index workflow (no version declaration); this test is the symmetric combination that pins down the ADR-0003 behavior that runtime version checking still fires when a workflow is entered via an explicit script target in a workflow without a default entry point. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-08z2**: Normal-execution invalid-JSON `package.json` warning on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow via `run()`. Set up `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (no `index` script, outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Call `run("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 1 })` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) generator yields one output with `result: "ok"` (execution succeeds despite the broken `package.json`), and (b) stderr contains an invalid-JSON warning for `ralph`. Invalid-JSON counterpart to T-API-08z (unsatisfied range) on the explicit-target-into-no-index-workflow path and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-26a. T-API-08w covers the same `package.json` failure mode under `maxIterations: 0` (version-check skipped); this test pins down that the normal-execution warning still fires when entering via an explicit `workflow:script` target in a workflow without a default entry point. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-08z3**: Normal-execution invalid-semver-range `package.json` warning on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow via `run()`. Same setup as T-API-08z2, but `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }` (valid JSON, invalid semver range). Assert: (a) generator yields one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains an invalid-semver warning for `ralph`. Invalid-semver counterpart to T-API-08z2 (invalid JSON); API counterpart to CLI T-VER-26b. T-API-08x covers the same failure mode under `maxIterations: 0`. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-08z4**: Normal-execution unreadable `package.json` warning on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow via `run()`. Same setup as T-API-08z2, but `.loopx/ralph/package.json` is set to mode 000 (unreadable). Assert: (a) generator yields one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains an unreadable-file warning for `ralph`. Unreadable-file counterpart to T-API-08z2 (invalid JSON) and T-API-08z3 (invalid semver); API counterpart to CLI T-VER-26c. T-API-08y covers the same failure mode under `maxIterations: 0`. Together with T-API-08z (unsatisfied range), T-API-08z2 (invalid JSON), and T-API-08z3 (invalid semver), this completes `run()` normal-execution parity across all four `package.json` warning branches for explicit `workflow:script` entry into no-index workflows. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-08aa**: First-entry-only version-warning deduplication on re-entry via `run()`. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` that outputs `{"result":"ok"}` (no `goto`, no `stop` — the loop resets to the starting target after each iteration) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range (e.g., `"loopx": ">=999.0.0"` in `dependencies`). Call `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 3 })` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) the generator yields exactly three outputs, and (b) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `ralph` — not one per iteration. CLI coverage exists (T-VER-03), but the programmatic API is a separate surface where ADR-0003's "first entry only" deduplication rule must also hold; this test pins down on the API surface that re-entering the same workflow via loop reset does not repeat the warning. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-08ab**: Cross-workflow alternating re-entry version-warning deduplication via `run()`. Create two workflows: `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` and `.loopx/beta/index.sh`, both with `package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range. Set up a multi-iteration loop where execution alternates: `alpha:index` → goto `"beta:index"` → (no goto, reset) → `alpha:index` → goto `"beta:index"` → stop. Call `run("alpha")` and iterate to completion. Assert: (a) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `alpha` and exactly one for `beta`, and (b) no duplicate warnings appear despite both workflows being entered twice. This is the API counterpart to T-VER-04a (CLI alternating dedupe). T-API-08aa covers same-workflow re-entry on the API surface; this extends the "first entry only" deduplication rule to the full A→B→A→B alternation pattern on `run()`. *(Spec 9.1, 3.2, 2.2)*

#### `run()` with Invalid `target`

`target` is a required parameter. In TypeScript, omitting it is a static type error. In JavaScript, or when the type check is bypassed, runtime-invalid `target` values are rejected lazily.

- **T-API-09**: `run(undefined as any)` returns a generator without throwing. On the first `next()`, the generator throws (invalid target). *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-20h**: `run(null as any)` returns a generator without throwing. On first `next()`, throws. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-20i**: `run(42 as any)` returns a generator without throwing. On first `next()`, throws. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-30**: `run("")` (empty string target) returns a generator. Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. On first `next()`, throws (invalid target). Assert the error message references the invalid target format, not a missing-workflow error. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-31**: `run(":")` (bare colon target) returns a generator. Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. On first `next()`, throws. Assert the error references the invalid target format. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-32**: `run(":script")` (leading colon). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. On first `next()`, throws. Assert the error references the invalid target format. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-33**: `run("workflow:")` (trailing colon). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. On first `next()`, throws. Assert the error references the invalid target format. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-34**: `run("a:b:c")` (multiple colons). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. On first `next()`, throws. Assert the error references the invalid target format. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-35a**: `run("-bad:index")` (workflow name violates name restrictions). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. On first `next()`, throws. Assert the error references the name restriction violation. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-35b**: `run("ralph:-bad")` (script name violates name restrictions). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. On first `next()`, throws. Assert the error references the name restriction violation. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-35d**: `run("bad.name")` (bare target where the workflow name violates name restrictions). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. On first `next()`, throws. Assert the error references the name restriction violation. This is the bare-name counterpart to T-API-35a (qualified target with invalid workflow name). *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-35c**: Invalid target format is rejected after discovery and global validation in the programmatic API, mirroring CLI T-CLI-114a. Create `.loopx/broken/check.sh` and `.loopx/broken/check.ts` (name collision) alongside `.loopx/valid/index.sh`. Call `run(":script")` — generator is returned (lazy). On first `next()`, the generator throws. Assert that the error mentions the name collision in `broken` — proving discovery and global validation ran before the invalid target format was rejected. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1, 5.4)*
- **T-API-35f**: Invalid target with a name-restriction violation is rejected after discovery and global validation in `run()`, mirroring CLI T-CLI-118b. Create `.loopx/broken/check.sh` and `.loopx/broken/check.ts` (name collision) alongside `.loopx/valid/index.sh`. Call `run("bad.name")` (bare target whose workflow-name portion contains `.`, violating the name restriction pattern `[a-zA-Z0-9_][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*`) — generator is returned (lazy). On first `next()`, the generator throws. Assert that the error mentions the name collision in `broken` — proving discovery and global validation ran before the invalid bare target name was rejected. T-API-35c covers the ordering proof for malformed colon-shape targets (`":script"`) in `run()`; this test covers the same ordering proof for the name-restriction invalid-target category, a distinct validation path under ADR-0003's expanded target validation rules. Per Spec 4.1/9.1, invalid targets are rejected "at the same point as a missing workflow (after discovery, or lazily on first iteration for the API)." *(Spec 9.1, 4.1, 5.4)*

#### `run()` Target Semantics

- **T-API-35**: `run("ralph")` runs `ralph:index`. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-36**: `run("ralph:check-ready")` runs the `check-ready` script in the `ralph` workflow. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-36a**: `run("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 1 })` where `.loopx/ralph/` exists with `check.sh` but no `index` script → generator yields the output from `check.sh`. This proves the programmatic API can target explicit scripts in workflows without an `index` entry point, complementing CLI coverage (T-CLI-110, T-DISC-19). *(Spec 9.1, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-37**: `run("ralph:index")` is equivalent to `run("ralph")`. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-35e**: `run("check-ready")` where `.loopx/ralph/check-ready.sh` exists but no `.loopx/check-ready/` workflow. On first `next()`, throws (no matching workflow). Assert that `ralph:check-ready` was NOT executed (no marker file written). A bare `run()` target is always a workflow name — it must not resolve to a script inside another workflow. This is the API counterpart to T-CLI-111a. *(Spec 9.1, 2.2, 4.1)*

#### `run()` Snapshot & Cancellation

- **T-API-09b**: `run()` cwd snapshot timing. Create two project directories: `projectA` (with `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` that writes a marker file) and `projectB` (with no `.loopx/`). Call `process.chdir(projectA)`, then `const gen = run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` (no explicit `cwd`, so it captures `process.cwd()`). Call `process.chdir(projectB)` before iterating. Call `gen.next()`. Assert: the generator yields successfully using `projectA`'s workflow (marker file written), not `projectB` — proving `process.cwd()` was captured at `run()` call time, not at first iteration. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-09a**: Manual iterator cancellation during a pending `next()`. Assert child process terminated and generator completes. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-09c**: `run()` options snapshot — mutating `maxIterations` after call has no effect. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` that outputs `{"result": "ok"}` (no stop/goto). `const opts = { maxIterations: 2 }; const gen = run("ralph", opts); opts.maxIterations = 1;` Iterate `gen` to completion. Assert exactly 2 outputs are yielded, not 1 — proving the options object was snapshotted at call time. *(Spec 9.1)*

#### `run()` with AbortSignal

- **T-API-10**: `run("ralph", { signal })` — aborting terminates the loop, generator throws abort error. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-10a**: Aborting while child process is active terminates the child process group. *(Spec 9.5, 9.1)*
- **T-API-10b**: Pre-aborted signal → generator throws on first `next()`, no child spawned. *(Spec 9.5, 9.1)*
- **T-API-10c**: Signal aborted between iterations → next `next()` throws abort error. *(Spec 9.5, 9.1)*

#### `runPromise()`

- **T-API-11**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 3 })` resolves with array of 3 `Output` objects. *(Spec 9.2)*
- **T-API-12**: `runPromise("ralph")` resolves when `stop: true`. *(Spec 9.2)*
- **T-API-13**: `runPromise("ralph")` rejects when script exits non-zero. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-14**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 3, envFile: "local.env", cwd: project.dir })` resolves with correct outputs. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5)*

#### `runPromise()` Target Semantics

- **T-API-47**: `runPromise("ralph:check-ready", { maxIterations: 1 })` resolves with an array containing the Output from the `check-ready` script in the `ralph` workflow. This is the `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-36 (`run()` with a qualified target). *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-48**: `runPromise("ralph:index", { maxIterations: 1 })` is equivalent to `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` — both resolve with identical Output arrays. This is the `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-37 (`run()` equivalence test). *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-48a**: `runPromise("check-ready")` where `.loopx/ralph/check-ready.sh` exists but no `.loopx/check-ready/` workflow → rejects. Assert that `ralph:check-ready` was NOT executed (no marker file written). This is the `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-35e. *(Spec 9.2, 2.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-47a**: `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 1 })` where `.loopx/ralph/` exists with `check.sh` but no `index` script → resolves with an array containing the Output from `check.sh`. This proves `runPromise()` can target explicit scripts in workflows without an `index` entry point, complementing `run()` coverage (T-API-36a). *(Spec 9.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-47b**: `runPromise("ralph", { cwd: projectA, maxIterations: 1 })` — `RunOptions.cwd` sets both `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` and the script execution cwd. Create a workflow in project A. Script writes `process.cwd()` (via `observe-cwd-ts`), `process.env.LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` (via `observe-env`), and `process.env.LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` (via `observe-env`) to marker files. Assert: (a) cwd has the same directory identity as `projectA` (not `.loopx/ralph/`), (b) `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT` equals the provided `projectA` string, and (c) `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR` equals `projectA/.loopx/ralph/`. This is the `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-07a and pins down Spec 9.5's unified cwd/project-root semantics on the promise surface. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 6.1)*

#### `runPromise()` with Invalid `target`

- **T-API-14a**: `runPromise(undefined as any)` returns a rejected promise (not synchronous throw). *(Spec 9.2)*
- **T-API-14a2**: `runPromise(null as any)` returns a rejected promise. *(Spec 9.2)*
- **T-API-14a3**: `runPromise(42 as any)` returns a rejected promise. *(Spec 9.2)*
- **T-API-38**: `runPromise("")` rejects (empty target). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Assert the rejection error references the invalid target format, not a missing-workflow error. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-39**: `runPromise("a:b:c")` rejects (multiple colons). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Assert the rejection error references the invalid target format. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-40**: `runPromise(":")` rejects (bare colon). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Assert the rejection error references the invalid target format. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-41**: `runPromise(":script")` rejects (leading colon). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Assert the rejection error references the invalid target format. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-42**: `runPromise("workflow:")` rejects (trailing colon). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Assert the rejection error references the invalid target format. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-43**: `runPromise("-bad:index")` rejects (workflow name violates name restrictions). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Assert the rejection error references the name restriction violation. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-44**: `runPromise("ralph:-bad")` rejects (script name violates name restrictions). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Assert the rejection error references the name restriction violation. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-44a**: `runPromise("bad.name")` rejects (bare target where the workflow name violates name restrictions). Fixture contains a valid `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Assert the rejection error references the name restriction violation. This is the bare-name counterpart to T-API-43 (qualified target with invalid workflow name). *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-44b**: Invalid target format is rejected after discovery and global validation in `runPromise()`, mirroring CLI T-CLI-114a and `run()` generator T-API-35c. Create `.loopx/broken/check.sh` and `.loopx/broken/check.ts` (name collision) alongside `.loopx/valid/index.sh`. Call `runPromise(":script")`. Assert the promise rejects with an error that mentions the name collision in `broken` — proving discovery and global validation ran before the malformed target string was rejected. Per Spec 4.1/9.2, invalid targets in `runPromise()` are rejected "at the same point as a missing workflow (after discovery)." *(Spec 9.2, 4.1, 5.4)*
- **T-API-44c**: Invalid target with a name-restriction violation is rejected after discovery and global validation in `runPromise()`, mirroring CLI T-CLI-118b and `run()` generator T-API-35f. Create `.loopx/broken/check.sh` and `.loopx/broken/check.ts` (name collision) alongside `.loopx/valid/index.sh`. Call `runPromise("bad.name")` (bare target whose workflow-name portion contains `.`, violating the name restriction pattern `[a-zA-Z0-9_][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*`). Assert the promise rejects with an error that mentions the name collision in `broken` — proving discovery and global validation ran before the invalid bare target name was rejected. T-API-44b covers the ordering proof for malformed colon-shape targets (`":script"`) in `runPromise()`; this test covers the same ordering proof for the name-restriction invalid-target category, a distinct validation path under ADR-0003's expanded target validation rules. Per Spec 4.1/9.2, invalid targets in `runPromise()` are rejected "at the same point as a missing workflow (after discovery)." *(Spec 9.2, 4.1, 5.4)*
- **T-API-45**: `runPromise("ralph")` where workflow `ralph` exists but has no `index` script → rejects (missing default entry point). *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-45a**: `runPromise("ralph:index")` where workflow `ralph` exists but has no `index` script → rejects (missing script `index` in workflow `ralph`). The workflow has other scripts (e.g., `check.sh`) but no `index.*`. The explicit `:index` target follows the ordinary missing-script rule rather than the bare default-entry-point rule. T-API-45 covers the bare `runPromise("ralph")` case (missing-default-entry path); T-API-46 covers a generic missing script (`runPromise("ralph:missing")`); this test pins down the explicit `runPromise("ralph:index")` case. This is the `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-20j2 and T-CLI-109a, ensuring the promise-based surface enforces the same explicit-`:index` missing rule as the CLI and `run()` generator surfaces. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-46**: `runPromise("ralph:missing")` where workflow `ralph` exists but script `missing` does not → rejects. *(Spec 9.2, 4.1)*

#### `runPromise()` Snapshot & Options

- **T-API-14b**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` resolves with empty array `[]`. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5)*
- **T-API-14b2**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` skips workflow-level version checking when the workflow's `package.json` contains invalid JSON. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing `{broken`. Assert: (a) resolves with `[]`, and (b) no `package.json` or version-related warning on stderr. This is the `runPromise` bare-target counterpart to T-API-08q (`run()` bare zero-iter invalid JSON), extending T-API-08b (runPromise bare zero-iter unsatisfied range) to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure branch. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119c). *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14b3**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` skips workflow-level version checking when the workflow's `package.json` is unreadable (mode 000). Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` at mode 000. Assert: (a) resolves with `[]`, and (b) no `package.json` warning on stderr. This is the `runPromise` bare-target counterpart to T-API-08o (`run()` bare zero-iter unreadable), extending T-API-08b (runPromise bare zero-iter unsatisfied range) to the unreadable-file failure branch. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119e). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14b4**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` skips workflow-level version checking when the workflow's `package.json` contains a valid JSON object with an invalid semver range for `loopx` (e.g., `"loopx": "not-a-range"` in `dependencies`). Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` accordingly. Assert: (a) resolves with `[]`, and (b) no `package.json` or version-related warning on stderr. This is the `runPromise` bare-target counterpart to T-API-08g (`run()` bare zero-iter invalid semver). Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119f). Together with T-API-08b (unsatisfied range), T-API-14b2 (invalid JSON), and T-API-14b3 (unreadable), this completes `runPromise()` bare-target `maxIterations: 0` version-check-skip parity across all four `package.json` failure modes from SPEC 3.2 — pinning down on the promise surface what `run()` already covers via T-API-08b/08g/08o/08q. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14c**: `runPromise()` cwd snapshot timing. Create two project directories: `projectA` (with `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` that writes a marker file) and `projectB` (with no `.loopx/`). Call `process.chdir(projectA)`, then `const p = runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Call `process.chdir(projectB)` before awaiting. Assert: the promise resolves successfully using `projectA`'s workflow — proving `process.cwd()` was captured at `runPromise()` call time. This is the `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-09b. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5)*
- **T-API-14d**: `runPromise()` options snapshot — mutating has no effect. Set up `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` that outputs `{"result": "ok"}` (no stop/goto). `const opts = { maxIterations: 2 }; const p = runPromise("ralph", opts); opts.maxIterations = 1;` Await `p`. Assert the resolved array has exactly 2 elements, not 1 — proving the options object was snapshotted at call time. This is the `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-09c. *(Spec 9.2, 9.1)*
- **T-API-14e**: `runPromise("nonexistent", { maxIterations: 0 })` rejects. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 7.1)*
- **T-API-14f**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `ralph` exists but has no `index` script → rejects. Target resolution validates the default entry point even with `maxIterations: 0`. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 4.1)*
- **T-API-14g**: `runPromise("ralph:missing", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `ralph` exists but script `missing` does not → rejects. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 4.1)*
- **T-API-14h**: `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists and `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not → resolves with empty array `[]`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08r. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 4.1)*
- **T-API-14i**: Normal-execution version mismatch warning via `runPromise()`. Same setup as T-API-08s: `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` outputs `{"result":"ok"}`, `package.json` declares an unsatisfied loopx range. Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains a version mismatch warning for `ralph`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08s. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14j**: Cross-workflow first-entry version warning via `runPromise()`. Same setup as T-API-08t: `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` (no `package.json`, gotos `beta:index`), `.loopx/beta/index.sh` (unsatisfied loopx range, stops). Call `runPromise("alpha")`. Assert: (a) resolves with two outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `beta`, and (c) no version warning for `alpha`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08t. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14j2**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning via `runPromise()` — invalid JSON variant. Same setup as T-API-08t2: `.loopx/clean/index.sh` (no `package.json`, gotos `broken:index`) and `.loopx/broken/index.sh` (stops) with `.loopx/broken/package.json` containing invalid JSON. Call `runPromise("clean")`. Assert: (a) resolves with two outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-JSON warning for `broken`, (c) no warning for `clean`, and (d) the promise resolves rather than rejecting (warning is non-fatal). This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08t2 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-07d. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 2.2)*
- **T-API-14j3**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning via `runPromise()` — unreadable variant. Same setup as T-API-08t3: `.loopx/broken/package.json` is mode 000. Assert: (a) resolves with two outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one unreadable-file warning for `broken`, (c) no warning for `clean`, and (d) the promise resolves (non-fatal). This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08t3 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-07e. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 2.2)*
- **T-API-14j4**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning via `runPromise()` — invalid semver range variant. Same setup as T-API-08t4: `.loopx/broken/package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }`. Assert: (a) resolves with two outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-semver warning for `broken`, (c) no warning for `clean`, and (d) the promise resolves (non-fatal). This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08t4 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-07f. Together with T-API-14j2 and T-API-14j3, this completes API parity for all three cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure branches on the `runPromise()` surface. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 2.2)*
- **T-API-14j5**: Cross-workflow first-entry version warning via `runPromise()` for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Same setup as T-API-08t5: `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` (no `package.json`, gotos `beta:check`), `.loopx/beta/check.sh` (no `index` script, stops) with `.loopx/beta/package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range. Call `runPromise("alpha")`. Assert: (a) resolves with two outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `beta`, and (c) no version warning for `alpha`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08t5 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-27, completing the no-index cross-workflow first-entry version-warning parity across the CLI, `run()`, and `runPromise()` surfaces. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-14j6**: Cross-workflow first-entry invalid-JSON `package.json` warning via `runPromise()` for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Same setup as T-API-08t6: `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` (no `package.json`, gotos `beta:check`), `.loopx/beta/check.sh` (no `index` script, stops) with `.loopx/beta/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Call `runPromise("alpha")`. Assert: (a) resolves with two outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-JSON warning for `beta`, (c) no warning for `alpha`, and (d) the promise resolves rather than rejecting (warning is non-fatal). This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08t6 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-27a. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-14j7**: Cross-workflow first-entry unreadable `package.json` warning via `runPromise()` for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Same setup as T-API-08t7: `.loopx/beta/package.json` is mode 000. Assert: (a) resolves with two outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one unreadable-file warning for `beta`, (c) no warning for `alpha`, and (d) the promise resolves (non-fatal). This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08t7 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-27b. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-14j8**: Cross-workflow first-entry invalid-semver-range `package.json` warning via `runPromise()` for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Same setup as T-API-08t8: `.loopx/beta/package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }`. Assert: (a) resolves with two outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-semver warning for `beta`, (c) no warning for `alpha`, and (d) the promise resolves (non-fatal). This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08t8 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-27c. Together with T-API-14j5 (unsatisfied range), T-API-14j6 (invalid JSON), and T-API-14j7 (unreadable), this completes `runPromise()` cross-workflow first-entry parity across all four `package.json` warning branches for qualified goto entry into no-index workflows. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-14k**: Broken workflow `package.json` warning on normal `runPromise()` execution. Same setup as T-API-08u: `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` outputs `{"result":"ok"}`, `package.json` contains invalid JSON. Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains a `package.json` parse-failure warning. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08u. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14k2**: Starting-workflow unreadable `package.json` warning on normal `runPromise()` execution. Same setup as T-API-08u2: `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` outputs `{"result":"ok"}`, `.loopx/ralph/package.json` is mode 000 (unreadable). Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains an unreadable-file warning for `ralph`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08u2, completing starting-workflow `package.json` failure-warning parity across the `run()`/`runPromise()` surfaces for the unreadable branch. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.2, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14k3**: Starting-workflow invalid-semver-range `package.json` warning on normal `runPromise()` execution. Same setup as T-API-08u3: `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` outputs `{"result":"ok"}`, `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains an invalid-semver warning for `ralph`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08u3. Together with T-API-14i (unsatisfied range), T-API-14k (invalid JSON), and T-API-14k2 (unreadable), this completes `runPromise()` normal-execution parity across all four starting-workflow `package.json` warning branches from SPEC 3.2. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14l**: `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists, `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not, and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declares an unsatisfied loopx range (e.g., `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }`) → resolves with empty array `[]` and no version mismatch or `package.json` warnings on stderr. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08v, combining T-API-14h (explicit `workflow:script` target under `maxIterations: 0` in a no-index workflow) with the zero-iteration version-check skip. Ensures the `runPromise` surface shares the same "explicit target still skips version checking under zero-iteration" behavior as the generator. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-14m**: `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists, `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not, and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`) → resolves with `[]` and no `package.json` warning on stderr. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08w, extending T-API-14l (unsatisfied range) to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure path. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119i). *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-14n**: `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists, `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not, and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains a valid JSON object with an invalid semver range for `loopx` (e.g., `"loopx": "not-a-range"` in `dependencies`) → resolves with `[]` and no `package.json` or version-related warning on stderr. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08x. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119j). *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-14o**: `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 0 })` where `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` exists, `.loopx/ralph/index.*` does not, and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` is unreadable (e.g., mode 000) → resolves with `[]` and no `package.json` warning on stderr. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08y. Mirrors CLI behavior (T-CLI-119k). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.2, 9.5, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-14p**: Normal-execution version mismatch warning on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow via `runPromise()`. Same setup as T-API-08z: `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (no `index` script, outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range. Call `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains a version mismatch warning for `ralph`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08z and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-26, completing the normal-execution version-warning parity for explicit `workflow:script` entry into no-index workflows across the CLI, `run()`, and `runPromise()` surfaces. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-14p2**: Normal-execution invalid-JSON `package.json` warning on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow via `runPromise()`. Same setup as T-API-08z2: `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (no `index` script, outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Call `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains an invalid-JSON warning for `ralph`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08z2 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-26a. T-API-14m covers the same failure mode under `maxIterations: 0`. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-14p3**: Normal-execution invalid-semver-range `package.json` warning on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow via `runPromise()`. Same setup as T-API-08z3: `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (no `index` script, outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }`. Call `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains an invalid-semver warning for `ralph`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08z3 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-26b. T-API-14n covers the same failure mode under `maxIterations: 0`. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-14p4**: Normal-execution unreadable `package.json` warning on explicit `workflow:script` entry into a no-index workflow via `runPromise()`. Same setup as T-API-08z4: `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (no `index` script, outputs `{"result":"ok"}`) with `.loopx/ralph/package.json` at mode 000 (unreadable). Call `runPromise("ralph:check", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with one output with `result: "ok"`, and (b) stderr contains an unreadable-file warning for `ralph`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08z4 and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-26c. T-API-14o covers the same failure mode under `maxIterations: 0`. Together with T-API-14p (unsatisfied range), T-API-14p2 (invalid JSON), and T-API-14p3 (invalid semver), this completes `runPromise()` normal-execution parity across all four `package.json` warning branches for explicit `workflow:script` entry into no-index workflows. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-API-14q**: First-entry-only version-warning deduplication on re-entry via `runPromise()`. Same setup as T-API-08aa: `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` outputs `{"result":"ok"}` (no `goto`, no `stop` — the loop resets to the starting target after each iteration), `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declares an unsatisfied loopx range. Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 3 })`. Assert: (a) resolves with exactly three outputs, and (b) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `ralph` — not one per iteration. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08aa, ensuring ADR-0003's "first entry only" deduplication rule holds identically on the promise-based API surface. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2)*
- **T-API-14r**: Cross-workflow alternating re-entry version-warning deduplication via `runPromise()`. Same setup as T-API-08ab: two workflows `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` and `.loopx/beta/index.sh`, both with `package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range, and a multi-iteration loop that alternates `alpha:index` → goto `"beta:index"` → (no goto, reset) → `alpha:index` → goto `"beta:index"` → stop. Call `runPromise("alpha")`. Assert: (a) the promise resolves with the expected outputs, (b) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `alpha` and exactly one for `beta`, and (c) no duplicate warnings appear despite both workflows being entered twice. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-08ab and the API counterpart to T-VER-04a (CLI), ensuring the alternating cross-workflow "first entry only" deduplication rule holds identically on the promise-based surface. *(Spec 9.2, 3.2, 2.2)*

#### Error Behavior

- **T-API-15**: Programmatic API never prints `result` to stdout. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-16**: Non-zero script exit causes `run()` generator to throw. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-17**: Invalid goto target causes `run()` generator to throw. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-18**: Script stderr is forwarded to the calling process's stderr. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-19**: When `run()` throws, previously yielded outputs are preserved. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-20a**: `run("nonexistent")` → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.3)*
- **T-API-20b**: `runPromise("nonexistent")` → rejects. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-20c**: `run("ralph")` with name collision in `.loopx/` → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.3)*
- **T-API-20d**: `run("ralph", { envFile: "nonexistent.env" })` → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-20e**: `runPromise("ralph", { envFile: "nonexistent.env" })` → rejects. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-20f**: `run("ralph", { cwd: dirWithoutLoopx })` → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.3)*
- **T-API-20g**: `runPromise("ralph", { cwd: dirWithoutLoopx })` → rejects. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-20j**: `run("ralph")` where workflow `ralph` exists but has no `index` script → generator throws on first `next()` (missing default entry point). *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-20j2**: `run("ralph:index")` where workflow `ralph` exists but has no `index` script → generator throws on first `next()` (missing script `index` in workflow `ralph`). The workflow has other scripts (e.g., `check.sh`) but no `index.*`. The explicit `:index` target follows the ordinary missing-script rule rather than the bare default-entry-point rule — ADR-0003 makes `index` special only when the script portion of the target is omitted. T-API-20j covers the bare `run("ralph")` case (missing-default-entry path); T-API-20k covers a generic missing script (`run("ralph:missing")`); this test pins down the explicit `run("ralph:index")` case so a buggy implementation cannot special-case `:index` to fall back to a different resolution path. This is the API counterpart to T-CLI-109a. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-20k**: `run("ralph:missing")` where workflow `ralph` exists but script `missing` does not → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 4.1)*
- **T-API-20l**: `run("good")` in normal execution with `.loopx/` containing a sibling workflow that has an invalid script name (e.g., `.loopx/good/index.sh` valid, `.loopx/broken/-bad.sh`) → generator throws on first `next()`. Global discovery validation catches the invalid script name in the sibling before execution begins. This is the normal-execution API counterpart to CLI T-DISC-47a and extends the `maxIterations: 0` coverage (T-API-08i) to non-zero iterations — T-API-20c proves the same for sibling same-base-name collisions, but sibling name-restriction violations are a distinct validation path. *(Spec 9.1, 9.3, 5.3, 5.4)*
- **T-API-20m**: `run("good")` in normal execution with `.loopx/` containing a sibling workflow whose name is invalid (e.g., `.loopx/good/index.sh` valid, `.loopx/-bad-workflow/index.sh`) → generator throws on first `next()`. Global discovery validation catches the invalid workflow name in the sibling before execution begins. This is the normal-execution API counterpart to CLI T-DISC-47b and extends the `maxIterations: 0` coverage (T-API-08j) to non-zero iterations — the workflow-name validation path is distinct from the script-name path tested in T-API-20l. *(Spec 9.1, 9.3, 5.3, 5.4)*
- **T-API-20n**: `runPromise("good")` in normal execution with `.loopx/` containing a sibling workflow that has an invalid script name (e.g., `.loopx/good/index.sh` valid, `.loopx/broken/-bad.sh`) → rejects. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-20l, ensuring the promise-based surface enforces sibling name-restriction validation identically to the generator surface in normal execution. *(Spec 9.2, 9.3, 5.3, 5.4)*
- **T-API-20o**: `runPromise("good")` in normal execution with `.loopx/` containing a sibling workflow whose name is invalid (e.g., `.loopx/good/index.sh` valid, `.loopx/-bad-workflow/index.sh`) → rejects. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-20m. *(Spec 9.2, 9.3, 5.3, 5.4)*
- **T-API-20p**: API parity for version-check ordering when the starting target cannot be entered. Create `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (valid workflow with no `index` script) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range (e.g., `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }`). Call `run("ralph")` with `maxIterations: 1`. Assert: (a) the generator throws on first `next()` with an error about the missing default entry point, and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings for `ralph`. Target resolution fails before workflow-entry version checking runs — the workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. This is the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-24 and completes the ADR-0003 "version check ordering before workflow entry" symmetry between the CLI and programmatic API surfaces. *(Spec 9.1, 9.3, 7.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-20p2**: API parity for version-check ordering when the starting target cannot be entered — `runPromise()` surface, unsatisfied range variant. Same fixture as T-API-20p: `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (valid workflow with no `index` script) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range (e.g., `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }`). Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) the promise rejects with an error about the missing default entry point, and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings for `ralph`. Target resolution fails before workflow-entry version checking runs — the workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. This is the `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-20p (`run()` generator surface) and CLI T-VER-24, closing the "missing default entry point beats version/package checking" ordering parity across all three surfaces (CLI, `run()`, `runPromise()`). ADR-0003 made explicit `index`-only default-entry semantics first-class, so the ordering rule must be pinned down on every entry surface. *(Spec 9.2, 9.3, 7.1, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-20p3**: API parity for version-check ordering when the starting target cannot be entered — `runPromise()` surface, broken JSON variant. Same setup as T-API-20p2, but `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains `{{{INVALID` (broken JSON) instead of an unsatisfied range. Call `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) the promise rejects with an error about the missing default entry point, and (b) stderr contains no JSON parse or version mismatch warnings for `ralph`. Broken-JSON counterpart to T-API-20p2 (unsatisfied range) and the `runPromise()` counterpart to CLI T-VER-24a, completing coverage of both `package.json` failure modes on the promise surface for the missing-default-entry ordering rule. Together with T-API-20p (unsatisfied range on `run()`), this pins down on the programmatic API that target resolution precedes both version-range comparison and `package.json` reading — neither branch is entered when the starting target resolution fails. *(Spec 9.2, 9.3, 7.1, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-20q**: API parity for version-check ordering when a goto target script does not exist. Create `.loopx/start/index.sh` that outputs `{ "goto": "other:missing" }`, `.loopx/other/index.sh` (valid), and `.loopx/other/package.json` containing `{{{INVALID` (broken JSON). Call `runPromise("start", { maxIterations: 2 })`. Assert: (a) the promise rejects with an error about the missing script `missing` in workflow `other`, and (b) stderr contains no `package.json` parse warnings or version mismatch warnings for `other`. Goto target resolution fails before first-entry version checking runs — the target workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. This is the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-25a. *(Spec 9.2, 9.3, 7.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-20q2**: API parity for version-check ordering when a goto target script does not exist — unsatisfied-range variant. Create `.loopx/start/index.sh` that outputs `{ "goto": "other:missing" }`, `.loopx/other/index.sh` (valid), and `.loopx/other/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }` (an unsatisfied range). Call `runPromise("start", { maxIterations: 2 })`. Assert: (a) the promise rejects with an error about the missing script `missing` in workflow `other`, and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings for `other`. Goto target resolution fails before first-entry version checking runs — the target workflow is never entered, so its version range is never compared. T-API-20q covers the broken-JSON variant on this path and is the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-25a; this test covers the unsatisfied-range variant and is the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-25, completing goto-target-missing-script ordering parity between CLI and `runPromise()` across both `package.json` failure modes. *(Spec 9.2, 9.3, 7.1, 3.2)*
- **T-API-20r**: API parity for version-check ordering when an explicit `workflow:script` start target names a missing script — via `run()`. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` (valid workflow, `index` present) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range (e.g., `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }`). Call `run("ralph:missing", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) the generator throws on first `next()` with an error about the missing script `missing` in workflow `ralph`, and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings for `ralph`. Target resolution fails before workflow-entry version checking runs — the workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. This is the `run()` API counterpart to CLI T-VER-24b and extends T-API-20p (missing default entry) and T-API-20q (missing goto target) to the explicit `workflow:script` start-target case. ADR-0003 made explicit `workflow:script` start targets first-class, so the ordering rule must hold on the API surface too. *(Spec 9.1, 9.3, 7.1, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-API-20s**: API parity for version-check ordering when an explicit `workflow:script` start target names a missing script — via `runPromise()`, broken JSON variant. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` (valid workflow, `index` present) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing `{{{INVALID` (broken JSON). Call `runPromise("ralph:missing", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) the promise rejects with an error about the missing script `missing` in workflow `ralph`, and (b) stderr contains no JSON parse or version mismatch warnings for `ralph`. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-20r and the API counterpart to CLI T-VER-24c — covering the broken-JSON failure mode on the promise surface and completing the ADR-0003 explicit-`workflow:script`-start ordering parity between CLI, `run()`, and `runPromise()`. *(Spec 9.2, 9.3, 7.1, 3.2, 4.1)*

#### `envFile` Option

- **T-API-21**: `run("ralph", { envFile: "local.env" })` loads the env file. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-21a**: Relative envFile path resolved against provided `cwd`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-21b**: Relative envFile path resolved against `process.cwd()` when no `cwd` option. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-21c**: Env file parse warnings forwarded to stderr via programmatic API. *(Spec 8.1, 9.3)*
- **T-API-21d**: Global env file parse warnings forwarded to stderr. *(Spec 8.1, 9.3)*

#### `maxIterations` Validation

- **T-API-22**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: -1 })` → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-23**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1.5 })` → generator throws. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-23a**: `run("ralph", { maxIterations: NaN })` → generator throws. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-24**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: NaN })` → rejects. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-24a**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: -1 })` → rejects. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-24b**: `runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1.5 })` → rejects. *(Spec 9.5)*

#### `runPromise()` with AbortSignal

- **T-API-25**: `runPromise("ralph", { signal })` — aborting rejects with abort error. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-25a**: Pre-aborted signal → rejects immediately, no child spawned. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-25b**: Abort between iterations → rejects. *(Spec 9.5, 9.2)*

#### `RunOptions.env` (Programmatic Env Injection)

Spec 9.5 adds an `env?: Record<string, string>` field to `RunOptions`. These tests cover shape validation, snapshot semantics, precedence, and boundary cases. All fixtures use `observe-env` to distinguish set-vs-absent.

##### Basic Injection

- **T-API-50**: `RunOptions.env` injects a variable into every spawned script. `runPromise("ralph", { env: { MYVAR: "hello" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Script observes `MYVAR`. Assert marker shows `{ present: true, value: "hello" }`. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-50a**: `RunOptions.env` applies to every script across iterations. Two iterations; both observe `MYVAR`. Assert both markers show `"hello"`. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-50b**: `RunOptions.env` applies across intra-workflow goto. `ralph:index` gotos `ralph:check`. Both observe `MYVAR`. Assert both show `"hello"`. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-50c**: `RunOptions.env` applies across cross-workflow goto. `alpha:index` gotos `beta:step`. Both observe `MYVAR`. Assert both show `"hello"`. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-50d**: `RunOptions.env` applies on loop reset. Multi-iteration loop where reset returns to the starting target. Observe `MYVAR` on every iteration. Assert every observation shows `"hello"`. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*

##### Precedence

- **T-API-51a**: `RunOptions.env` is overridden by protocol variables. `runPromise("ralph", { env: { LOOPX_WORKFLOW: "fake", LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT: "/tmp/fake", LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR: "/tmp/fake-dir", LOOPX_TMPDIR: "/tmp/fake-tmp", LOOPX_BIN: "/tmp/fake-bin" } })`. Scripts observe each variable. Assert each marker contains the real injected value (tier-1 protocol), not the `RunOptions.env` (tier-2) value. Per Spec 9.5 "No name validation beyond string-to-string", `LOOPX_*` keys in `RunOptions.env` are silently overridden by protocol injection. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-51b**: `RunOptions.env` overrides local env-file values. Local env file `.env` contains `MYVAR=from-file`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { envFile: ".env", env: { MYVAR: "from-options" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Script observes `MYVAR`. Assert marker shows `"from-options"`. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-51c**: `RunOptions.env` overrides global env-file values. Global env file contains `MYVAR=from-global`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { env: { MYVAR: "from-options" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert marker shows `"from-options"`. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-51d**: `RunOptions.env` overrides inherited `process.env` values. Parent process has `MYVAR=inherited`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { env: { MYVAR: "from-options" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert marker shows `"from-options"`. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-51e**: Full precedence chain. Inherited `MYVAR=1`, global env file `MYVAR=2`, local env file `MYVAR=3`, `RunOptions.env.MYVAR=4`, protocol variables (unchanged — `MYVAR` is not a protocol name). Script observes `MYVAR`. Assert `"4"` — `RunOptions.env` wins over all lower tiers, and protocol doesn't apply to non-`LOOPX_*` names. *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*

##### Snapshot Semantics

- **T-API-52**: `RunOptions.env` is snapshotted at call time. `const e = { MYVAR: "initial" }; const p = runPromise("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 }); e.MYVAR = "mutated";` Await `p`. Script observes `MYVAR`. Assert marker shows `"initial"` — mutating the original object after `runPromise()` returns has no effect on the running loop. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-52a**: `RunOptions.env` snapshot is shallow. `const e = { MYVAR: "initial" }; const gen = run("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 }); e.NEWVAR = "added"; await gen.next();` Script observes both `MYVAR` and `NEWVAR`. Assert `MYVAR` present with `"initial"` and `NEWVAR` absent — the shallow snapshot captured the initial keys, and the added key is not observed. Paired with T-API-52 (value mutation) to pin down "own enumerable string-keyed properties read once". *(Spec 9.5, 9.1)*
- **T-API-52b**: `RunOptions.env` snapshot timing under `run()` is lazy (before first `next()`). Mirrors T-API-09b for `RunOptions.env`. `const e = { MYVAR: "A" }; const gen = run("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 }); e.MYVAR = "B"; await gen.next();` Script observes `MYVAR`. Per Spec 9.5 "Shape ... Lifetime. Entries are captured synchronously at call time as a shallow copy" — the snapshot is taken at `run()` call time, not at first `next()`. Assert marker shows `"A"`. This test intentionally differs from T-API-09b (which covers inherited `process.env`, captured lazily) to prove `RunOptions.env` has *eager* snapshot semantics while `process.env` has *lazy* semantics under `run()`. *(Spec 9.5, 9.1)*

##### Invalid Shape

- **T-API-53**: `RunOptions.env = null` → generator throws on first `next()` (invalid shape). `run("ralph", { env: null as any })` returns a generator; `.next()` throws with an error mentioning invalid `env`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-53a**: `RunOptions.env = []` (array) → generator throws on first `next()`. Arrays are rejected per Spec 9.5 "non-null, non-array, non-function object". *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-53b**: `RunOptions.env = () => {}` (function) → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-53c**: `RunOptions.env = "string"` → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-53d**: `RunOptions.env = 42` → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-54**: Non-string entry value → generator throws on first `next()`. `run("ralph", { env: { MYVAR: 42 as any } })` — non-string value is rejected. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-54a**: `undefined` entry value → generator throws on first `next()`. `run("ralph", { env: { MYVAR: undefined as any } })`. Per Spec 9.5, all own enumerable string-keyed entries must have string values; `undefined` is not a string. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-54b**: `null` entry value → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-54c**: Object entry value → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-55**: `runPromise` equivalents for invalid shapes — all invalid `RunOptions.env` shapes reject the promise. Parameterized across null, array, function, string, number, and non-string entry values. *(Spec 9.5, 9.2)*

##### Inherited / Symbol / Non-Enumerable Keys

- **T-API-56**: Inherited keys on the options.env object are ignored. `const proto = { INHERITED: "proto-val" }; const e = Object.create(proto); e.OWN = "own-val"; runPromise("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 })`. Script observes both. Assert `OWN` present with `"own-val"` and `INHERITED` absent — loopx reads only own enumerable string-keyed properties. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-56a**: Symbol-keyed entries are ignored. `const sym = Symbol("SYM"); const e = { OWN: "own-val", [sym]: "sym-val" }; runPromise("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 })`. Script observes `OWN` and (via TS `Object.getOwnPropertySymbols` or simply observing all `LOOPX_`-free env keys) asserts that no symbol-derived key leaked into the child env. Mainly: `OWN` is present, and the child env has no `SYM`-like stringified key. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-56b**: Non-enumerable string-keyed entries are ignored. `const e = {}; Object.defineProperty(e, "HIDDEN", { value: "hidden-val", enumerable: false }); e.VISIBLE = "visible-val"; runPromise("ralph", { env: e, maxIterations: 1 })`. Script observes both. Assert `VISIBLE` present, `HIDDEN` absent. *(Spec 9.5)*

##### Runtime-Rejected Names / Values (Embedded NUL)

- **T-API-57**: `RunOptions.env` entry with embedded NUL in the value surfaces as a spawn failure. `runPromise("ralph", { env: { MYVAR: "bad val" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Per Spec 9.5 "No name validation beyond string-to-string" — runtime-level rejections (embedded NUL) surface at child launch / spawn failure. Assert: the promise rejects with a spawn-failure error. The error is *not* a shape-validation error — shape validation passed (both key and value are strings); the rejection comes from the runtime's environment-building layer. *(Spec 9.5, 9.3)*
- **T-API-57a**: `RunOptions.env` entry with embedded NUL in the key surfaces as a spawn failure. `runPromise("ralph", { env: { "BAD KEY": "val" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert promise rejects with spawn-failure error. *(Spec 9.5, 9.3)*
- **T-API-57b**: `RunOptions.env` entry with `=` in the key surfaces per runtime behavior. Per Spec 9.5, loopx does not reject `=` at the shape level; whether the runtime rejects it is implementation-defined. Assert one of: (a) the runtime rejects and the promise rejects with a spawn failure, or (b) the runtime accepts and the variable is observable (spawn succeeded). Test passes if either outcome holds but the CLI exit code / generator outcome is never some third category. Documents the "runtime does not distinguish tiers" clause: any env tier (not just `RunOptions.env`) with the same malformed key / value has the same outcome. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-57c**: `RunOptions.env` entry with an **empty-string key** is not rejected at the shape level. Per SPEC 9.5 "No name validation beyond string-to-string ... does not reject `=` or empty-string names". Call `runPromise("ralph", { env: { "": "empty-key-value" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. The shape is valid (own enumerable string-keyed property with a string value). Outcome is implementation-defined and runtime-dependent: either (a) the runtime rejects the empty-string key at spawn and the promise rejects with a spawn-failure error (not an option-shape-validation error), or (b) the runtime accepts it and the child env has whatever the runtime does with an empty name (observably absent or present — either is conforming). Assert: the outcome is either (a) or (b) — the CLI exit code / generator outcome is never some third category, and in particular the failure surface is never "invalid `options.env` shape". T-API-57 covers NUL in value, T-API-57a covers NUL in key, T-API-57b covers `=` in key; this test closes the empty-string-key branch, completing shape-level-accepted runtime-rejected coverage. *(Spec 9.5, 9.3)*

##### `LOOPX_*` Keys in `RunOptions.env`

- **T-API-58**: `RunOptions.env` supplying a `LOOPX_*` key is silently overridden by protocol injection (no error, no warning). `runPromise("ralph", { env: { LOOPX_WORKFLOW: "user-fake", CUSTOM: "user-val" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Script observes both. Assert: `LOOPX_WORKFLOW` shows the real workflow name, `CUSTOM` shows `"user-val"`. Stderr contains no warning about `LOOPX_WORKFLOW` being overridden — loopx does not warn (Spec 9.5). *(Spec 9.5, 8.3)*
- **T-API-58a**: `RunOptions.env.LOOPX_DELEGATED` reaches spawned scripts (not a script-protocol-protected tier). Per Spec 9.5, `LOOPX_DELEGATED` is startup-reserved only, not script-protocol-protected — `RunOptions.env` may supply it to spawned scripts. Call `runPromise("ralph", { env: { LOOPX_DELEGATED: "user-supplied" } })`. Script observes `LOOPX_DELEGATED`. Assert marker shows `"user-supplied"`. This distinguishes the five script-protocol-protected names (T-API-51a/58) from the startup-only `LOOPX_DELEGATED`. *(Spec 9.5, 3.2, 8.3, 13)*

##### `RunOptions.env` Does Not Affect loopx's Own Lookups

- **T-API-59**: `RunOptions.env` does **not** redirect global env-file lookup. Set `process.env.XDG_CONFIG_HOME=/real/config/path`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { env: { XDG_CONFIG_HOME: "/fake/config/path" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Script observes `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` — assert marker shows `"/fake/config/path"` (the `RunOptions.env` value reaches the child). But also: place an env file at `/real/config/path/loopx/env` containing `MARKER=real`, and at `/fake/config/path/loopx/env` containing `MARKER=fake`. Script observes `MARKER`. Assert marker shows `"real"` — the global env file was resolved using loopx's own `process.env` (not `RunOptions.env`). Per Spec 8.1 "`RunOptions.env` does **not** affect global env-file path resolution". *(Spec 8.1, 8.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-59a**: `RunOptions.env` does **not** redirect global env-file lookup via `HOME`. Similar structure to T-API-59 but using `HOME` instead of `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` (the fallback path). Unset `XDG_CONFIG_HOME`, set `process.env.HOME=/real/home`. Call with `RunOptions.env.HOME=/fake/home`. Place env files at both `/real/home/.config/loopx/env` (`MARKER=real`) and `/fake/home/.config/loopx/env` (`MARKER=fake`). Assert script's `MARKER` observation is `"real"` (loopx read from `$HOME/.config/loopx/env` using loopx's own `HOME`, not the child's). *(Spec 8.1, 8.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-60**: `RunOptions.env` does **not** redirect tmpdir parent selection. Set `process.env.TMPDIR=/tmp/real-parent`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { env: { TMPDIR: "/tmp/fake-parent" }, maxIterations: 1 })`. Script observes both `TMPDIR` and `LOOPX_TMPDIR`. Assert: (a) child's `TMPDIR` is `"/tmp/fake-parent"` (the `RunOptions.env` value reaches the child), (b) `LOOPX_TMPDIR` lives under `/tmp/real-parent/` (loopx's own tmpdir parent was captured from loopx's own `process.env`). *(Spec 7.4, 8.3, 9.5)*

#### Advanced `options` / `options.signal` Semantics

Spec 9.1 / 9.3 / 9.5 describe option-snapshot behavior, pre-abort precedence, pinned-priority, pre-first-`next()` carve-out, and other advanced semantics. These tests close coverage.

##### `options` Shape Validation

- **T-API-61**: `run("ralph", null)` → generator throws on first `next()`. Per Spec 9.5, `options` must be omitted, `undefined`, or a non-null non-array non-function object. *(Spec 9.5, 9.1)*
- **T-API-61a**: `run("ralph", [])` (array) → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-61b**: `run("ralph", () => {})` (function) → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-61c**: `run("ralph", "string")` → generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-61d**: `runPromise("ralph", null)` → rejects. *(Spec 9.5, 9.2)*
- **T-API-61e**: `runPromise("ralph", [])` → rejects. *(Spec 9.5, 9.2)*

##### Throwing Getters

- **T-API-62**: Throwing getter on `options` object itself — generator throws on first `next()`. `const opts = {}; Object.defineProperty(opts, "env", { get() { throw new Error("boom"); } }); run("ralph", opts);` Generator is returned without throwing at call site; on first `next()`, throws. The error is surfaced as pre-iteration error, not escaping at call site. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-62a**: Throwing getter on `options.signal` — generator throws on first `next()`. Signal is read first (Spec 9.1), so a throwing `signal` getter captures as a snapshot error. Generator is still returned normally. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-62b**: Throwing getter on `options.cwd` — generator throws on first `next()`. The `cwd` getter is a pinned-priority option per Spec 9.3 "Pinned pre-iteration priority". *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-62c**: Throwing getter on `options.envFile` — generator throws on first `next()`. Pinned-priority option. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-62d**: Throwing getter on `options.maxIterations` — generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-62e**: Throwing enumerable getter inside `options.env` — generator throws on first `next()`. `const env = { A: "a" }; Object.defineProperty(env, "B", { enumerable: true, get() { throw new Error("boom"); } }); run("ralph", { env })`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-62f**: Proxy `ownKeys` trap that throws while enumerating `options.env` — generator throws on first `next()`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-62g**: Throwing getter under `runPromise` — rejects (not synchronous throw). `runPromise("ralph", new Proxy({}, { get(_, k) { if (k === "env") throw new Error("boom"); return undefined; } }))`. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5)*

##### Option-Field Single-Read Contract

SPEC 9.1 / 9.2 specify: "Each option field is read at most once per call, and a throwing getter or proxy trap is not re-invoked to retry." Existing tests cover many individual throwing-getter / proxy-trap failure cases but do not assert the **single-read** contract itself — a buggy implementation could work for non-throwing getters by reading them multiple times without any test catching the violation.

- **T-API-62h**: `run()` reads each option field at most once per call. Set up counter-based getters on every pinned `RunOptions` field: `signal`, `cwd`, `envFile`, `maxIterations`, `env`. Each getter increments its own counter and returns a valid value. Call `run("ralph", opts, ...)` where `opts` has these five counter-based getters. Iterate the generator to completion (e.g., `maxIterations: 2` with a simple workflow). After the generator settles, assert each counter is **exactly 1** — no field was read twice during the option snapshot. Per SPEC 9.1 "each option field is read at most once per call." A buggy implementation that re-reads options across iterations or retries a getter on a caught exception would fail this assertion. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-62h2**: `runPromise()` reads each option field at most once per call. Same counter-based getter fixture as T-API-62h, but via `runPromise("ralph", opts)`. Await the promise to resolution. Assert each counter is exactly 1. This is the `runPromise` counterpart to T-API-62h. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5)*

##### Generator-Returns-Without-Throwing Invariants

- **T-API-63**: `run()` returns a generator without throwing, even under every invalid-options scenario. Parameterize over {invalid-target, invalid-options-shape, throwing-option-getter, already-aborted-signal, invalid-cwd, invalid-envFile, invalid-maxIterations, invalid-env}.
