For each input, assert that `run(...)` returns a non-null object with `.next()`, `.return()`, `.throw()` methods without raising at the call site. The error is surfaced on first `next()`. This is Spec 9.1's "run() still returns a generator without throwing" invariant — critical because any call-site throw would break consumer composition patterns. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-63a**: `runPromise()` returns a promise (not a thrown error) for every invalid input. Parameterize same cases as T-API-63. Assert `runPromise(...)` returns a `Promise` instance (check with `typeof p.then === "function"`) that then rejects. Spec 9.2 — call never throws; failure surfaces as rejection. *(Spec 9.2)*

##### Signal Semantics — Duck-Typed / Reentrant

- **T-API-64**: Invalid `options.signal` shape is an option error, not an abort. `run("ralph", { signal: "not-a-signal" as any })` returns a generator; on first `next()`, throws an option-validation error (not an abort error). The error message references the invalid signal shape. Spec 9.3 — an invalid `options.signal` "remains an ordinary option-snapshot error". *(Spec 9.3, 9.5, 9.1)*
- **T-API-64a**: Duck-typed signal compatibility. A non-`AbortSignal` object that exposes `aborted: boolean` and `addEventListener("abort", fn)` is accepted as a signal. Create a duck-typed signal `{ aborted: false, addEventListener(type, fn) { if (type === "abort") this._listener = fn; }, _fire() { this.aborted = true; this._listener?.(); } }`. Call `runPromise("ralph", { signal: duck, ... })`, then `duck._fire()`. Assert the promise rejects with the abort error. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-64b**: Reentrant `addEventListener` — duck signal's `addEventListener` synchronously invokes the listener during registration. loopx treats the signal as aborted. Duck signal constructor: `addEventListener(type, fn) { fn(); }`. `runPromise("ralph", { signal: duck, maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert the promise rejects with an abort error on first observation — no child is spawned. Per Spec 9.5, "if `addEventListener` synchronously invokes the registered listener during registration ... loopx treats the signal as aborted". *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-64c**: Duck-typed signal with `aborted: true` at capture time — loopx treats as aborted, no child spawned. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-64d**: Real pre-aborted `AbortSignal`. `const c = new AbortController(); c.abort(); runPromise("ralph", { signal: c.signal, maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert the promise rejects with abort error, no child was spawned. Real `AbortSignal` instances passed already-aborted must always be observed as aborted. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-API-64e**: Signal getter is read first. `const opts = {}; let order = []; Object.defineProperty(opts, "signal", { get() { order.push("signal"); return undefined; } }); Object.defineProperty(opts, "env", { get() { order.push("env"); return undefined; } }); run("ralph", opts);` Await `.next()`. Assert `order[0] === "signal"`. Per Spec 9.1, signal is read before other fields. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-API-64f**: Duck-typed signal with a throwing `addEventListener` surfaces as an option-snapshot error, not a call-site throw. Per SPEC 9.5 the `addEventListener` method must be "callable and returns without throwing when loopx invokes it". Construct a duck signal whose `addEventListener` throws synchronously: `const duck = { aborted: false, addEventListener() { throw new Error("listener-register-failed"); } };` Call `run("ralph", { signal: duck, maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert: (a) `run()` returns a generator (not a synchronous throw at the call site), (b) on the first `next()`, the generator throws an option-snapshot error referencing the invalid signal (or wrapping the listener-register exception) — the error must be an **option-shape / signal-validation** error, not an abort error and not a runtime spawn-failure error, (c) no child is spawned, (d) no tmpdir is created. This is the throwing-`addEventListener` counterpart to T-API-64b (reentrant `addEventListener` that fires the listener — treated as aborted) and T-API-64 (non-signal shape — option error). A throwing register does not qualify as aborted (the listener did not actually fire `true` on `aborted`) and does not qualify as a usable signal (the contract is violated), so the correct surface is the option-snapshot error path. *(Spec 9.5, 9.1)*
- **T-API-64g**: `runPromise()` counterpart to T-API-64f — throwing `addEventListener` on duck signal rejects with an option-snapshot error. Same setup as T-API-64f. `runPromise("ralph", { signal: duck, maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert the promise rejects with an option-shape / signal-validation error (not an abort error, not a spawn-failure error). *(Spec 9.5, 9.2)*

##### Abort Precedence

- **T-API-65**: Abort beats missing env-file. `const c = new AbortController(); c.abort(); runPromise("ralph", { signal: c.signal, envFile: "nonexistent.env", maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert promise rejects with abort error (not env-file-missing error). Per Spec 9.3 "Abort precedence over pre-iteration failures", once a usable signal is captured and aborts before the first child spawn, it displaces all other pre-iteration failure modes. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-65a**: Abort beats invalid target. `const c = new AbortController(); c.abort(); runPromise(":bad", { signal: c.signal, maxIterations: 1 })`. Assert abort error, not invalid-target error. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-65b**: Abort beats discovery failure (missing `.loopx/`). *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-65c**: Abort beats env-file-load failure (malformed file causing parse error). *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-65d**: Abort beats tmpdir-creation failure. Simulate tmpdir-creation failure by setting `TMPDIR` to a path whose parent is read-only. Pre-abort the signal. Assert abort error, not tmpdir-creation error. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5, 7.4)*
- **T-API-65e**: Invalid `options.signal` shape does not enter the abort pathway. `run("ralph", { signal: "not-a-signal" as any, envFile: "nonexistent.env" })`. Per Spec 9.3 "An invalid `options` value or non-`AbortSignal`-compatible `options.signal` captures no signal and does not enter this pathway". Assert the first-`next()` error references the invalid signal shape (or the missing env file — implementation-defined ordering between those two), **not** an abort error. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-66**: Abort after final yield but before settlement produces abort error. Mirror T-TMP-23 / Spec 9.3 "Abort after final yield". `const gen = run("ralph", { signal: c.signal, maxIterations: 1 }); const { value } = await gen.next(); c.abort(); await gen.next();` — expect the second `next()` to throw the abort error, not to resolve `{ done: true }` silently. *(Spec 9.3)*
- **T-API-66a**: Abort after final yield but before settlement produces abort error on subsequent `.return()`. Per SPEC 9.3: "Abort after final yield ... produces the abort error on the next generator interaction — `g.next()`, `.return()`, or `.throw()`." T-API-66 covers the `.next()` branch; this covers `.return()`. `const gen = run("ralph", { signal: c.signal, maxIterations: 1 }); const { value } = await gen.next(); c.abort(); await expect(gen.return(undefined)).rejects.toThrow(<abort error>);` Assert the `.return()` call rejects with the abort error rather than settling `{ done: true, value: undefined }` silently. *(Spec 9.3, 9.1)*
- **T-API-66b**: Abort after final yield but before settlement produces abort error on subsequent `.throw()`. Same setup as T-API-66a. `const gen = run("ralph", { signal: c.signal, maxIterations: 1 }); const { value } = await gen.next(); c.abort(); await expect(gen.throw(new Error("consumer-err"))).rejects.toThrow(<abort error>);` Assert the `.throw()` call rejects with the **abort** error (the signal displaces the consumer-supplied error, per SPEC 9.3's abort-after-final-yield rule). Together, T-API-66 / T-API-66a / T-API-66b cover all three settle-triggering interactions enumerated in SPEC 9.3. *(Spec 9.3, 9.1)*

##### Pinned Priority

- **T-API-67**: Invalid `options.cwd` (non-string) surfaces before project-root-dependent discovery failure. Call `run("ralph", { cwd: 42 as any })` in a fixture where `.loopx/` does **not** exist at the current `process.cwd()`. Assert the first-`next()` error references the invalid `cwd` (not the missing `.loopx/`). Per Spec 9.3 "Pinned pre-iteration priority" — non-string `options.cwd` must surface before discovery errors. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-67a**: Throwing `options.cwd` getter surfaces before project-root-dependent discovery failure. Mirrors T-API-67 with a throwing getter. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-67b**: Invalid `options.envFile` (non-string) surfaces before project-root-dependent failure. Same structure — the invalid envFile surfaces before missing-`.loopx/` / discovery / env-file-load / target / tmpdir failures. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*
- **T-API-67c**: Throwing `options.envFile` getter surfaces before project-root-dependent failure. *(Spec 9.3, 9.5)*

##### Pre-First-`next()` Carve-out

Spec 9.1 defines a carve-out: `.return()` or `.throw()` as the consumer's *first* interaction with the generator returned by `run()` settles silently, suppressing all pre-iteration errors.

- **T-API-68**: `.return()` as first interaction suppresses invalid-target error. `const gen = run(undefined as any); await gen.return(undefined);` Assert no error is thrown. No child is spawned, no tmpdir created. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-68a**: `.return()` as first interaction suppresses discovery failure. Call in a fixture without `.loopx/`. `const gen = run("ralph"); await gen.return(undefined);` Assert no error. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-68b**: `.return()` as first interaction suppresses env-file-load failure. `const gen = run("ralph", { envFile: "nonexistent.env" }); await gen.return(undefined);` Assert no error. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-68c**: `.return()` as first interaction suppresses option-snapshot failure. `const gen = run("ralph", { maxIterations: -1 }); await gen.return(undefined);` Assert no error. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-68d**: `.return()` as first interaction suppresses pre-aborted signal. `const c = new AbortController(); c.abort(); const gen = run("ralph", { signal: c.signal }); await gen.return(undefined);` Assert no error. Per Spec 9.1: "A `signal` captured at call time is not consulted; even an already-aborted signal does not surface the abort error through this path." *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-68e**: `.return()` as first interaction does not create a tmpdir. Snapshot `os.tmpdir()` before and after the `.return()` call. Assert no new `loopx-*` directory was created. *(Spec 9.1, 7.4)*
- **T-API-69**: `.throw()` as first interaction — generator settles by throwing (consumer-supplied) error. `const gen = run(undefined as any); await expect(gen.throw(new Error("my-err"))).rejects.toThrow("my-err");` The consumer's error surfaces, not the invalid-target error. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-69a**: `.throw()` as first interaction suppresses env-file-load failure. `await gen.throw(new Error("my-err"))` where gen was created with invalid envFile. Consumer-error surfaces, not env-file error. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-69b**: `.throw()` as first interaction suppresses pre-aborted signal. Consumer-error surfaces, no abort error. *(Spec 9.1)*
- **T-API-69c**: `.throw()` as first interaction does not create a tmpdir. *(Spec 9.1, 7.4)*
- **T-API-70**: `runPromise` has no carve-out. `runPromise(undefined as any, { envFile: "nonexistent.env" })` always rejects; there is no `.return()` / `.throw()` path on a promise. Explicitly documents Spec 9.1 "This carve-out applies only to `run()`; `runPromise()` has no equivalent." The test is a pair of "both rejections happen" assertions on `runPromise` for each invalid input, matching T-API-68a/68b/68c/68d. *(Spec 9.2)*

##### Snapshot Timing (Inherited Env)

- **T-API-71**: `run()` inherited-env snapshot is lazy (captured at first `next()`). Set `process.env.MYVAR=A`. `const gen = run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 });` — no snapshot yet. Set `process.env.MYVAR=B` **before** `gen.next()`. Await `.next()`. Script observes `MYVAR`. Assert marker shows `"B"` — the mutation between `run()` returning and first `next()` is observed. *(Spec 9.1, 8.1)*
- **T-API-71a**: `run()` inherited-env snapshot is frozen at first `next()` (later mutations not observed). Set `process.env.MYVAR=A`. `const gen = run("ralph", { maxIterations: 2 }); await gen.next();` (first iteration captures `"A"`). Set `process.env.MYVAR=B`. `await gen.next();` (second iteration). Assert both iterations saw `"A"`. *(Spec 9.1, 8.1)*
- **T-API-72**: `runPromise()` inherited-env snapshot is eager (captured at call site). Set `process.env.MYVAR=A`. `const p = runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 });` — snapshot taken synchronously. Set `process.env.MYVAR=B`. Await `p`. Script observes `MYVAR`. Assert marker shows `"A"` — mutation after return did not propagate. *(Spec 9.2, 8.1)*

##### Global Env File Resolution Snapshot Timing (`XDG_CONFIG_HOME` / `HOME`)

SPEC 8.1 says global env-file path resolution (`$XDG_CONFIG_HOME/loopx/env`, or `$HOME/.config/loopx/env` fallback) reads `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` / `HOME` from the inherited environment on the **same schedule as the inherited-env snapshot**: lazy under `run()` (captured at first `next()`), eager under `runPromise()` (captured at the call site). T-API-71 / T-API-71a / T-API-72 cover inherited-env snapshot timing but do not exercise the `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` / `HOME` resolution path specifically — a buggy implementation could snapshot `process.env` lazily but read `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` / `HOME` eagerly (or vice versa).

- **T-API-73**: `run()` — `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` resolution is lazy (captured at first `next()`). Create two isolated config directories, `/tmp/xdg-A/loopx/env` (with `MARKER=from-A`) and `/tmp/xdg-B/loopx/env` (with `MARKER=from-B`). Set `process.env.XDG_CONFIG_HOME = "/tmp/xdg-A"`. Call `const gen = run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Set `process.env.XDG_CONFIG_HOME = "/tmp/xdg-B"` **before** `await gen.next()`. Script observes `MARKER`. Assert the marker shows `"from-B"` — the mutation between `run()` returning and first `next()` redirected global env-file lookup. A buggy implementation that read `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` eagerly would show `"from-A"`. *(Spec 9.1, 8.1)*
- **T-API-73a**: `runPromise()` — `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` resolution is eager (captured at call site). Same two-config setup as T-API-73. Set `process.env.XDG_CONFIG_HOME = "/tmp/xdg-A"`. Call `const p = runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })` — snapshot taken synchronously. Set `process.env.XDG_CONFIG_HOME = "/tmp/xdg-B"`. Await `p`. Script observes `MARKER`. Assert the marker shows `"from-A"` — mutation after return did not redirect global env-file lookup. *(Spec 9.2, 8.1)*
- **T-API-73b**: `run()` — `HOME` fallback resolution is lazy (captured at first `next()`). Unset `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` in `process.env` so loopx falls back to `$HOME/.config/loopx/env`. Create two isolated home directories, `/tmp/home-A/.config/loopx/env` (with `MARKER=from-A`) and `/tmp/home-B/.config/loopx/env` (with `MARKER=from-B`). Set `process.env.HOME = "/tmp/home-A"`. Call `const gen = run("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Set `process.env.HOME = "/tmp/home-B"` before `await gen.next()`. Script observes `MARKER`. Assert the marker shows `"from-B"` — the `HOME` mutation between `run()` returning and first `next()` redirected global env-file lookup via the fallback path. *(Spec 9.1, 8.1)*
- **T-API-73c**: `runPromise()` — `HOME` fallback resolution is eager (captured at call site). Same two-home setup as T-API-73b. Set `process.env.HOME = "/tmp/home-A"`, unset `XDG_CONFIG_HOME`. Call `const p = runPromise("ralph", { maxIterations: 1 })`. Set `process.env.HOME = "/tmp/home-B"`. Await `p`. Script observes `MARKER`. Assert the marker shows `"from-A"` — mutation after return did not affect the fallback path. *(Spec 9.2, 8.1)*

### 4.10 Install Command

**Spec refs:** 10.1–10.9

All install tests use local servers (HTTP, file:// git repos). No network access.

#### Source Detection

- **T-INST-01**: `loopx install myorg/my-workflow` is treated as a git source (github shorthand). Verify by using `withGitURLRewrite` to redirect to a local bare repo, and asserting workflows are installed into `.loopx/`. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-01a**: `loopx install myorg/my-workflow.git` → error, exit code 1. The shorthand must not end in `.git`. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-02**: `loopx install https://github.com/org/repo` → treated as git (known host). *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-03**: `loopx install https://gitlab.com/org/repo` → treated as git. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-04**: `loopx install https://bitbucket.org/org/repo` → treated as git. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-05**: `loopx install https://example.com/repo.git` → treated as git (.git suffix). *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-06**: `loopx install http://localhost:PORT/pkg.tar.gz` → treated as tarball. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-07**: `loopx install http://localhost:PORT/pkg.tgz` → treated as tarball. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-08**: `loopx install http://localhost:PORT/script.ts` → rejected (single-file URL install is not supported). Error, exit code 1. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-08a**: `loopx install https://github.com/org/repo/archive/main.tar.gz` → treated as tarball (not git). *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-08c**: `loopx install https://github.com/org/repo/` → treated as git (trailing slash allowed). *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-08d**: `loopx install http://localhost:PORT/pkg.tar.gz?token=abc` → treated as tarball. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-08e**: `loopx install http://localhost:PORT/some-file.js` → rejected. Any URL that is not git or tarball is an error. *(Spec 10.1)*
- **T-INST-08f**: `loopx install https://github.com/org/repo/tree/main` → rejected. Known-host git detection only matches exact `/<owner>/<repo>` or `/<owner>/<repo>.git` paths. A URL with additional path segments (like `/tree/main`) is not treated as a git repo. Since it is also not a tarball URL, it is rejected with an error (exit code 1). *(Spec 10.1)*

#### Install CLI Parsing

- **T-INST-40**: `loopx install` with no source → usage error, exit code 1. *(Spec 4.2, 10)*
- **T-INST-40a**: `loopx install -w ralph` with no source → usage error, exit code 1. The `-w` flag does not substitute for the required `<source>` argument. *(Spec 4.2, 10)*
- **T-INST-40b**: `loopx install --workflow ralph` with no source → usage error, exit code 1. Same as T-INST-40a using the long-form `--workflow` flag. *(Spec 4.2, 10)*
- **T-INST-40c**: `loopx install -y` with no source → usage error, exit code 1. The `-y` flag does not substitute for the required `<source>` argument. *(Spec 4.2, 10)*
- **T-INST-40d**: `loopx install <source1> <source2>` → usage error, exit code 1. The install grammar accepts exactly one positional source argument; extra positionals are rejected. *(Spec 4.2, 10)*
- **T-INST-40e**: `loopx install -w ralph <source1> <source2>` → usage error, exit code 1. Extra positionals are rejected even when combined with the `-w` flag. *(Spec 4.2, 10)*
- **T-INST-41**: `loopx install -h` → install help, exit 0. Source not required. Assert that the help text explicitly lists: (a) `-w` / `--workflow` option with description, (b) `-y` option with description, (c) **`--no-install` option with description** (per SPEC 4.2 / 11.3 — suppresses auto-install of workflow dependencies per Spec 10.10), (d) supported source types (git repos, tarballs, `org/repo` shorthand), and (e) does NOT mention single-file URL install as a supported source type — single-file URL install was removed (ADR-0003) and the help text must not advertise it. *(Spec 4.2, 10.1, 10.10, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-41a**: `loopx install --help` produces identical stdout, stderr, and exit code as `loopx install -h`. Run both in the same fixture. Assert: (a) stdout is byte-identical between the two invocations, (b) stderr is byte-identical, and (c) both exit 0. This proves the `--help` long form is a true alias for `-h`, consistent with the top-level and run help `--help` parity tests (T-CLI-03, T-CLI-41). *(Spec 4.2, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-42**: `loopx install -h --unknown` → install help, exit 0 (unknown flag ignored under `-h`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-42a**: `loopx install -h http://localhost:PORT/pkg.tar.gz` → install help, exit 0. Start a local HTTP server that tracks incoming requests. Assert: (a) help is shown, (b) the HTTP server received zero requests, and (c) `.loopx/` was not created or modified. Proves that `-h` makes no network requests even when a valid source is provided. *(Spec 4.2, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-42b**: `loopx install http://localhost:PORT/pkg.tar.gz -h` → install help, exit 0. Same assertions as T-INST-42a (zero HTTP requests, `.loopx/` untouched). Proves `-h` after the source argument also short-circuits without network activity. *(Spec 4.2, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-42c**: `loopx install -h` with `.loopx/` containing a broken workflow tree — an invalid workflow name (e.g., `.loopx/-bad-workflow/index.sh`), a name collision (e.g., `check.sh` and `check.ts` in the same workflow), and an invalid script name (e.g., `-bad.sh`) — still exits 0. Assert: (a) help text is shown, (b) stderr contains no discovery or validation warnings, and (c) exit code is 0. This proves install help does not inspect `.loopx/`, per Spec 11.3. *(Spec 4.2, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-42d**: `loopx install --help http://localhost:PORT/pkg.tar.gz` → install help, exit 0. Start a local HTTP server that tracks incoming requests. Assert: (a) help is shown, (b) the HTTP server received zero requests, and (c) `.loopx/` was not created or modified. This is the long-form counterpart to T-INST-42a. T-INST-41a proves `--help` and `-h` produce identical output, but output parity alone would not catch an implementation that fetches the source before short-circuiting — this test verifies the behavioral guarantee that `--help` makes no network requests or filesystem changes. *(Spec 4.2, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-42e**: `loopx install --help --unknown` → install help, exit 0. The long-form `--help` in leading position short-circuits, ignoring the unrecognized `--unknown` flag. This is the `--help`-first counterpart to T-INST-42 (`-h --unknown`) and T-INST-49d (`--unknown --help`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-42f**: `loopx install --help --workflow` → install help, exit 0. The long-form `--help` in leading position short-circuits, ignoring the `--workflow` flag (which has no operand). This is the `--help` long-form counterpart to T-INST-48 (`-h -w`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-42g**: `loopx install -h <source1> <source2>` → install help, exit 0. Start a local HTTP server that tracks incoming requests. Assert: (a) help is shown, (b) the HTTP server received zero requests, and (c) `.loopx/` was not created or modified. The extra positionals do not prevent the help short-circuit and no network requests are made. This is the help-side counterpart to T-INST-40d (extra positionals without `-h` → usage error). *(Spec 4.2, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-42h**: `loopx install <source1> <source2> --help` → install help, exit 0. Start a local HTTP server that tracks incoming requests. Assert: (a) help is shown, (b) the HTTP server received zero requests, and (c) `.loopx/` was not created or modified. The `--help` after multiple positionals still short-circuits. This is the trailing-help counterpart to T-INST-42g. *(Spec 4.2, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-42i**: `loopx install --help -w a -w b` → install help, exit 0. The long-form `--help` short-circuits, ignoring the duplicate `-w` flags. This is the `--help`-first counterpart to T-INST-49b (`-w a -w b -h`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-42j**: `loopx install --help -y -y` → install help, exit 0. The long-form `--help` short-circuits, ignoring the duplicate `-y` flags. This is the `--help`-first counterpart to T-INST-49c (`-y -y -h`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-42k**: `loopx install http://localhost:PORT/script.ts -h` → install help, exit 0. Start a local HTTP server that tracks incoming requests and serves a file at `/script.ts`. Assert: (a) help is shown, (b) the HTTP server received zero requests (the rejected source triggered no network activity), (c) `.loopx/` was not created or modified, and (d) stderr contains no single-file-URL-rejection error. This proves help short-circuit suppresses source classification errors — a single-file URL is normally rejected (T-INST-08) with an error under ADR-0003, but the help short-circuit must fire before source classification. T-INST-42a/42b cover help with valid sources (no network); this test covers the stronger guarantee that help also suppresses source-type validation. *(Spec 4.2, 10.1, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-42l**: `loopx install org/repo.git --help` → install help, exit 0. Assert: (a) help is shown, (b) stderr contains no error about the `.git` suffix being disallowed in the `org/repo` shorthand, and (c) `.loopx/` was not created or modified. The `org/repo.git` form is normally rejected (T-INST-01a) because the shorthand must not end in `.git`, but the `--help` short-circuit must fire before shorthand validation. This is the long-form `--help` counterpart to T-INST-42k and proves help suppresses a second distinct source classification error (invalid `org/repo` shorthand), complementing the single-file URL coverage in T-INST-42k. *(Spec 4.2, 10.1, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-43**: `loopx install -w a -w b <source>` → usage error, exit code 1 (duplicate `-w`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-43a**: `loopx install --workflow a --workflow b <source>` → usage error, exit code 1 (duplicate `--workflow`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-43b**: `loopx install -w a --workflow b <source>` → usage error, exit code 1 (duplicate workflow flag — mixed short and long forms still count as a duplicate). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-44**: `loopx install -y -y <source>` → usage error, exit code 1 (duplicate `-y`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-44a**: `loopx install --no-install --no-install <source>` → usage error, exit code 1 (duplicate `--no-install`). Per Spec 4.2, repeating `--no-install` is a usage error unless `-h` / `--help` is present. This extends the duplicate-flag rejection pattern established by T-INST-43 (`-w`), T-INST-43a (`--workflow`), T-INST-43b (mixed), and T-INST-44 (`-y`) to the new `--no-install` flag added by Spec 10.10. *(Spec 4.2, 10.10)*
- **T-INST-44b**: `loopx install -h --no-install <source>` → install help, exit 0. The `-h` short-circuit ignores `--no-install` entirely (no validation of its presence or absence). Source is present, but help short-circuit suppresses install. Assert: (a) help stdout, (b) exit 0, (c) no source download / network activity, (d) `.loopx/` untouched. Extends T-INST-42 / T-INST-42a pattern to `--no-install`. *(Spec 4.2, 10.10, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-44c**: `loopx install --help --no-install --no-install <source>` → install help, exit 0. The `--help` short-circuit also suppresses duplicate-`--no-install` usage errors — Spec 4.2 says the short-circuit ignores all other install-level arguments unconditionally (including duplicate or extraneous `--no-install`). Assert help output, exit 0, no duplicate-flag error on stderr. *(Spec 4.2, 10.10, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-44d**: `loopx install --no-install -h <source>` → install help, exit 0. `--no-install` appearing before `-h` does not block the late-help short-circuit pattern (T-INST-49a–49g). Assert help output, exit 0. *(Spec 4.2, 10.10, 11.3)*
- **T-INST-45**: `loopx install --unknown <source>` → usage error, exit code 1 (unrecognized flag). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-45a**: `loopx install -x <source>` → usage error, exit code 1 (unrecognized short flag). This is the install-scoped counterpart to T-CLI-72 (`loopx run -x ralph`), ensuring short flags are rejected identically to long flags. *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-46**: `loopx install -h -w a -w b` shows install help and exits 0 (duplicate `-w` not rejected under help). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-47**: `loopx install -h -y -y` shows install help and exits 0 (duplicate `-y` not rejected under help). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-48**: `loopx install -h -w` shows install help and exits 0 (missing `-w` operand not rejected under help). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-49**: `loopx install -w` (no operand for `-w`, no source) exits with code 1 (usage error). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-49e**: `loopx install --workflow` (no operand for `--workflow`, no source) exits with code 1 (usage error). This is the long-form counterpart to T-INST-49. *(Spec 4.2)*

#### Late-Help Short-Circuit (Invalid Args Before `-h`)

- **T-INST-49a**: `loopx install --unknown -h` shows install help and exits 0. The unrecognized flag before `-h` does not prevent the help short-circuit. *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-49b**: `loopx install -w a -w b -h` shows install help and exits 0. The duplicate `-w` before `-h` does not prevent the help short-circuit. *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-49c**: `loopx install -y -y -h` shows install help and exits 0. The duplicate `-y` before `-h` does not prevent the help short-circuit. *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-49d**: `loopx install --unknown --help` shows install help and exits 0. Long-form `--help` after invalid args also short-circuits. *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-49f**: `loopx install -w -h` shows install help and exits 0. A naive parser would consume `-h` as the operand for `-w`, but the `-h` short-circuit fires unconditionally when `-h` is present — all other install-level arguments are ignored. This is the missing-operand counterpart to T-INST-49a–49d (which cover invalid or duplicate flags before `-h`). *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-INST-49g**: `loopx install --workflow --help` shows install help and exits 0. Long-form counterpart to T-INST-49f: `--workflow` would consume `--help` as its operand in naive parsing, but the help short-circuit ignores all other arguments unconditionally. *(Spec 4.2)*

#### Workflow Classification — Single-Workflow Source

- **T-INST-50**: Git repo with root-level `index.ts`, a non-script file (`package.json`), and a pure non-script root directory (`docs/` containing only `.md` files — no supported script extensions) → single-workflow source. Entire repo installed as `.loopx/<repo-name>/`. Assert the workflow directory contains all root-level files including non-script files (`package.json`) **and** non-script directories (`docs/`). This covers the ADR-0003 rule that all root files and directories are copied for single-workflow sources, including directories that contain no script-extension files. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-50a**: Git repo with root-level `index.js` → single-workflow source. Installed as `.loopx/<repo-name>/`. This extends install-path extension coverage (T-INST-50 covers `.ts`) to positively verify that `.js` is recognized as a supported script extension in the install single-workflow classification codepath. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-50b**: Parameterized: single-workflow root classification for all five supported extensions. For each extension in [`.sh`, `.js`, `.jsx`, `.ts`, `.tsx`], create a git repo with a single root-level `index.<ext>` file. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: the source is classified as single-workflow and installed as `.loopx/<repo-name>/`. T-INST-50 covers `.ts` and T-INST-50a covers `.js` individually; this parameterized test closes the gaps for `.sh`, `.jsx`, and `.tsx` and exercises all five extensions uniformly in the single-workflow root classification codepath. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-51**: Git repo with root-level `index.ts` and a `lib/` subdirectory containing `.ts` files → still single-workflow (root-level script files take precedence unconditionally). `lib/` is workflow content, not a separate workflow. Assert `.loopx/<repo-name>/lib/` exists. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-52**: Root-level script files force single-workflow classification even when subdirectories also contain scripts. Git repo with root-level `index.sh` and two subdirectories `tools/` and `helpers/` that each contain their own top-level script files (e.g., `tools/build.sh`, `helpers/setup.ts`) — subdirectories that would themselves qualify as workflows in a multi-workflow source. `loopx install <source>` → single-workflow install. Assert: (a) `.loopx/<repo-name>/` is created (single workflow, named after the repo), (b) `.loopx/<repo-name>/tools/build.sh` and `.loopx/<repo-name>/helpers/setup.ts` exist (subdirectories are copied inside the workflow as content), (c) `.loopx/tools/` and `.loopx/helpers/` do **not** exist (the subdirectories are NOT installed as sibling workflows). This pins down the ADR-0003 "root-level script files take precedence unconditionally" rule — the presence of `index.sh` at the root forces single-workflow classification, and the would-be-workflow subdirectories are treated as workflow internals. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-52a**: Root-level "config-style" file with a supported extension (e.g., `eslint.config.js` or `vitest.config.ts`) at the repository root forces single-workflow classification, even when subdirectories also qualify as workflows (contain their own top-level script files). The config file is a root-level file with a supported script extension, so it triggers the single-workflow rule unconditionally. Additionally, the config file is a top-level script candidate whose base name (e.g., `eslint.config`) contains a dot — violating the script naming restriction `[a-zA-Z0-9_][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*`. Assert that install classifies the source as single-workflow AND fails with a validation error about the invalid script name. The sibling subdirectories are not treated as separate workflows. *(Spec 10.3, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-52c**: Root-level non-index script file forces single-workflow classification even when subdirectories qualify as workflows. Git repo with root-level `setup.ts` (but no `index.*` file) and two subdirectories `ralph/` and `other/` that each contain their own top-level script files (e.g., `ralph/index.sh`, `other/index.sh`) — subdirectories that would qualify as workflows in a multi-workflow source. `loopx install <source>` → single-workflow install. Assert: (a) `.loopx/<repo-name>/` is created (single workflow, named after the repo), (b) `.loopx/<repo-name>/setup.ts`, `.loopx/<repo-name>/ralph/index.sh`, and `.loopx/<repo-name>/other/index.sh` exist (subdirectories are copied as workflow content), (c) `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/` do **not** exist (the subdirectories are NOT installed as sibling workflows), and (d) no error about missing `index` — a missing default entry point is allowed at install time. T-INST-52 uses `index.sh` at the root and T-INST-52a uses a root-level file with an invalid name; this pins down that **any** valid root-level script file — not just one named `index` — forces single-workflow classification independently of the default entry point convention. *(Spec 10.3, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-52d**: Root-level "config-style" file with a supported extension in a tarball source forces single-workflow classification, same as for git sources. Create a `.tar.gz` whose source root (after any wrapper-directory stripping) contains `eslint.config.js` at the root level, plus subdirectories that would themselves qualify as workflows (e.g., `ralph/index.sh` and `other/index.sh`). `loopx install <tarball-url>` → the source is classified as single-workflow (the root-level `.js` file triggers the rule unconditionally), and install fails with a validation error about the invalid script name (`eslint.config` contains a dot that violates the naming restriction `[a-zA-Z0-9_][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*`). Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) the error references the invalid script name, (c) `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/` do NOT exist (sibling subdirectories were not installed as separate workflows). This is the tarball counterpart to T-INST-52a (git). Per SPEC 10.2, classification after extraction is source-type-agnostic, so the "root-level supported-extension config file forces single-workflow classification" rule must hold for both source types. *(Spec 10.2, 10.3, 10.4)*

#### Workflow Classification — Multi-Workflow Source

- **T-INST-53**: Git repo with no root-level script files but two subdirectories `ralph/` and `other/` each containing an `index.sh` → multi-workflow source. Both installed as `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/`. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-53a**: Multi-workflow git repo where one subdirectory qualifies via `index.jsx`. Source contains `ralph/index.sh` and `other/index.jsx`, with no root-level script files → both installed as `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/`. This extends install-path extension coverage (T-INST-53 covers `.sh`) to positively verify that `.jsx` is recognized in the install multi-workflow classification codepath. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-53b**: Multi-workflow git repo where one subdirectory qualifies via `index.tsx`. Source contains `ralph/index.sh` and `other/index.tsx`, with no root-level script files → both installed as `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/`. This extends install-path extension coverage to positively verify that `.tsx` is recognized in the install multi-workflow classification codepath. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-53c**: Parameterized: multi-workflow subdirectory classification for all five supported extensions. For each extension in [`.sh`, `.js`, `.jsx`, `.ts`, `.tsx`], create a multi-workflow git repo where one subdirectory (`target/`) qualifies via a single `index.<ext>` file, alongside another valid workflow `other/index.sh`, with no root-level script files. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: both `target` and `other` are installed. T-INST-53 covers `.sh`, T-INST-53a covers `.jsx`, and T-INST-53b covers `.tsx` individually; this parameterized test closes the gaps for `.js` and `.ts` and exercises all five extensions uniformly in the multi-workflow subdirectory classification codepath. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-54**: Multi-workflow repo: repo-root support files (README, LICENSE, `package.json`, etc.) are NOT copied into `.loopx/`. Only workflow directories are installed. Assert that a root `package.json` in the source does not create `.loopx/package.json` **and** that a root `README.md` in the source does not create `.loopx/README.md`. Both file types are repo-level support files that must be excluded when only workflow directories are copied. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-54a**: Multi-workflow install preserves workflow-internal non-script files and subdirectories. Source repo contains `ralph/index.ts`, `ralph/package.json`, `ralph/lib/helpers.ts`, and `ralph/README.md` (plus `other/index.sh` to force multi-workflow classification). After install, assert `.loopx/ralph/package.json`, `.loopx/ralph/lib/helpers.ts`, and `.loopx/ralph/README.md` are all present. This verifies that the entire workflow directory — not just discovered script files — is copied. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-54b**: Multi-workflow source-root `package.json` is ignored during validation and version checking. Source repo contains `ralph/index.sh`, `other/index.sh`, and a repo-root `package.json` that is either invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`) or declares a loopx version range not satisfied by the running version. `loopx install <source>` succeeds, installing both workflows. Assert: no warning or error on stderr related to `package.json` or version mismatch. In the workflow model, only each workflow's own `package.json` matters for version checking — the repo-root file is a support file that is neither copied (T-INST-54) nor read for validation. *(Spec 10.3, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-54c**: Multi-workflow install does not copy root support directories. Source repo contains `ralph/index.sh`, `other/index.sh`, `docs/README.md`, and `shared/config.json`. After install, assert `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/` exist, but `.loopx/docs/` and `.loopx/shared/` do not exist. This is the directory counterpart to T-INST-54 (which covers root support files) — T-INST-55 verifies that non-workflow subdirectories are silently skipped during classification, but does not assert their absence from the destination. A buggy installer that correctly classifies workflows but still copies all subdirectories into `.loopx/` would pass T-INST-55 but fail here. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-54d**: Multi-workflow tarball source-root `package.json` is ignored during validation and version checking. Create a `.tar.gz` whose source root (after any wrapper-directory stripping) contains workflow subdirectories `ralph/index.sh` and `other/index.sh`, plus a source-root `package.json` that is either invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`) or declares a loopx version range not satisfied by the running version. `loopx install <tarball-url>` succeeds, installing both workflows. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) both `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/` are installed, (c) no warning or error on stderr related to `package.json` or version mismatch, and (d) `.loopx/package.json` does not exist (the source-root file was not copied). This is the tarball counterpart to T-INST-54b (git multi-workflow): per SPEC 10.2, classification after extraction is source-type-agnostic, so the "source-root `package.json` is not read for multi-workflow classification or version checking" rule must hold for both source types. *(Spec 10.2, 10.3, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-55**: Multi-workflow repo: subdirectories with no script files are silently skipped. They don't cause failure. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-55a**: Non-recursive workflow detection during install classification. Multi-workflow source contains a candidate directory `tools/` with only nested supported-extension files (e.g., `tools/lib/helper.ts`) and no top-level script files (no `tools/*.sh|js|jsx|ts|tsx`). That directory is skipped as a non-workflow — only top-level files count for workflow detection. Other valid workflow directories in the source are installed normally. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-55c**: Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` contains only `index.mjs` (unsupported extension) alongside valid workflow `other/` (containing `index.sh`). `ralph/` is skipped as a non-workflow — `.mjs` is not a supported script extension, so the directory has no top-level script files. Assert: (a) only `.loopx/other/` is installed, (b) `.loopx/ralph/` does not exist, and (c) no warning or error about `ralph/`. This is the install-time counterpart to T-DISC-06/07, which cover `.mjs`/`.cjs` being unrecognized at runtime discovery. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-55b**: Multi-workflow source with an invalid-named non-workflow subdirectory. Source repo contains `ralph/index.sh`, `other/index.sh`, and `-bad-dir/README.md` (no script files — not a workflow). Install succeeds, installing only `ralph` and `other`. The `-bad-dir` directory is silently skipped with no error or warning about its invalid name. This locks down the rule that name validation applies only to discovered workflows — directories that don't qualify as workflows are never validated, even if their names would fail the naming restriction pattern. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-55e**: Multi-workflow source containing a legacy-style directory-script subdirectory is handled correctly: the legacy subdirectory is skipped, and only valid workflow directories are installed. Source repo has `good/index.sh` plus `legacy/package.json` (with `{ "main": "src/run.js" }`) and `legacy/src/run.js`, but **no** top-level files with supported script extensions inside `legacy/` (the only supported-extension file is nested in `src/`). `loopx install <source>` → exits 0. Assert: (a) `.loopx/good/` is installed and contains `index.sh`, (b) `.loopx/legacy/` does **not** exist — the `legacy/` directory had no top-level script files and was silently skipped as a non-workflow. This is the multi-workflow-subdirectory counterpart to T-INST-56a (which covers the source-root legacy directory-script as a zero-workflow case). T-CLI-104c and T-DISC-20c cover runtime non-discovery of legacy directory-script layouts; this covers the install classification path for a legacy subdirectory coexisting with valid workflows. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-55d**: Root-level unsupported script-like files (`.mjs`/`.cjs`) do not force single-workflow classification. Source root contains `index.mjs` (or `config.cjs`) plus `ralph/index.sh` and `other/index.sh`. Because `.mjs` and `.cjs` are not supported script extensions (Spec 2.1), the root has no files with supported extensions and the source is classified as multi-workflow — both `ralph` and `other` are installed. Assert: `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/` exist. This pins down the boundary between T-INST-50a (supported root-level files force single-workflow) and T-INST-56c/55c (unsupported extensions are ignored) for the case where valid workflow subdirectories coexist with unsupported root files. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*

#### Workflow Classification — Zero-Workflow Source

- **T-INST-56**: Git repo with no root-level script files and no subdirectories that qualify as workflows → error. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-56a**: A source repo structured as a legacy directory script — root `package.json` with `main` pointing to a deeply nested file (e.g., `{ "main": "src/app/run.js" }`), with the script file only inside a nested subdirectory (`src/app/`) and no top-level files with supported script extensions. The top-level `src/` directory contains no top-level script files (`src/*.{sh,js,jsx,ts,tsx}`) so it does not qualify as a workflow — the source is classified as zero-workflow and rejected with an error. Assert exit code 1 and that the error indicates no installable workflows were found. This proves the install mechanism does not fall back to legacy directory-script install behavior — the `main` field is not used for workflow classification. *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-56e**: Legacy directory-script source is rejected as zero-workflow without migration-guidance messaging. Create a source root with a `package.json` whose `main` points to a nested file (e.g., `{ "main": "src/app/run.js" }`) and no top-level files with supported script extensions (the script file lives only inside a nested subdirectory like `src/app/run.js`). Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) the error indicates no installable workflows were found, and (c) — **structurally** rather than by prose blacklisting — stderr does not contain a migration-guidance or deprecation warning as a separate output category alongside the zero-workflow error. Concretely: the stderr output is limited to the standard "no installable workflows found" error (and any unrelated warnings that would be emitted regardless of the legacy layout). There is no additional warning/notice/advisory line whose subject is the legacy directory-script layout (the `main` field, the nested script file, or the `package.json`-without-top-level-scripts shape are not flagged in any extra output category beyond the routine zero-workflow rejection). Prose-level phrase matching is intentionally avoided — the check targets the presence of a distinct migration-warning output category, not specific wording. T-INST-56a proves the zero-workflow rejection for this shape; this test extends it with the structural anti-migration-messaging assertion, aligning install behavior with ADR-0003's explicit "no legacy compatibility or migration tooling" consequence and mirroring runtime coverage in T-DISC-10a (flat script) and T-DISC-20c (directory script). *(Spec 10.3)*
- **T-INST-56c**: Source root containing only `index.mjs` at root level (no files with supported extensions) → zero-workflow error. `.mjs` is not a supported script extension (Spec 2.1), so no script files are found at the root level and no subdirectories qualify as workflows. This is the install-classification counterpart to T-DISC-06, which covers `.mjs` being unrecognized at runtime discovery. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-56d**: Source root containing only `index.cjs` at root level → zero-workflow error. `.cjs` is not a supported script extension. This is the install-classification counterpart to T-DISC-07. *(Spec 10.3, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-56b**: Tarball source with no installable workflows → error. Create a `.tar.gz` whose source root (after wrapper-directory stripping) contains no root-level script files and no subdirectories that qualify as workflows (e.g., only `README.md` and a `lib/` directory with `.ts` files nested inside). `loopx install <tarball-url>` → exits with code 1 with an error indicating no installable workflows were found. This is the tarball counterpart to T-INST-56 (git zero-workflow) — the classification logic is source-type-agnostic, so both source types must reject zero-workflow sources. *(Spec 10.3, 10.2)*

#### Selective Workflow Installation

- **T-INST-57**: `loopx install -w ralph <multi-workflow-source>` installs only `ralph`. Assert `.loopx/ralph/` exists but `.loopx/other/` does not. *(Spec 10.8)*
- **T-INST-57a**: `loopx install --workflow ralph <multi-workflow-source>` is equivalent to `loopx install -w ralph <source>`. Assert `.loopx/ralph/` exists but `.loopx/other/` does not. This tests the long-form `--workflow` flag. *(Spec 4.2, 10.8)*
- **T-INST-57b**: `loopx install -w ralph <multi-workflow-source>` where the source root also contains `README.md`, `package.json`, `docs/`, `shared/`, and a sibling workflow `other/` (with `index.sh`) → only `.loopx/ralph/` is created. Assert: no source-root support files or directories (`README.md`, `package.json`, `docs/`, `shared/`) are copied into `.loopx/`, and `.loopx/other/` does not exist. This is the `-w` counterpart to T-INST-54 / T-INST-54c, which prove self-containment for full multi-workflow installs — the same rule must hold on the selective `-w` code path. *(Spec 10.3, 10.8)*
- **T-INST-57c**: `loopx install -w ralph <multi-workflow-tarball>` installs only `ralph`. Create a `.tar.gz` whose source root (after any wrapper-directory stripping) contains subdirectories `ralph/` (with `index.sh`) and `other/` (with `index.sh`), with no root-level script files. Run `loopx install -w ralph <tarball-url>`. Assert: (a) `.loopx/ralph/` is installed and contains `index.sh`, and (b) `.loopx/other/` does not exist. T-INST-57 / T-INST-57a / T-INST-57b cover the `-w` selective-install path with git-backed sources; this test explicitly exercises the tarball source path. Per SPEC 10.2, classification after extraction is source-type-agnostic, so the selective-install behavior must hold identically for tarball and git sources — this closes the gap left by the otherwise git-heavy `-w` coverage. *(Spec 10.2, 10.8)*
- **T-INST-58**: `loopx install -w nonexistent <multi-workflow-source>` → error (workflow not in source). *(Spec 10.8)*
- **T-INST-59**: `loopx install -w ralph <single-workflow-source>` → error (`-w` is invalid for single-workflow sources). The source must have root-level script files (e.g., `index.ts`) **and** subdirectories containing supported-extension files (e.g., `lib/helpers.ts`, `src/utils.js`), so the test genuinely proves that root-level scripts force single-workflow classification even in the presence of subdirectories with script-extension files. Using `-w` is an error regardless of the name provided. *(Spec 10.3, 10.8)*
- **T-INST-59a**: `loopx install --workflow ralph <single-workflow-source>` → error. Long-form `--workflow` parity with T-INST-59: `--workflow` is invalid for single-workflow sources, same as `-w`. *(Spec 10.8, 4.2)*
- **T-INST-59b**: `loopx install -w ralph <single-workflow-source>` → error, where the source root contains a **non-index** script file (e.g., `setup.ts`) **and** subdirectories that would themselves qualify as workflows (e.g., `lib/helpers.ts`, `src/utils.js`). T-INST-59 / T-INST-59a use a root-level `index.ts` and so can be satisfied by an implementation that only treats `index.*` as the single-workflow trigger; this test uses a non-index root script so it proves the `-w` rejection fires for **any** root-level script file, not just the default entry point. Aligns the `-w` rejection coverage with T-INST-52c (which proves the same non-index root-script classification rule at the classification level). *(Spec 10.3, 10.8)*
- **T-INST-60**: With `-w`, only the selected workflow is validated. Invalid sibling workflows don't block installation. *(Spec 10.8)*
- **T-INST-60a**: With `-w`, source-validation failures in unselected sibling workflows do not block installation. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` is valid (contains `index.sh`) and `broken/` has an invalid script name (e.g., `broken/-bad.sh`). `loopx install -w ralph <source>` succeeds and `.loopx/ralph/` is created — the invalid script name in `broken/` is not evaluated because `-w ralph` limits preflight to the selected workflow only. *(Spec 10.8, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-60b**: With `-w`, version mismatches in unselected sibling workflows do not block installation and emit no warnings. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` has no version declaration (no `package.json`) and `other/` declares a loopx range not satisfied by the running version. `loopx install -w ralph <source>` succeeds — `other/`'s version mismatch is not evaluated because `-w ralph` limits preflight to the selected workflow only. Assert: exit code 0 **and** stderr contains no version-mismatch warning for `other/`. *(Spec 10.8, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-60c**: With `-w`, destination collisions for unselected sibling workflows do not block installation. Multi-workflow source contains `ralph/` (with `index.sh`) and `other/` (with `index.sh`). `.loopx/other/` already exists as a workflow (contains at least one script file). `loopx install -w ralph <source>` succeeds without `-y` — `other/`'s destination collision is not evaluated because `-w ralph` limits preflight to the selected workflow only. *(Spec 10.8, 10.5)*
- **T-INST-60d**: With `-w`, an invalid workflow name on an unselected sibling does not block installation. Multi-workflow source contains `ralph/` (with `index.sh`) and `-bad-name/` (with `index.sh` — valid scripts but invalid workflow name). `loopx install -w ralph <source>` succeeds — the invalid workflow name in `-bad-name/` is not evaluated because `-w ralph` limits preflight to the selected workflow only. *(Spec 10.8, 5.3)*
- **T-INST-60e**: With `-w`, a same-base-name collision in an unselected sibling does not block installation. Multi-workflow source contains `ralph/` (with `index.sh`) and `other/` (with `check.sh` and `check.ts`). `loopx install -w ralph <source>` succeeds — `other/`'s same-base-name collision is not evaluated because `-w ralph` limits preflight to the selected workflow only. *(Spec 10.8, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-60f**: With `-w`, a broken `package.json` in an unselected sibling workflow emits no warning. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` is valid (contains `index.sh`, no `package.json`) and `broken/` contains `index.sh` plus a `package.json` with invalid JSON content (e.g., `{broken`). `loopx install -w ralph <source>` succeeds. Assert: no `package.json`-related warning or error on stderr. The broken sibling's `package.json` is never read because `-w ralph` limits all validation — including version checking — to the selected workflow only. *(Spec 10.8, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-60g**: With `-w`, the selected workflow's own invalid script names are still fatal. Multi-workflow source where `broken/` contains `-bad.sh` (invalid script name) and `ralph/` is valid (contains `index.sh`). `loopx install -w broken <source>` → exits with code 1. T-INST-60a proves unselected siblings' invalid names are ignored; this proves the selected workflow itself is not exempt from install-time validation under `-w`. *(Spec 10.8, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-60h**: With `-w`, the selected workflow's own same-base-name collisions are still fatal. Multi-workflow source where `broken/` contains `check.sh` and `check.ts` (same base name, different extensions) and `ralph/` is valid (contains `index.sh`). `loopx install -w broken <source>` → exits with code 1. T-INST-60e proves unselected siblings' collisions are ignored; this proves the selected workflow itself is still checked. *(Spec 10.8, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-60i**: With `-w`, the selected workflow's own version mismatch is still a blocking error. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` contains `index.sh` plus a `package.json` declaring a `loopx` version range not satisfied by the running version, and `other/` is valid (contains `index.sh`, no `package.json`). `loopx install -w ralph <source>` → exits with code 1. T-INST-60b proves unselected siblings' version mismatches are ignored; this proves the selected workflow's version declaration is still enforced under `-w`. *(Spec 10.8, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-60j**: With `-w -y`, the selected workflow's version mismatch is overridden. Same source as T-INST-60i. `loopx install -w -y ralph <source>` succeeds. Assert `.loopx/ralph/` is created and contains `index.sh` and the workflow's `package.json` with its version declaration preserved. *(Spec 10.8, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-60k**: With `-w`, the selected workflow's own destination collision is still a blocking error. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` contains `index.sh` and `other/` is valid (contains `index.sh`). `.loopx/ralph/` already exists as a workflow (contains at least one top-level script file). `loopx install -w ralph <source>` → exits with code 1. T-INST-60c proves unselected siblings' destination collisions are ignored; this proves the selected workflow's collision is still enforced under `-w`. *(Spec 10.8, 10.5)*
- **T-INST-60l**: With `-w -y`, the selected workflow's destination collision is overridden. Same setup as T-INST-60k. `loopx install -w -y ralph <source>` succeeds. Assert `.loopx/ralph/` contains the new workflow content from the source (not the old content). `.loopx/other/` does not exist — only the selected workflow is installed. *(Spec 10.8, 10.5)*
- **T-INST-60p**: With `-w -y`, a non-workflow destination for the selected workflow still causes failure. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` contains `index.sh` and `other/` is valid (contains `index.sh`). `.loopx/ralph` already exists but is not a workflow by structure (e.g., a plain file, an empty directory, or a symlink to a non-workflow target). `loopx install -w ralph -y <source>` → exits with code 1. The `-y` flag overrides workflow-path collisions and version mismatches, but does not override non-workflow destination paths — even on the selective `-w` code path. T-INST-60k/60l cover the `-w` collision path where the destination is a real workflow; T-INST-68/69/70a/70c cover non-workflow collision refusal on the generic (non-`-w`) path. This combination is worth testing because `-w` often gets its own code path. *(Spec 10.8, 10.5)*
- **T-INST-60m**: With `-w`, selecting a workflow with an invalid name causes install to fail. Multi-workflow source contains `-bad-name/` (with `index.sh` — valid scripts but invalid workflow name) and `good/` (with `index.sh`). `loopx install -w -bad-name <source>` → exits with code 1. T-INST-60d proves an unselected invalid workflow name does not block `-w`; this proves the selected workflow's name is still validated even under `-w`. *(Spec 10.8, 5.3)*
- **T-INST-60n**: `--workflow` long form exercises the same selective-validation semantics as `-w`. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` is valid (contains `index.sh`) and `broken/` has an invalid script name (e.g., `broken/-bad.sh`). `.loopx/` initially empty. `loopx install --workflow ralph <source>` succeeds and `.loopx/ralph/` is created — the invalid script name in `broken/` is not evaluated. This mirrors T-INST-60a but uses the `--workflow` long form to verify that selective validation is not inadvertently tied to the short `-w` parsing path. *(Spec 10.8, 10.4, 4.2)*
- **T-INST-60o**: With `-w`, selecting a subdirectory that does not qualify as a workflow is an error. Multi-workflow source contains `good/index.sh` and `legacy/package.json` (with `{ "main": "src/run.js" }`) plus `legacy/src/run.js`, but no top-level script files inside `legacy/`. `loopx install -w legacy <source>` → exits with code 1 (named workflow does not exist in source). `legacy/` is not a workflow because it has no top-level supported-extension files — the `-w` flag does not cause loopx to relax workflow detection rules. This is the selective-install counterpart to T-INST-55e (which covers the same legacy subdirectory being silently skipped during full multi-workflow install). *(Spec 10.8, 10.3)*
- **T-INST-60q**: With `-w`, the selected workflow's own `package.json` with invalid JSON emits a single non-fatal warning and the install still succeeds. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` contains `index.sh` plus a `package.json` with invalid JSON content (e.g., `{broken`), and `other/` is valid (contains `index.sh`, no `package.json`). `loopx install -w ralph <source>` → exit code 0. Assert: (a) stderr contains exactly one `package.json` parse-failure warning for `ralph`, (b) `.loopx/ralph/` is installed and contains both `index.sh` and the broken `package.json` (file is preserved as-is), and (c) `.loopx/other/` does not exist. T-INST-75 proves invalid JSON emits a non-fatal warning on the generic install path; T-INST-60f proves the warning is suppressed for unselected siblings under `-w`; this test pins down that the selected workflow under `-w` still receives the normal non-fatal warning behavior — the `-w` code path does not accidentally promote the warning to a fatal error or suppress it entirely for the selected workflow. *(Spec 10.8, 10.6, 3.2)*
- **T-INST-60r**: With `-w`, the selected workflow's own unreadable `package.json` emits a single non-fatal warning and the install still succeeds. Same structure as T-INST-60q, but `ralph/package.json` is set to mode 000 (unreadable) instead of containing invalid JSON. **Source must be a tarball** (or another non-git source path), since Git does not reliably preserve mode 000 file permissions across clone. `loopx install -w ralph <tarball-url>` → exit code 0. Assert: (a) stderr contains exactly one `package.json` read-failure warning for `ralph`, (b) `.loopx/ralph/` is installed and contains `index.sh` and the unreadable `package.json`, and (c) `.loopx/other/` does not exist. This is the unreadable-file counterpart to T-INST-60q (invalid JSON) — T-INST-74 covers the generic path; this test covers the selective `-w` path. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 10.8, 10.6, 3.2)*
- **T-INST-60s**: With `-w`, the selected workflow's own `package.json` with an invalid semver range for `loopx` emits a single non-fatal warning and the install still succeeds. Same structure as T-INST-60q, but `ralph/package.json` contains valid JSON with an invalid semver range (e.g., `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }`) instead of invalid JSON. `loopx install -w ralph <source>` → exit code 0. Assert: (a) stderr contains exactly one invalid-semver warning for `ralph`, (b) `.loopx/ralph/` is installed and contains `index.sh` and the `package.json` with its original (invalid) range preserved, and (c) `.loopx/other/` does not exist. This is the invalid-semver counterpart to T-INST-60q (invalid JSON) and T-INST-60r (unreadable) — T-INST-76 covers the generic path; this test covers the selective `-w` path. Together, T-INST-60q/60r/60s prove the `-w` code path preserves the non-fatal-warning behavior across all three `package.json` failure branches for the selected workflow. *(Spec 10.8, 10.6, 3.2)*

#### Install-time Validation

- **T-INST-61**: Workflow with invalid script name (e.g., `-bad.sh`) → install fails. *(Spec 10.4)*
- **T-INST-62**: Workflow with same-base-name collision (e.g., `check.sh` and `check.ts`) → install fails. *(Spec 10.4)*
- **T-INST-62a**: Workflow source with both `index.sh` and `index.ts` → install fails. This is the `index`-specific variant of T-INST-62 — a buggy installer could special-case `index` and still pass the generic same-base-name collision test (T-INST-62). *(Spec 10.4, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-63**: Derived workflow name must match name restriction rules. Invalid name → install fails. *(Spec 10.4)*
- **T-INST-63a**: Digit-start workflow name is valid at install time. Single-workflow source whose derived name starts with a digit (e.g., repo named `3checks` containing `check.sh`). `loopx install <source>` succeeds and installs to `.loopx/3checks/`. This covers the install-time workflow-name validation path separately from runtime discovery (T-DISC-26a/26b), since install has its own name-validation code path. *(Spec 10.4, 5.3)*
- **T-INST-63b**: Install rejects a workflow name containing `:`. Source whose derived workflow name includes a colon (e.g., a tarball archive named `my:workflow.tar.gz` containing root-level `index.sh`). `loopx install <source>` → exits with code 1. The `:` is the reserved target delimiter and is explicitly disallowed in names. This mirrors runtime discovery coverage (T-DISC-32) at the install-time validation code path. *(Spec 10.4, 5.3)*
- **T-INST-63c**: Install rejects a script base name containing `:`. Single-workflow source containing a script file with `:` in its base name (e.g., `check:ready.sh` alongside a valid `index.sh`). `loopx install <source>` → exits with code 1. This mirrors runtime discovery coverage (T-DISC-31) at the install-time validation code path. *(Spec 10.4, 5.3)*
- **T-INST-63d**: Numeric script names are valid at install time. Single-workflow source containing `index.sh`, `1start.sh`, and `42.sh`. `loopx install <source>` succeeds. Assert `.loopx/<repo-name>/` contains all three scripts. This is the install-time positive counterpart to T-DISC-30a/30b (digit-start and all-digit script names valid at runtime discovery) — runtime naming allows these, but install-time script-name validation is only covered explicitly with negative cases (T-INST-61, T-INST-63c) without a symmetric positive case for numeric names. *(Spec 10.4, 5.3)*
- **T-INST-63e**: Install rejects a multi-workflow subdirectory name containing `:`. Multi-workflow source whose source root (after any wrapper-directory stripping) contains a subdirectory named with `:` (e.g., `foo:bar/index.sh`) alongside a valid sibling workflow (e.g., `other/index.sh`) and no root-level script files. `loopx install <source>` → exits with code 1 with a name-restriction error identifying the offending subdirectory name. Per the install atomicity rules (Spec 10.7), no workflows are written — assert `.loopx/foo:bar/` does not exist AND `.loopx/other/` does not exist. T-INST-63b covers the single-workflow tarball archive-name derivation path (archive name `my:workflow.tar.gz`); this test exercises the **second** install-time workflow name source — multi-workflow subdirectory-name derivation — ensuring ADR-0003's reserved-delimiter `:` rule fires on both derivation paths. A buggy implementation could reject `:` only in the archive-name path and silently install (or skip) a `:`-named subdirectory in the multi-workflow path. *(Spec 10.4, 10.3, 5.3, 10.7)*
- **T-INST-64**: Missing `index` script is allowed at install time for single-workflow sources. A single-workflow source whose root contains `check.sh` but no `index.*` file. `loopx install <source>` succeeds. Assert the installed workflow is present under `.loopx/<repo-name>/` and contains `check.sh`. This explicitly covers the single-workflow classification path introduced by ADR-0003 — root-level script files make the source single-workflow, and missing `index` is still allowed. A bug could exist where a multi-workflow subdirectory can omit `index` but a single-workflow source incorrectly requires it. *(Spec 10.4, 10.3)*
- **T-INST-64b**: Missing `index` script is allowed at install time for multi-workflow sources. Multi-workflow source with `tools/check.sh` (no `tools/index.*`) and `other/index.sh` (to force multi-workflow classification). `loopx install <source>` succeeds. Assert both `.loopx/tools/` and `.loopx/other/` are installed, and `.loopx/tools/` contains `check.sh`. This complements the single-workflow path (T-INST-64) — a bug could allow missing index in single-workflow sources but incorrectly require it in multi-workflow subdirectories. *(Spec 10.4, 10.3)*
- **T-INST-64c**: Missing `index` script is allowed at install time for multi-workflow sources with `-w` scoping. Same source as T-INST-64b. `loopx install -w tools <source>` succeeds. Assert `.loopx/tools/` is installed and contains `check.sh`, and `.loopx/other/` does not exist. This covers the selective-install path for a workflow without an index script. *(Spec 10.4, 10.8)*
- **T-INST-64a**: Install-time validation is non-recursive within a workflow. Single-workflow source has a top-level `index.ts` plus a nested `lib/` subdirectory containing `-bad.ts` (invalid script name) and both `check.sh` and `check.ts` (same-base-name collision). Install succeeds because nested files within a workflow are not discovered or validated as scripts — only top-level files are checked. Assert exit code 0 and that `.loopx/<repo-name>/lib/-bad.ts`, `.loopx/<repo-name>/lib/check.sh`, and `.loopx/<repo-name>/lib/check.ts` are all present in the installed workflow (copied as workflow content, not rejected as invalid scripts). *(Spec 10.4, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-64d**: Install-time validation is non-recursive within workflows in a multi-workflow source. Multi-workflow source with two workflows: `ralph/index.sh` plus `ralph/lib/-bad.ts` (invalid script name) and `ralph/lib/check.sh` + `ralph/lib/check.ts` (same-base-name collision), and `other/index.sh` (a second workflow to force multi-workflow classification). Install succeeds because nested files within a workflow are not discovered or validated as scripts — only top-level files are checked. Assert exit code 0 and that `.loopx/ralph/lib/-bad.ts`, `.loopx/ralph/lib/check.sh`, and `.loopx/ralph/lib/check.ts` are all present in the installed workflow (copied as workflow content, not rejected as invalid scripts). This is the multi-workflow counterpart to T-INST-64a (which covers the single-workflow path). *(Spec 10.4, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-52b**: Multi-workflow source with `ralph/index.sh`, `ralph/eslint.config.js`, and `other/index.sh` → install fails because every top-level file with a supported extension inside a workflow directory is a discovered script, and `eslint.config` violates the script name restriction `[a-zA-Z0-9_][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*` (the dot is not allowed). Assert exit code 1 and that the error references the invalid script name. This is the install-time mirror of T-DISC-15a / T-DISC-15b, which test the same "no opt-out" rule at runtime discovery — a buggy installer could special-case config/helper-style files during workflow-directory scanning and still pass the current suite. *(Spec 2.1, 5.3, 10.4)*

#### Collision Handling

- **T-INST-65**: Path does not exist → workflow installed without collision check. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-66**: Path exists and is a workflow by structure → install refused with error. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-67**: Path exists and is a workflow by structure, with `-y` → existing workflow replaced. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-67a**: Path exists and is a workflow by structure but would fail runtime validation, with `-y` → existing workflow replaced. Set up `.loopx/foo/` containing a script with an invalid name (`-bad.sh`) and a same-base-name collision (`check.sh` + `check.ts`). `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a valid workflow named `foo`. Assert the existing invalid workflow is replaced successfully. The collision structural check requires only that the destination path is a directory with at least one top-level file with a supported script extension — it does not perform full runtime validation. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-68**: Path exists but is NOT a workflow by structure (e.g., directory with no script files, or a non-directory entry) → install refused with error, even with `-y`. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-69**: `-y` must not replace non-workflow entries. A plain file at `.loopx/<name>` is refused even with `-y`. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-70**: Symlinked workflow collision: structural check follows the symlink target. `.loopx/foo` is a symlink pointing to a directory that contains at least one top-level file with a supported script extension. `loopx install <source>` where the source contains a workflow named `foo` → install refused with collision error. The structural check followed the symlink and found a workflow at the target. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-70b**: Symlinked workflow with `-y`: removes the symlink itself, not the target directory. `.loopx/foo` is a symlink pointing to a directory that qualifies as a workflow (contains a top-level script file). `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a workflow named `foo` → install succeeds. Assert: (a) `.loopx/foo` is now a regular directory (not a symlink) containing the new workflow content, and (b) the original symlink target directory still exists and is unmodified. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-70a**: Symlink-to-non-workflow collision refusal. `.loopx/foo` is a symlink whose target is a directory with no top-level script files (e.g., the target contains only `lib/helper.ts` nested in a subdirectory). `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a workflow named `foo` → install refuses with an error, even with `-y`. The structural check follows the symlink, finds the target is not a workflow (no top-level script files), and treats it as a non-workflow destination path. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-70c**: Symlink-to-file collision refusal. `.loopx/foo` is a symlink whose target is a regular file (not a directory). `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a workflow named `foo` → install refuses with an error, even with `-y`. A symlink to a file is a non-directory filesystem entry — it cannot be a workflow by structure (workflows are directories containing script files), so `-y` must not replace it. This completes the symlink/non-directory branch: T-INST-70/70b cover symlink-to-workflow-directory, T-INST-70a covers symlink-to-non-workflow-directory, and this test covers symlink-to-file. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-70d**: Symlink-to-structurally-valid-but-full-validation-invalid workflow is replaceable with `-y`. Create a directory outside `.loopx/` (e.g., `/tmp/invalid-workflow/`) that is structurally a workflow (contains at least one top-level file with a supported script extension, e.g., `index.sh`) but would fail full runtime validation — it contains a same-base-name collision (`check.sh` and `check.ts`) and an invalid script name (`-bad.sh`). Then symlink `.loopx/foo → /tmp/invalid-workflow/`. Run `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a valid workflow named `foo`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) `.loopx/foo` is now a regular directory (symlink replaced) containing the new workflow content, and (c) the original symlink target directory `/tmp/invalid-workflow/` still exists and is unmodified (symlink itself was removed, not the target). T-INST-67a proves this "local structural check only" rule for regular-directory replacements, and T-INST-70b proves symlink-to-valid-workflow replaces; this test completes the coverage by proving the rule holds on the symlink path even when the target would fail full validation. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-71**: `-y` replaceability check is local to `.loopx/<workflow-name>` — broken siblings elsewhere under `.loopx/` do not affect collision evaluation. Set up: `.loopx/foo/` exists as a replaceable workflow (contains at least one top-level file with a supported script extension), and an unrelated sibling `.loopx/broken/` exists as a non-workflow directory (e.g., contains only a `README.md` and no script files). `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a valid workflow named `foo`. Assert: install succeeds and `.loopx/foo/` is replaced with the new workflow content. The structural check inspects only the target path `.loopx/foo/`, not the entire `.loopx/` tree — the broken sibling is irrelevant. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-71a**: `-y` replaceability check is local to `.loopx/<workflow-name>` — invalid sibling *workflows* elsewhere under `.loopx/` do not affect collision evaluation. Set up: `.loopx/foo/` exists as a replaceable workflow (contains `index.sh`), and `.loopx/broken/` exists as a workflow that would fail runtime validation (e.g., contains `check.sh` and `check.ts` — same-base-name collision, or `-bad.sh` — invalid script name). `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a valid workflow named `foo`. Assert: install succeeds and `.loopx/foo/` is replaced with the new workflow content. This strengthens T-INST-71 (which uses a non-workflow sibling) to prove that even invalid workflows elsewhere under `.loopx/` are ignored during collision evaluation — the install mechanism inspects only the target path. *(Spec 10.5)*
- **T-INST-97**: Installing workflow `foo` succeeds when a non-workflow file `.loopx/foo.sh` exists. The collision check targets `.loopx/foo/` (directory), not `.loopx/foo.sh` (file) — they are different filesystem paths, so there is no collision. *(Spec 10.5)*

#### Version Checking on Install

- **T-INST-72**: Workflow declares a loopx version range not satisfied by running version → install refused with error. *(Spec 10.6)*
- **T-INST-73**: With `-y`, version mismatch is overridden and install proceeds. Version declaration preserved. *(Spec 10.6)*
- **T-INST-72a**: Install-time version check for a no-index workflow with version mismatch. Single-workflow source containing `check.sh` (no `index` script) and a `package.json` declaring a loopx range not satisfied by the running version. `loopx install <source>` → exits with code 1 (version mismatch error). This combines the no-index install path (T-INST-64) with version checking (T-INST-72) — both covered separately, but the combination tests that the version check still runs for workflows that lack a default entry point. *(Spec 10.6, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-73a**: Same setup as T-INST-72a with `-y`. `loopx install -y <source>` → exits 0. Assert the workflow is installed with `check.sh` and `package.json` version declaration preserved. This is the `-y` override counterpart to T-INST-72a. *(Spec 10.6, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-74**: Workflow `package.json` unreadable → warning, install proceeds (no version validation). **Source must be a tarball** (or another non-git source path), since Git does not reliably preserve mode 000 file permissions across clone. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 10.6, 3.2)*
- **T-INST-74a**: Install-time `package.json` unreadable warning for a no-index workflow. Single-workflow source containing `check.sh` (no `index.*` script) and a `package.json` file with mode 000 (unreadable). **Source must be a tarball** (or another non-git source path). Run `loopx install <tarball-url>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) stderr contains an unreadable-file warning for the workflow, and (c) the workflow is installed at `.loopx/<name>/` and contains `check.sh` and the unreadable `package.json`. This combines the no-index install path (T-INST-64) with the unreadable-`package.json` warning path (T-INST-74) — both covered separately, but the combination tests that the `package.json` failure warning still fires for workflows without a default entry point. A buggy implementation could scope the `package.json` read/warn code to the same guard that triggers version comparison, and silently skip both on no-index workflows. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 10.6, 3.2, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-75**: Workflow `package.json` invalid JSON → warning, install proceeds. *(Spec 10.6, 3.2)*
- **T-INST-75a**: Install-time `package.json` invalid-JSON warning for a no-index workflow. Single-workflow source containing `check.sh` (no `index.*` script) and a `package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Run `loopx install <source>`.
