Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) stderr contains an invalid-JSON warning for the workflow, and (c) the workflow is installed at `.loopx/<name>/` and contains `check.sh` and the broken `package.json` (file is preserved as-is). This is the invalid-JSON counterpart to T-INST-74a (unreadable), combining the no-index install path (T-INST-64) with the invalid-JSON warning path (T-INST-75). *(Spec 10.6, 3.2, 10.4)*
- **T-INST-76**: Workflow `package.json` invalid semver range → warning, install proceeds. *(Spec 10.6, 3.2)*
- **T-INST-76a**: Install-time `package.json` invalid-semver-range warning for a no-index workflow. Single-workflow source containing `check.sh` (no `index.*` script) and a `package.json` containing valid JSON with an invalid semver range for `loopx` (e.g., `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }`). Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) stderr contains an invalid-semver warning for the workflow, and (c) the workflow is installed at `.loopx/<name>/` and contains `check.sh` and the `package.json` with its original (invalid) range preserved. This is the invalid-semver counterpart to T-INST-74a (unreadable) and T-INST-75a (invalid JSON), combining the no-index install path (T-INST-64) with the invalid-semver warning path (T-INST-76). Together T-INST-74a/75a/76a close the install-time `package.json` failure-warning coverage gap for no-index workflows across all three non-blocking failure branches — complementing T-INST-72a/73a which cover the blocking version-mismatch branch on the same path. *(Spec 10.6, 3.2, 10.4)*

#### Install Atomicity

- **T-INST-77**: Multi-workflow install: all workflows pass preflight → all installed. *(Spec 10.7)*
- **T-INST-78**: Multi-workflow install: one workflow fails preflight (e.g., name collision at destination) → entire install fails, no workflows written. Assert `.loopx/` unchanged. *(Spec 10.7)*
- **T-INST-79**: Staging failure leaves `.loopx/` unchanged. Multi-workflow source (**must be a tarball** or another non-git source path — Git does not reliably preserve mode 000 file permissions across clone) where `ralph/` is valid (contains `index.sh`) and `broken/` contains a script file (`index.sh`) plus a non-script file with permissions set to `000` (unreadable). `loopx install <tarball-url>` → staging fails when trying to copy the unreadable file in `broken/`. Assert: exit code 1, `.loopx/` is unchanged (neither `ralph/` nor `broken/` was written), and the error message identifies the failing workflow and the underlying cause. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 10.7)*
- **T-INST-80**: Multi-workflow install with `-y` succeeds despite destination collisions and version mismatches. Multi-workflow source where `ralph/` (with `index.sh`) has a destination collision (`.loopx/ralph/` already exists as a workflow with different content) and `other/` (with `index.sh` and a `package.json` declaring a loopx version range not satisfied by the running version) has a version mismatch. `loopx install -y <source>` → exits 0. Assert: `.loopx/ralph/` contains the new content from the source (replaced), and `.loopx/other/` is installed with its `package.json` version declaration preserved. *(Spec 10.7)*
- **T-INST-80a**: Multi-workflow install with multiple preflight failures across different workflows (e.g., workflow A has a name collision at destination, workflow B has an invalid script name, workflow C declares a loopx version range not satisfied by the running version) → single aggregated error report listing all failures across all workflows, including the version mismatch. No workflows written. *(Spec 10.7)*
- **T-INST-80b**: `-y` replacement preserves the existing workflow when staging fails. Multi-workflow source (**must be a tarball** or another non-git source path — Git does not reliably preserve mode 000 file permissions across clone) where `ralph/` is valid (has `index.sh`) and `other/` contains a script file (`index.sh`) plus a non-script file with permissions set to `000` (unreadable). `.loopx/ralph/` already exists as a workflow with known content. `loopx install -y <tarball-url>` → staging fails when trying to copy the unreadable file in `other/`. Assert: exit code 1, the existing `.loopx/ralph/` is still intact with its original content (not removed or modified — the commit phase never ran). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 10.7)*
- **T-INST-80c**: Commit-phase failure reports which workflows were and were not committed. Multi-workflow source with three workflows: `alpha/`, `beta/`, `gamma/` (each with `index.sh`). Set `NODE_ENV=test` and `LOOPX_TEST_INSTALL_FAULT=commit-fail-after:1` in the process environment to simulate a rename failure after committing one workflow (see section 1.4, install fault injection seam — the seam is only honored when `NODE_ENV=test`). Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) error output identifies which workflow(s) were successfully committed and which were not, and (c) exactly one workflow directory exists in `.loopx/`. *(Spec 10.7)*
- **T-INST-80d**: Install-time `package.json` warning behavior is "once per affected workflow" and is not accidentally deduplicated by runtime-style first-entry logic. Install two workflows (**from a tarball source** or another non-git source path — Git does not reliably preserve mode 000 file permissions across clone), each with an unreadable `package.json` → each workflow's warning appears independently (two warnings, not one). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-80e**: Install-time `package.json` warning behavior for invalid semver ranges is "once per affected workflow." Install two workflows, each with a valid `package.json` containing an invalid semver range for `loopx` (e.g., `"loopx": "not-a-range"`) → each workflow's warning appears independently (two warnings, not one). Install proceeds for both workflows (invalid semver skips version check, does not block install). This is the invalid-semver counterpart to T-INST-80d (unreadable files). *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-80f**: Install-time `package.json` warning behavior for invalid JSON is "once per affected workflow." Install two workflows, each with a `package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`) → each workflow's warning appears independently (two warnings, not one). Install proceeds for both workflows (invalid JSON skips version check, does not block install). This is the invalid-JSON counterpart to T-INST-80d (unreadable files) and T-INST-80e (invalid semver). *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-INST-80g**: `-y` does not override a zero-workflow source. `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains no root-level script files and no subdirectories that qualify as workflows → error, exit code 1, regardless of `-y`. *(Spec 10.3, 10.7)*
- **T-INST-80h**: `-y` does not override invalid workflow or script names. `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a workflow with an invalid script name (e.g., `-bad.sh`) → error, exit code 1, regardless of `-y`. *(Spec 10.4, 10.7)*
- **T-INST-80i**: `-y` does not override same-base-name collisions within a workflow. `loopx install -y <source>` where the source contains a workflow with `check.sh` and `check.ts` (same base name, different extensions) → error, exit code 1, regardless of `-y`. *(Spec 10.4, 10.7)*
- **T-INST-80j**: `-y` does not override an invalid workflow name. `loopx install -y <source>` where the derived workflow name violates `[a-zA-Z0-9_][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*` (e.g., source directory named `bad.name`) → error, exit code 1, regardless of `-y`. *(Spec 10.4, 10.7)*

#### Tarball Install

- **T-INST-81**: Multi-workflow tarball install with exact name derivation. Create a `.tar.gz` whose source root (after any wrapper-directory stripping) contains subdirectories `ralph/` (with `index.sh`) and `other/` (with `index.sh`). Install the tarball. Assert installed paths are exactly `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/`, with the expected scripts present. Workflow names are derived from the source-root subdirectory names. *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-82**: Wrapper-directory stripping for multi-workflow tarball. Create a `.tar.gz` with a single top-level directory `pkg/` containing `pkg/ralph/index.sh` and `pkg/other/index.sh`. After extraction, `pkg/` is stripped and the source root becomes the contents of `pkg/`. Assert installed paths are `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/` (not `.loopx/pkg/`). *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-83**: No wrapper-directory stripping for multi-entry tarball. Create a `.tar.gz` with multiple top-level entries `ralph/index.sh` and `other/index.sh` (no single wrapper directory). After extraction, the entries are used directly as the source root. Assert installed paths are `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/`. *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-83a**: Multi-workflow tarball self-containment. Create a `.tar.gz` whose source root (after any wrapper-directory stripping) contains two workflow subdirectories `ralph/` (with `index.sh`) and `other/` (with `index.sh`), plus root-level support files `README.md` and `LICENSE`, a root-level support directory `docs/` (containing `docs/guide.md`), and a non-workflow directory `shared/` (containing only `shared/config.json` — no top-level script files). `loopx install <tarball-url>` → exit code 0. Assert: (a) `.loopx/ralph/` and `.loopx/other/` are installed and contain their respective scripts, (b) `.loopx/README.md`, `.loopx/LICENSE`, `.loopx/docs/`, and `.loopx/shared/` do NOT exist — no root support files or directories are copied. Per SPEC 10.2, classification after extraction is source-type-agnostic, so the multi-workflow self-containment rules that apply to git sources (T-INST-54 covers root support files, T-INST-54c covers root support directories, T-INST-55 covers non-workflow subdirectories skipped) must apply equally to tarball sources. Existing tarball coverage (T-INST-81–83) pins down wrapper stripping and workflow-name derivation but does not assert self-containment; this test closes that gap. *(Spec 10.2, 10.3)*
- **T-INST-84**: `.tgz` extension handled identically. *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-85**: Single-workflow tarball: workflow name derived from archive name (URL last segment minus `.tar.gz`/`.tgz`, query/fragment stripped). *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-86**: Tarball URL with query string → query stripped from archive-name derivation. *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-86a**: Tarball URL with fragment → fragment stripped from archive-name derivation. `loopx install http://localhost:PORT/pkg.tar.gz#v1` installs a single-workflow source. Assert the installed workflow is named `pkg` (fragment `#v1` stripped before deriving the archive name). *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-85a**: Single-workflow tarball with wrapper-directory stripping. Create a `.tar.gz` named `my-agent.tar.gz` with a single top-level wrapper directory (e.g., `wrapper/`) containing a single-workflow source at its root (e.g., `wrapper/index.sh`, `wrapper/check.sh` — root-level script files). Install the tarball. Assert: (a) the wrapper directory is stripped before classification (the source is classified as single-workflow from the unwrapped contents), (b) the installed workflow name is `my-agent` (derived from the archive name, not the wrapper directory name `wrapper`), and (c) the installed workflow at `.loopx/my-agent/` contains the expected scripts. This combines wrapper-directory stripping (tested for multi-workflow in T-INST-82) with single-workflow archive-name derivation (tested without wrapping in T-INST-85). *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-85b**: Single-workflow tarball with root-level script files plus subdirectories containing supported-extension files. Create a `.tar.gz` named `my-agent.tar.gz` whose source root (after any wrapper-directory stripping) contains root-level script files (e.g., `index.sh`, `check.sh`) plus subdirectories with supported-extension files (e.g., `lib/helpers.ts`, `src/utils.js`) and non-script root-level files (`package.json`, `README.md`). Install the tarball. Assert: (a) the source is classified as single-workflow (root-level script files take precedence unconditionally), (b) the installed workflow name is `my-agent` (derived from the archive name), (c) all root-level files and subdirectories are copied into `.loopx/my-agent/` (including `lib/`, `src/`, `package.json`, `README.md`), and (d) no sibling workflows are created from the subdirectories. This is the tarball counterpart to the git-source root-level-script precedence tests (T-INST-50–52). *(Spec 10.2, 10.3)*

#### Git Install

- **T-INST-87**: Shallow clone (`--depth 1`). Use `withFakeGit({ logFile })` so every `git` invocation loopx makes is recorded to a log file (the shim wraps the real `git` and is transparent to loopx's cloning). Run `loopx install <git-source>` against a local bare repo. Assert the log contains exactly one `git clone` invocation whose argv includes `--depth` `1` (or equivalently `--depth=1`) before the source URL. Per SPEC 10.2 "The repository is cloned with `--depth 1` (shallow clone) into a temporary location." A post-clone `git log` assertion on the installed workflow is not viable (staged workflows have no `.git/` after commit), so the `--depth 1` flag is the correct black-box-visible surface. *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-88**: Single-workflow git repo: name derived from repo URL minus `.git`. *(Spec 10.2)*
- **T-INST-89**: Multi-workflow git repo: workflow names derived from subdirectory names. *(Spec 10.2)*

#### Common Rules

- **T-INST-90**: `.loopx/` directory created if it doesn't exist. *(Spec 10)*
- **T-INST-92**: HTTP 404 during tarball download → error, exit code 1, no partial directory. *(Spec 10.9)*
- **T-INST-93**: Git clone failure (non-existent repo) → error, exit code 1, no partial directory. *(Spec 10.9)*
- **T-INST-94**: Tarball extraction failure (corrupt archive) → error, exit code 1, no partial directory. *(Spec 10.9)*
- **T-INST-95**: Empty tarball (valid `.tar.gz` with no entries) → error, exit code 1. *(Spec 10.9)*
- **T-INST-96**: Successful single-workflow git install → installed workflow is runnable via `loopx run <name>`. *(Spec 10)*
- **T-INST-97a**: Pre-commit failure leaves `.loopx/` unchanged. Per Spec 10.7 / 10.9's stage-then-commit model, any pre-commit install failure (source download, extraction, preflight, staging — enumerated in Spec 10.9's "Install failure cleanup" bullet) leaves `.loopx/` itself unchanged; no destination-path cleanup is required. Create a fixture where the single-workflow source fails during staging (e.g., tarball with an unreadable file under `process.getuid() !== 0`, mode 000). Before running install, snapshot the state of `.loopx/` (either empty or containing unrelated workflows). Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) `.loopx/` is byte-identical to the pre-install snapshot (no new workflow directory under `.loopx/<name>/`, and any pre-existing sibling workflows unmodified), and (c) stderr identifies the failing workflow and the underlying cause. This rewrites the earlier cleanup-of-partial-workflow-directory assertion to match SPEC 10.9 post-ADR-0004: under stage-then-commit, the staging directory is the only thing that could be partial, and it is removed; `.loopx/` itself never receives a partial write. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 10.7, 10.9)*
- **T-INST-97a2**: Pre-commit failure (preflight) leaves `.loopx/` unchanged. Create a single-workflow source whose workflow name violates name restrictions. Snapshot `.loopx/`, run install, assert exit 1 and `.loopx/` unchanged. This is the preflight-fails-at-single-workflow variant of T-INST-97a (which covers the staging failure); together they pin down that neither pre-commit phase leaves `.loopx/` in a partial state for single-workflow sources. *(Spec 10.7, 10.9)*
- **T-INST-97b**: Successful install does not create `.loopx/package.json`. Run a successful single-workflow git install into a project. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the workflow is installed at `.loopx/<name>/`, and (c) `.loopx/package.json` does not exist. There is no `.loopx/`-level manifest — version authority lives only in the project root `package.json` and each workflow's own `package.json`. *(Spec 10.6)*

#### Auto-install of Workflow Dependencies (Spec 10.10)

All tests in this block use `withFakeNpm` (section 2.3) to control `npm`'s behavior deterministically. The helper records every invocation to a log file so tests can assert which workflows `npm install` was invoked for, in what order, and with what environment. Without the fake shim, these tests would be flaky (depend on real npm + registry) or impossible (`spawnFailure`, signal, non-zero exit cannot be driven by real npm reliably).

##### Auto-install Trigger

- **T-INST-110**: Default post-commit `npm install` runs once per committed workflow with top-level `package.json`. Install a multi-workflow source where `alpha/` has a top-level `package.json` (and `alpha/index.sh`) and `beta/` has a top-level `package.json` (and `beta/index.sh`). Use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 0, logFile })`. Run `loopx install <source>` (no `--no-install`). Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the shim log records exactly two invocations, (c) one invocation's cwd is `.loopx/alpha/` and the other is `.loopx/beta/`, (d) each invocation's argv is **exactly** `["install"]` — no additional flags (`--production`, `--ignore-scripts`, `--omit=dev`, etc.) are passed, per SPEC 10.10 "does not pass `--production` / `--omit=dev` / `--ignore-scripts` / any other flags", and (e) invocations occur sequentially in commit order. *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-110a**: `npm install` is skipped silently for workflows without a top-level `package.json`. Multi-workflow source where `alpha/` has `alpha/index.sh` + `alpha/package.json`, and `beta/` has only `beta/index.sh` (no `package.json`). Use `withFakeNpm`. Run install. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the shim log records exactly one invocation — for `alpha/`, (c) no warning about `beta/` missing a `package.json` — the skip is silent (Spec 10.10 "Workflows without a top-level `package.json` are skipped silently"). *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-110c**: Presence of `package.json` alone triggers auto-install — dependency content is not inspected. Single-workflow source with `index.sh` and a minimal `package.json` containing exactly `{ "name": "minimal-workflow", "version": "1.0.0" }` (no `dependencies`, no `devDependencies`, no `scripts`, no `loopx` field). Use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 0, logFile })`. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the fake-npm shim log records exactly one invocation for the workflow (argv `["install"]`, cwd = `.loopx/<name>/`), (c) a synthesized `.gitignore` was created in the workflow directory. Per SPEC 10.10 "The trigger is the presence of a top-level `package.json`; whether that file declares any dependencies is not inspected." A buggy implementation that skipped auto-install when the `package.json` lists zero dependencies would fail this test. *(Spec 10.10, 2.1)*
- **T-INST-110b**: `-w <name>` scopes auto-install to the selected workflow. Same source as T-INST-110 (both `alpha/` and `beta/` have `package.json`). Run `loopx install -w alpha <source>`. Assert shim log records exactly one invocation, for `alpha/`, and none for `beta/`. Extends T-INST-57 (selective installation) to the auto-install pass. *(Spec 10.10, 10.8)*

##### `--no-install` Opt-Out

- **T-INST-111**: `--no-install` suppresses both `npm install` and `.gitignore` synthesis. Single-workflow source with top-level `package.json` but no `.gitignore`. Use `withFakeNpm` to observe any invocation. Run `loopx install --no-install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the shim log is empty (no `npm` invocations), (c) `.loopx/<name>/.gitignore` was **not** created, (d) other install-time behavior succeeded (workflow files present at `.loopx/<name>/`). Per Spec 10.10 "`--no-install` ... does not suppress any other install-time behavior; only the `npm install` step and the `.gitignore` safeguard ... are skipped." *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-111a**: `--no-install` on a workflow with a pre-existing `.gitignore` leaves that file unchanged. Source's `.gitignore` contains `dist/\n`. Use `withFakeNpm`. Run `loopx install --no-install <source>`. Assert: (a) no `npm` invocation, (b) the installed `.loopx/<name>/.gitignore` has the same content as the source (`dist/\n`) — loopx did not touch it. *(Spec 10.10)*

##### `.gitignore` Safeguard

- **T-INST-112**: Missing `.gitignore` is created with exactly one line: `node_modules`. Single-workflow source with `package.json` but no `.gitignore`. Use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 0 })`. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit 0, (b) `.loopx/<name>/.gitignore` exists, (c) its content is exactly `node_modules` (optionally with a single trailing newline — implementation-defined), (d) the `npm install` shim was invoked (order: safeguard before spawn). *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-112a**: Existing `.gitignore` is left unchanged (no append, no rewrite, no warning). Source's `.gitignore` contains `dist/\n# my custom comment\n`. Use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 0 })`. Run install. Assert: (a) exit 0, (b) `.loopx/<name>/.gitignore` content is byte-identical to the source's (`dist/\n# my custom comment\n`) — no `node_modules` line appended, (c) no warning on stderr about `node_modules` not being listed, (d) `npm install` still ran. *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-112b**: `.gitignore` synthesis is skipped when the workflow has no top-level `package.json`. Source has `index.sh` but no `package.json`. Run install. Assert `.loopx/<name>/.gitignore` was not created. `.gitignore` synthesis runs only under the same trigger as `npm install`. *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-112c**: `.gitignore` write failure skips `npm install` for that workflow and contributes to aggregate failure. Multi-workflow source where `alpha/` has a normal `package.json` (and no pre-existing `.gitignore`, so loopx must synthesize one) and `beta/` has a `package.json` (also no pre-existing `.gitignore`). Use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 0, logFile })`. Run install with `NODE_ENV=test` and `LOOPX_TEST_AUTOINSTALL_FAULT=gitignore-write-fail:beta` (the fault-injection seam from section 1.4). Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) the shim log shows an invocation for `alpha/` but **not** for `beta/` — `npm install` was skipped when the safeguard could not be established, (c) stderr contains an aggregate failure report listing `beta/` with a `.gitignore` write failure, (d) `alpha/` is not listed in the aggregate report (its safeguard and `npm install` both succeeded). Using the `LOOPX_TEST_AUTOINSTALL_FAULT` seam (rather than real filesystem permissions) keeps the test deterministic, CI-friendly, and runnable under any user (including `root`). *(Spec 10.10)*

##### Malformed `package.json`

- **T-INST-113**: Malformed `package.json` (invalid JSON) — warning once, auto-install skipped silently. Single-workflow source with `package.json` containing `{broken`. Use `withFakeNpm`. Run install. Assert: (a) exit code 0 (malformed `package.json` is non-fatal per Spec 3.2/10.6), (b) the shim log is empty (`npm install` not invoked — the skip is silent per Spec 10.10 "does not add a second warning"), (c) stderr contains exactly one `package.json` parse-failure warning for the workflow (from Spec 3.2's existing warning path, not a new auto-install warning), (d) `.loopx/<name>/.gitignore` was not created (safeguard also skipped for the malformed workflow), (e) no aggregate failure report is emitted (skipped-due-to-malformed workflow is not an auto-install failure). *(Spec 10.10, 3.2)*
- **T-INST-113a**: Malformed `package.json` (unreadable) — same as T-INST-113 but with mode 000. Single-workflow source from a **tarball** (git does not preserve mode 000). Use `withFakeNpm`. Run install. Assert: exit 0, no `npm` invocation, single unreadable-file warning, no `.gitignore` synthesis, no aggregate failure report. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 10.10, 3.2)*
- **T-INST-113b**: Malformed `package.json` (invalid semver range) — same structure as T-INST-113. Source's `package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }`. Use `withFakeNpm`. Run install. Assert: exit 0, no `npm` invocation, single invalid-semver warning, no `.gitignore` synthesis, no aggregate failure report. *(Spec 10.10, 3.2)*

##### `npm install` Failures

- **T-INST-114**: `npm install` non-zero exit — aggregate report, continue processing later workflows, final exit 1. Multi-workflow source: `alpha/`, `beta/`, `gamma/` each with `package.json`. Use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 1, logFile })` for the **second** invocation only — this requires a shim mode that returns non-zero only for a specific invocation count. Simplest implementation: the shim writes its count before exiting, and exits non-zero when its invocation matches a configured index. Alternative: use three separate path prefixes and fake-npm-shim targeting only one. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) shim log shows three invocations (for `alpha/`, `beta/`, `gamma/` in that order) — loopx proceeded past the failure to later workflows, (c) stderr contains an aggregate failure report listing exactly `beta/` as a `npm install` non-zero-exit failure, (d) `alpha/` and `gamma/` are not listed, (e) all three workflow directories are committed at `.loopx/<name>/` — the non-zero npm exit does **not** roll back committed workflow files (Spec 10.10 "Dependency-install failures do not roll back the file-level install"). *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-114a**: `npm` spawn failure — aggregate report, continue processing later workflows, final exit 1. Same three-workflow source. Use `withFakeNpm({ spawnFailure: true, logFile })` — the shim file is not created, so spawning `npm` fails with `ENOENT`. Run install. Assert: (a) exit code 1, (b) log shows zero invocations (spawn itself failed — the shim never ran), (c) stderr aggregate failure report lists all three workflows (each got its own spawn failure), (d) all three workflow directories still committed. This distinguishes spawn-failure (Spec 10.10 "`npm` is not on `PATH`") from non-zero-exit (T-INST-114). *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-114b**: `npm install` spawn failure on one workflow does not prevent `npm install` on subsequent workflows. Configure the fake-npm-shim so that spawn succeeds for `alpha/` and `gamma/` but fails only for `beta/` (e.g., via a PATH rewrite that points the shim at a broken wrapper for one specific call — or via a shim mode `spawnFailureOn: 2` implemented by recording count, then if count matches, the shim `exec`s a non-existent binary). Assert log shows invocations for `alpha/` and `gamma/` (successful spawns) but none for `beta/`, and the aggregate report lists `beta/` as spawn-failure. *(Spec 10.10)*

##### Environment Purity

- **T-INST-115**: `npm install` inherits loopx's `process.env` only — no `LOOPX_*`, no env-file injection, no `RunOptions.env`. Set loopx's inherited `MYVAR=inherited`. Create a global env file with `INJECTED_GLOBAL=yes`. Create a local env file (loaded via `-e local.env`) with `INJECTED_LOCAL=yes`. Call... wait — `RunOptions.env` applies only to the programmatic API, not CLI. For the CLI case, install doesn't have `RunOptions.env`. Instead, test the CLI path: set `MYVAR=inherited` and a global env file with `INJECTED_GLOBAL=yes`. Use `withFakeNpm({ logFile })` where the shim's log records the child's `MYVAR`, `INJECTED_GLOBAL`, and all `LOOPX_*` variables. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: the recorded child env shows (a) `MYVAR=inherited`, (b) **no** `INJECTED_GLOBAL` — the global env file was loaded for script execution, not for auto-install, (c) **no** `LOOPX_*` variables (no `LOOPX_BIN`, `LOOPX_PROJECT_ROOT`, `LOOPX_WORKFLOW`, `LOOPX_WORKFLOW_DIR`, `LOOPX_TMPDIR` in the npm child). Per Spec 10.10 "The `npm install` child inherits loopx's own `process.env` unchanged. `LOOPX_*` protocol variables, `RunOptions.env`, and env-file entries are not injected". *(Spec 10.10, 8.3)*

##### Signal During `npm install`

- **T-INST-116**: SIGINT during `npm install` forwards to child process group and loopx exits with signal code. Use `withFakeNpm({ sleepSeconds: 30, logFile })` — the shim writes PID/ready to stderr then sleeps. Use `runCLIWithSignal` to spawn `loopx install <source>`. `waitForStderr("ready")`, then send SIGINT to loopx. Assert: (a) loopx exits with code 130 (128 + SIGINT), (b) the shim's PID no longer appears in the process table (was terminated — verify via `kill -0 <pid>` returning non-zero). *(Spec 10.10, 7.3)*
- **T-INST-116a**: SIGTERM during `npm install` → exit 143, shim terminated. Same as T-INST-116 with SIGTERM. *(Spec 10.10, 7.3)*
- **T-INST-116b**: Signal during `npm install` — remaining workflows are not processed. Multi-workflow source `alpha/`, `beta/`, `gamma/`. Use `withFakeNpm({ sleepSeconds: 30 })` with a configuration where the shim sleeps only on the first invocation (`alpha/`). Send SIGINT while `alpha/`'s shim is sleeping. Assert: (a) exit 130, (b) shim log shows only one invocation (for `alpha/`) — `beta/` and `gamma/` were not reached. Per Spec 10.10 "Remaining committed workflows are not processed". *(Spec 10.10, 7.3)*
- **T-INST-116c**: SIGKILL escalation when the `npm install` child ignores SIGTERM beyond the 5-second grace period. SPEC 10.10 "Signals during `npm install`" states: "the section 7.3 grace period and SIGKILL escalation rules apply by analogy" — i.e., after loopx forwards the signal to the npm child's process group, it waits 5 seconds for the group to exit and then sends SIGKILL. T-INST-116 / T-INST-116a cover the clean-exit path (the shim sleeps passively and is terminated by the forwarded signal); this test covers the escalation path. Extend `withFakeNpm` options so the shim installs a SIGTERM trap that ignores the signal (equivalent to the `signal-trap-ignore` fixture in section 2.4), writes its PID to the marker file, writes `"ready"` to stderr, then sleeps indefinitely (e.g., `sleepSeconds: 30` combined with a `trapSignals: ["TERM", "INT"]` flag that installs `trap '' TERM INT` in the shim's Bash preamble). Run `loopx install <multi-workflow source>` via `runCLIWithSignal`. Wait for `"ready"` on stderr, record the shim PID, then send SIGTERM to loopx. Assert: (a) loopx waits approximately 5 seconds before the shim is terminated (the grace-period window — the test may allow a tolerance of 4–7 seconds to account for scheduling jitter), (b) after that window, the shim process is no longer running (verified via `kill -0 <shim-pid>` returning non-zero, indicating SIGKILL took effect since the shim was trapping/ignoring SIGTERM), (c) loopx exits with code 143 (128 + 15 for SIGTERM), and (d) the aggregate-failure-report branch from SPEC 10.10 is not triggered (the install was interrupted by a signal, not by a non-zero npm exit). This pins down that the SPEC 7.3 "5 seconds, then SIGKILL" escalation applies identically to the `npm install` child. `@flaky-retry(2)` due to the real-time 5-second wait. *(Spec 10.10, 7.3)*

##### No Rollback on Auto-install Failure

- **T-INST-117**: Auto-install failures do not remove committed workflow files. Run T-INST-114 (non-zero exit for `beta/`). After the command exits 1, assert `.loopx/alpha/`, `.loopx/beta/`, and `.loopx/gamma/` all exist on disk with their intended contents (`index.sh`, `package.json`), and any synthesized `.gitignore` files are present. The failure report does not trigger rollback — the user remediates manually. *(Spec 10.10, 10.7, 10.9)*
- **T-INST-117a**: Partial `node_modules/` state from an interrupted `npm install` is not cleaned up. Use `withFakeNpm` with a mode where the shim creates `node_modules/partial-file` before exiting non-zero. Run install. After exit 1, assert `.loopx/<name>/node_modules/partial-file` still exists — loopx did not remove it. *(Spec 10.10)*

##### Package-Manager Selection (Always `npm`)

SPEC 10.10: "`npm install` unconditionally. loopx does not inspect `bun.lockb`, `pnpm-lock.yaml`, `yarn.lock`, or a `packageManager` field to select a different manager". These tests pin down that loopx never selects a non-npm tool based on lockfile or `packageManager` signals.

All tests use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 0, logFile })` and no other shims — so if loopx attempts to spawn `bun`, `pnpm`, or `yarn`, the spawn either finds a real binary on `PATH` (which is unlikely under a test harness with scrubbed `PATH`) or fails, but in either case the `npm` shim log would show zero invocations, failing the assertion.

- **T-INST-118**: `packageManager: "pnpm@..."` field does not cause loopx to select pnpm. Single-workflow source with `package.json` containing `{ "packageManager": "pnpm@8.6.0", "dependencies": {} }` and a sibling `pnpm-lock.yaml`. Use `withFakeNpm`. Run install. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the fake-npm shim log records exactly one invocation for the workflow (cwd = `.loopx/<name>/`, argv = `["install"]`), and (c) no `pnpm` or other manager was spawned (verified via a scrubbed `PATH` that excludes any `pnpm`/`yarn`/`bun` binary — see `T-INST-GLOBAL-01`'s PATH-scrubbing pattern). Per SPEC 10.10 "loopx does not inspect ... a `packageManager` field to select a different manager". *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-118a**: `bun.lockb` does not cause loopx to select bun. Single-workflow source with `package.json` and a sibling `bun.lockb` file (a zero-byte placeholder is sufficient for presence detection). Use `withFakeNpm`. Run install. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the fake-npm shim log records exactly one invocation, and (c) no `bun` binary was spawned. *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-118b**: `yarn.lock` does not cause loopx to select yarn. Same structure with `yarn.lock` (zero-byte placeholder). Assert the fake-npm shim was invoked; `yarn` was not. *(Spec 10.10)*
- **T-INST-118c**: Multiple lockfiles and a `packageManager` field still select `npm`. Source with `package.json` containing `{ "packageManager": "yarn@3.6.1" }`, and sibling `bun.lockb`, `pnpm-lock.yaml`, and `yarn.lock` files simultaneously. Use `withFakeNpm`. Assert the fake-npm shim was invoked (exactly once, for the workflow), and no other manager was spawned. Per SPEC 10.10, none of these signals has any effect — `npm install` unconditionally. *(Spec 10.10)*

##### Auto-install Stdout / Stderr Passthrough

SPEC 10.10: "npm's stdout and stderr stream through to loopx's stdout and stderr unchanged; loopx neither buffers nor parses npm output and does not introduce a progress indicator of its own."

- **T-INST-119**: Fake npm's stdout and stderr stream through loopx unchanged. Single-workflow source with `package.json`. Use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 0, stdout: "npm-stdout-MARKER\n", stderr: "npm-stderr-MARKER\n", logFile })`. Run `loopx install <source>`. Capture loopx's stdout and stderr. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) loopx's stdout **contains** the byte sequence `npm-stdout-MARKER\n` (unchanged passthrough), (c) loopx's stderr **contains** `npm-stderr-MARKER\n`, and (d) loopx's stdout does **not** contain a loopx-generated progress line or wrapping ("Running npm install...", "Installing dependencies...", spinner glyphs, etc.) before or after the npm output — the enumerated "progress indicator" text is not present. Per SPEC 10.10 "streams through ... unchanged" and "does not introduce a progress indicator of its own". *(Spec 10.10)*

##### `-y` Replacement: Auto-install Freshness

SPEC 10.10 "Interaction with `-y`": "File-level replacement removes the existing workflow directory (including any previously installed `node_modules/` and any previously synthesized `.gitignore`) before the replacement is committed; the safeguard and `npm install` then run fresh against the replacement's `package.json` and `.gitignore` (or absence thereof)."

- **T-INST-120**: `-y` replacement removes old `node_modules/` and synthesized `.gitignore`, then auto-install runs fresh. Pre-seed `.loopx/ralph/` (before running the install command under test) with `ralph/index.sh`, `ralph/package.json`, `ralph/node_modules/old-marker` (a file whose continued presence proves stale `node_modules/` was not cleaned), and a previously synthesized `ralph/.gitignore` containing exactly `node_modules\n`. Prepare a **replacement** single-workflow source with `index.sh` and `package.json` but **no** `.gitignore` and **no** `node_modules/`. Use `withFakeNpm({ exitCode: 0, logFile })`. Run `loopx install -y <replacement-source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) `.loopx/ralph/node_modules/old-marker` does **not** exist after the command completes — the old `node_modules/` was removed as part of replacement, (c) a fresh `.loopx/ralph/.gitignore` exists containing exactly `node_modules` (optionally with a single trailing newline — implementation-defined) — the safeguard was re-synthesized fresh against the replacement (which had no `.gitignore`), (d) the fake-npm shim log records exactly one invocation for `.loopx/ralph/` — `npm install` ran fresh against the replacement, and (e) loopx's stdout/stderr do not contain a warning about the old `node_modules/` (removal is silent). *(Spec 10.10, 10.5)*
- **T-INST-120a**: `-y` replacement preserves a pre-existing `.gitignore` in the **replacement** source. Pre-seed `.loopx/ralph/` with `node_modules/old-marker` and a previously-synthesized `.gitignore` (containing `node_modules\n`) as in T-INST-120. Prepare a replacement source with `index.sh`, `package.json`, and a `.gitignore` containing `dist/\n# custom\n` (pre-existing). Use `withFakeNpm`. Run `loopx install -y <replacement-source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) old `node_modules/` is gone, (c) the installed `.loopx/ralph/.gitignore` has the replacement's content (`dist/\n# custom\n`) — the replacement's pre-existing `.gitignore` is **not** overwritten by loopx's safeguard (T-INST-112a behavior applies fresh), (d) the fake-npm shim ran once for `.loopx/ralph/`. *(Spec 10.10, 10.5)*

#### Global Install Smoke Test

- **T-INST-GLOBAL-01**: Full global install lifecycle, including workflow-side `import "loopx"` resolution. `npm pack` the built loopx package, install the resulting tarball into an isolated global prefix, and create a fixture project with a `.loopx/ralph/index.ts` script whose content is `import { output } from "loopx"; output({ stop: true });`. Run `<tempdir>/bin/loopx run ralph` (no `-n`) against the fixture project. Assert: (a) exit code 0 (the loop halted cleanly via `stop: true`, proving the import resolved and `output()` executed), and (b) the script actually ran (e.g., marker file written before the `output()` call, or infer from the clean `stop: true` exit). The fixture must exercise `import "loopx"` — just asserting "a TS workflow runs globally" is too weak for Spec 3.1 under the workflow model; this proves a global install is sufficient for workflow JS/TS scripts that import loopx helpers. The spawn environment **must not leak dev-tree binaries into the installed loopx**: PATH must be constructed to include only the isolated global prefix's `bin/` and a minimal system PATH (e.g., `/usr/bin`, `/usr/local/bin`, and whatever directory provides the Node/Bun interpreter under test), with all ancestor `node_modules/.bin` entries filtered out — passing `process.env.PATH` through unchanged is forbidden, because `npm run`/`npx` prepend the loopx repo's `./node_modules/.bin` before invoking vitest, which would silently supply `tsx`, `bun`, and any other binary the runner spawns from the dev tree and mask a missing declared dependency in the published package. The child process's cwd must likewise sit outside the loopx repo so that no ancestor-walked `node_modules/` can resolve transpilers or other runtime binaries. The test must also guard against symlink-based leakage (e.g., `npm install -g .` from a local path creating a symlink back into the dev `dist/`): install from the packed tarball, not a directory, and assert that the installed `loopx` package root is a real directory, not a symlink, before running the fixture. *(Spec 3.1, 3.3)*
- **T-INST-GLOBAL-01a**: `[Bun]` Full global install lifecycle under Bun. Same fixture, spawn-environment requirements (scrubbed PATH with no dev-tree `node_modules/.bin`, cwd outside the loopx repo, real-directory install from packed tarball), and assertions as T-INST-GLOBAL-01 (workflow `index.ts` uses `import { output } from "loopx"; output({ stop: true });`), but run via Bun. Proves global install plus workflow-side `import "loopx"` resolution both work under Bun. *(Spec 3.1, 3.3)*

### 4.11 Signal Handling

**Spec refs:** 7.3

Signal tests use the `signal-ready-then-sleep`, `signal-trap-exit`, `signal-trap-ignore`, and `spawn-grandchild` fixtures inside workflows. All signal fixtures follow the ready-protocol.

- **T-SIG-01**: Send SIGINT to loopx while a script is running. Assert loopx exits with code 130. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-02**: Send SIGTERM to loopx while a script is running. Assert exit code 143. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-03**: After SIGINT, the child script process is no longer running. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-04**: Grace period: child traps SIGTERM and exits within 2 seconds → no SIGKILL needed. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-05**: Grace period exceeded: child traps SIGTERM and hangs → SIGKILL after ~5 seconds. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-06**: Process group signal: script spawns a grandchild. Both terminated after SIGTERM. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-07**: Between-iterations signal. Assert loopx exits immediately. `@flaky-retry(3)`. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-08**: Signal identity preserved (SIGINT forwarded as SIGINT, SIGTERM as SIGTERM). *(Spec 7.3)*

#### Pre-iteration Signal-Wins Precedence

SPEC 7.3 defines a CLI-specific rule: SIGINT / SIGTERM observed by loopx's installed pre-iteration signal handler **wins** over non-signal pre-iteration failures not yet surfaced at that point. loopx cleans up any partial tmpdir and exits with `128 + signal number` regardless of which non-signal pre-iteration step (target syntax validation, `.loopx/` discovery, env-file loading, target resolution, tmpdir creation) would otherwise have failed. These tests cover the rule across the enumerated failure modes.

All tests in this block use `runCLIWithSignal` to deliver the signal during the pre-iteration window. Each test combines a non-signal pre-iteration failure (configured to fail deterministically) with a signal delivered before the failure surfaces, then asserts the signal-exit-code outcome rather than the failure-exit-code outcome. To synchronize signal delivery with the pre-iteration window, the harness relies on the **pre-iteration sentinel stderr marker** declared as a test-only seam in section 1.4: `waitForStderr(<implementation-defined sentinel>)` observes the line emitted by loopx at pre-iteration start (after signal-handler installation, before discovery / env-file loading / target resolution / tmpdir creation), then delivers the signal during the remaining pre-iteration window. Because the sentinel is a test-only seam (not a SPEC requirement — see section 1.4), these tests are tagged `@flaky-retry(3)` to tolerate environments where the sentinel is unavailable or harness timing drifts; a short real-time delay before signaling is the fallback synchronization strategy in that case. As an additional robustness lever, a slow pre-iteration step (e.g., a `.loopx/` layout with many workflow subdirectories to scan) widens the pre-iteration window and reduces the retry rate.

- **T-SIG-20**: Signal during pre-iteration wins over missing env file. Configure a slow pre-iteration (e.g., a `.loopx/` layout with many workflow subdirectories to scan), a missing `-e nonexistent.env`, and a valid workflow target. Start loopx via `runCLIWithSignal`, deliver SIGINT during the pre-iteration window. Assert: exit code 130 (not 1), and stderr does not emit the missing-env-file error as the fatal-exit reason — the signal displaced it. `@flaky-retry(3)`. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-21**: Signal during pre-iteration wins over missing workflow. Configure a `.loopx/` with many sibling workflows (slow discovery) and target a non-existent workflow (`loopx run nonexistent-workflow`). Deliver SIGINT during the pre-iteration window. Assert exit code 130 (not 1), and no missing-workflow error is the fatal-exit reason. `@flaky-retry(3)`. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-22**: Signal during pre-iteration wins over invalid target. Configure the same slow-pre-iteration fixture; target `":script"` (invalid target format per SPEC 4.1). Deliver SIGINT during pre-iteration. Assert exit code 130, not 1 for invalid-target. `@flaky-retry(3)`. *(Spec 7.3)*
- **T-SIG-23**: Signal during pre-iteration wins over tmpdir creation failure. Configure `TMPDIR` to an unwritable path (like T-TMP-12a), and a valid target. Deliver SIGINT during pre-iteration. Assert exit code 130 (not 1 for tmpdir creation failure). Additionally assert no `loopx-*` directory is left behind under any parent (signal-wins still honors the best-effort cleanup clause from SPEC 7.4). `@flaky-retry(3)`. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 7.3, 7.4)*

### 4.12 CLI Delegation

**Spec refs:** 3.2

#### Setup

Delegation tests create the following structure:
```
/tmp/test-project/
  package.json            ← declares loopx as dependency
  node_modules/
    .bin/
      loopx → symlink or wrapper script pointing to a "local" build
  .loopx/
    ralph/
      index.sh → script that writes LOOPX_BIN to a file
```

The "global" binary is the primary build. The "local" binary is a separate build or a wrapper that sets a marker.

#### Tests

- **T-DEL-01**: When `node_modules/.bin/loopx` exists in CWD and project-root `package.json` declares `loopx` in `dependencies`, the global binary delegates to it. Verify by having the local binary write a marker file. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-02**: Delegation checks CWD only, not ancestor directories. Create a parent directory with a `package.json` that declares `loopx` as a dependency and a corresponding `node_modules/.bin/loopx`. Run loopx from a child directory (which has no `node_modules/.bin/loopx` and no `package.json`). Assert the global binary runs (no delegation). The parent must have a `package.json` declaring `loopx` so the test proves ancestor traversal was actually removed — without it, the test could pass for the weaker reason that the parent binary is undeclared (per T-DEL-16), not because ancestor traversal is not performed. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-03**: Delegation works before `.loopx/` exists. Run `loopx version` from a project root that has `package.json` declaring loopx and `node_modules/.bin/loopx`. Assert the local binary handles the command. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-04**: `LOOPX_DELEGATED=1` in environment prevents delegation. Even if `node_modules/.bin/loopx` exists, the global binary runs. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-05**: After delegation, `LOOPX_BIN` contains the resolved realpath of the local binary (not the global one, not a symlink). *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-06**: After delegation, `import from "loopx"` in scripts resolves to the **local (delegated-to) version's** package. The local (delegated-to) `node_modules/loopx` package must export a sentinel value that differs from the global CLI's package. The test script imports from `"loopx"` and writes the sentinel to a marker file. Assert: the marker file contains the delegated package's sentinel, proving module resolution actually points to the local version and not just that delegation occurred at the binary level. *(Spec 3.2, 3.3)*
- **T-DEL-07**: Delegation sets `LOOPX_DELEGATED=1` in the delegated process. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-08**: Delegation happens before command handling. Run global binary with `version` → local binary handles it. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-09**: `LOOPX_DELEGATED=""` (empty string) prevents delegation. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-10**: Delegation preserves SIGINT exit code (130). *(Spec 3.2, 7.3, 12)*
- **T-DEL-11**: Delegation preserves SIGTERM exit code (143). *(Spec 3.2, 7.3, 12)*

#### Project-Root `package.json` Failure Modes

- **T-DEL-12**: No `package.json` at project root → no delegation. Place a marker-writing binary at `node_modules/.bin/loopx` in the project root (so a delegatable binary exists on the filesystem). Run `loopx version` via the global binary. Assert: (a) the global install runs (marker file is NOT created), (b) no warning on stderr, and (c) exit code 0 with the global version string. Without the local binary in the fixture, "no delegation" is trivially true — this setup ensures the decision is driven by the missing `package.json`, not the absent binary. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-13**: Unreadable `package.json` → warning on stderr. Delegation skipped, global runs. Place a marker-writing binary at `node_modules/.bin/loopx` in the project root. Create a `package.json` at the project root and set its permissions to `000` (unreadable). Run `loopx version` via the global binary. Assert: (a) the global install runs (marker file is NOT created), (b) stderr contains a warning about the unreadable `package.json`, and (c) exit code 0 with the global version string. Without the local binary in the fixture, "delegation skipped" passes without exercising the `package.json`-driven decision path. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-14**: Invalid JSON in `package.json` → warning on stderr. Delegation skipped, global runs. Place a marker-writing binary at `node_modules/.bin/loopx` in the project root. Create a `package.json` at the project root containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Run `loopx version` via the global binary. Assert: (a) the global install runs (marker file is NOT created), (b) stderr contains a warning about the invalid JSON, and (c) exit code 0 with the global version string. Without the local binary in the fixture, "delegation skipped" passes without exercising the `package.json`-driven decision path. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-14a**: Delegation failure warning on a non-version command. Same setup as T-DEL-14 (project root with invalid-JSON `package.json` and a marker-writing `node_modules/.bin/loopx`). Run `loopx install -h` via the global binary. Assert: (a) the global install runs (marker file is NOT created), (b) stderr contains a warning about the invalid JSON, and (c) exit code 0 with install help output. T-DEL-13 and T-DEL-14 prove delegation failure modes on `loopx version`; this proves the same failure-mode warnings fire for a non-version, non-run command, pinning down that delegation failure warnings happen before command parsing for all commands. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-14b**: Delegation failure warning on bare invocation / top-level help. Same setup as T-DEL-14 (project root with invalid-JSON `package.json` and a marker-writing `node_modules/.bin/loopx`). Run bare `loopx` (no arguments) via the global binary. Assert: (a) the global install runs (marker file is NOT created — delegation was skipped due to the broken `package.json`), (b) stderr contains a warning about the invalid JSON, and (c) exit code 0 with top-level help output. T-DEL-13/T-DEL-14/T-DEL-14a prove delegation failure-mode warnings on `loopx version` and `loopx install -h`; this test extends failure-mode coverage to the bare-invocation / top-level-help path. T-DEL-22 and T-DEL-23 cover the positive (successful) delegation case on top-level help and bare invocation respectively; this test covers the negative (skipped-with-warning) case, pinning down that the "delegation happens before command parsing for all commands" rule holds on that path even when delegation is skipped. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-15**: `loopx` declared in `package.json` but `node_modules/.bin/loopx` does not exist → warning on stderr. Delegation skipped, global runs. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-16**: `node_modules/.bin/loopx` exists but `loopx` not declared in any dependency field → no delegation, no warning. The binary is undeclared. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-17**: Project-root `package.json` declares `loopx` in `optionalDependencies` (not `dependencies` or `devDependencies`) and `node_modules/.bin/loopx` exists → delegation occurs. `optionalDependencies` is checked at the project root level for locating a local binary. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-18**: Project-root `package.json` declares `loopx` in `devDependencies` (not `dependencies` or `optionalDependencies`) and `node_modules/.bin/loopx` exists → delegation occurs. `devDependencies` is checked at the project root level for locating a local binary. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-27**: Project-root `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `peerDependencies` (not in `dependencies`, `devDependencies`, or `optionalDependencies`) and `node_modules/.bin/loopx` exists → no delegation, no warning. Per SPEC 3.2, project-root delegation checks only `dependencies`, `devDependencies`, and `optionalDependencies` — `peerDependencies` is not one of the enumerated fields. Place a marker-writing binary at `node_modules/.bin/loopx` in the project root so a delegatable binary exists on the filesystem. Create a project-root `package.json` declaring `loopx` only under `peerDependencies` with any range. Run `loopx version` via the global binary. Assert: (a) the global install runs (marker file is NOT created), (b) stderr contains no warning (this is the "not declared in any checked dependency field" path from T-DEL-16, not the "declared but binary missing" path from T-DEL-15), and (c) exit code 0 with the global version string. T-DEL-17 / T-DEL-18 prove the positive cases for `optionalDependencies` and `devDependencies`, and T-DEL-16 proves the "no declaration" case; this closes the gap by proving that `peerDependencies` is not implicitly treated as one of the checked fields. **Classification:** derived-spec coverage, not core ADR-0003 acceptance coverage. SPEC 3.2 enumerates the three delegation-checked fields explicitly (`dependencies`, `devDependencies`, `optionalDependencies`) but does not explicitly discuss `peerDependencies`; this test validates an exclusion that follows from the enumerated-list semantics rather than from a direct ADR-0003 statement. Keep as a useful boundary test, but do not gate ADR-0003 acceptance on it. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-19**: Delegation is presence-based, not range-based. Project-root `package.json` declares `loopx` in `dependencies` with a semver range NOT satisfied by the local binary's actual version (e.g., `"loopx": "^99.0.0"`), and `node_modules/.bin/loopx` exists → delegation still occurs. The global binary delegates based on declaration presence and binary existence, without comparing the declared range against the local binary's version. Verify by having the local binary write a marker file. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-20**: Workflow-local `package.json` and `node_modules/.bin/loopx` do not trigger delegation. Create a project root with no `package.json`. Create `.loopx/ralph/package.json` declaring `loopx` in `dependencies` and place a marker-writing binary at `.loopx/ralph/node_modules/.bin/loopx`. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh`. Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph`. Assert: (a) the global binary runs (marker file is NOT created), and (b) execution succeeds normally. Delegation is based on the project-root `package.json` only — workflow-level version declarations are not used for delegation. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-21**: Delegation applies to non-version, non-run commands. Set up a project root with `package.json` declaring `loopx` in `dependencies` and a corresponding marker-writing `node_modules/.bin/loopx`. Run `loopx install -h` via the global binary. Assert the local binary handles the command (marker file created). This pins down that the simplified delegation model (cwd-only, command-agnostic, before command parsing) applies to commands beyond `version` and `run` — including commands that do not require `.loopx/`. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-22**: Delegation applies to top-level help. Same delegation setup as T-DEL-21. Run `loopx -h` via the global binary. Assert the local binary handles the command (marker file created). Spec 3.2 says delegation happens before command parsing, so the top-level help short-circuit path must also delegate. This extends T-DEL-08 (version), T-DEL-21 (install -h) to the top-level help path. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-23**: Delegation applies to bare invocation. Same delegation setup as T-DEL-21. Run bare `loopx` (no arguments) via the global binary. Assert the local binary handles the command (marker file created). Bare `loopx` is equivalent to `loopx -h` (Spec 4.1), but delegation occurs before that equivalence is resolved — a bad implementation could skip delegation for the zero-argument case. *(Spec 3.2)*

#### Delegation × Version-Check Interaction

- **T-DEL-24**: Runtime delegation × version checking. Set up delegation: project root `package.json` declares `loopx` in `dependencies` with `node_modules/.bin/loopx` present. The local (delegated-to) binary reports version `2.0.0`. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with a `package.json` declaring `"loopx": "^2.0.0"` in `dependencies`. Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph` via the global binary. Assert: (a) delegation occurs (local binary handles the command), and (b) no version mismatch warning on stderr — the version check compares the workflow's declared range against the delegated local version (`2.0.0`), not the global launcher version. This closes the gap between delegation (T-DEL-01–23) and runtime version checking (T-VER-01–25), which are each tested in isolation but never in combination. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-DEL-25**: Install-time delegation × version checking. Same delegation setup as T-DEL-24: local binary reports version `2.0.0`. Source workflow declares `"loopx": "^2.0.0"` in its `package.json`. Run `loopx install <source>` via the global binary. Assert: (a) delegation occurs, (b) install succeeds without version mismatch error, and (c) the workflow is installed in `.loopx/`. The install-time version check must compare the workflow's declared range against the effective delegated version, not the global launcher version. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*

#### Additional Delegated Subcommand Coverage

- **T-DEL-26**: Delegation applies to `env list`. Same delegation setup as T-DEL-21. Run `loopx env list` via the global binary. Assert the local binary handles the command (marker file created). T-DEL-08 covers `version`, T-DEL-21 covers `install -h`, T-DEL-22 covers `-h`, and T-DEL-23 covers bare invocation — this extends delegation coverage to a non-help, non-version, non-install subcommand, fully pinning down the "all commands" claim from Spec 3.2. *(Spec 3.2)*

### 4.13 Workflow-Level Version Checking

**Spec refs:** 3.2

- **T-VER-01**: Workflow `package.json` declares a loopx range satisfied by the running version → execution proceeds, no warning. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-02**: Workflow `package.json` declares a loopx range NOT satisfied → warning on stderr, execution continues (non-fatal). *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-03**: Warning occurs only on first entry to a workflow. Re-entering the same workflow (via loop reset or goto) does not repeat the warning. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-04**: Cross-workflow first-entry warning. Starting workflow has no version declaration. Goto to a second workflow that declares an unsatisfied range → warning emitted on first entry to second workflow. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-04a**: Cross-workflow alternating re-entry version-warning deduplication. Create two workflows: `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` and `.loopx/beta/index.sh`, both with `package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range. Set up a multi-iteration loop where execution alternates: `alpha:index` → goto `beta:index` → (no goto, reset) → `alpha:index` → goto `beta:index` → stop. Assert: (a) stderr contains exactly one version mismatch warning for `alpha` and exactly one for `beta`, (b) no duplicate warnings appear despite both workflows being entered twice. This makes the ADR-0003 cross-workflow "first entry only" intent explicit — T-VER-03 covers single-workflow re-entry and T-VER-04 covers first entry to a second workflow, but neither covers the full A→B→A→B alternation pattern. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-05**: Starting workflow checked before first iteration. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-06**: `-n 0` skips workflow version warnings. Set up workflow with unsatisfied version range. Assert no warning on stderr. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-07**: Workflow `package.json` unreadable → warning, execution continues. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-07a**: Runtime `package.json` failure warning follows "first entry only" dedupe. Create a workflow with invalid JSON in its `package.json`. Run a loop that re-enters the workflow multiple times (e.g., via loop reset). Assert that the `package.json` failure warning appears exactly once on stderr, not on each re-entry. This locks down the same "first entry only" rule that T-VER-03 tests for version mismatch warnings, applied to `package.json` failure warnings (unreadable, invalid JSON, invalid semver range). *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-07b**: Runtime `package.json` failure warning follows "first entry only" dedupe for invalid semver ranges. Create a workflow with a valid `package.json` containing an invalid semver range for `loopx` (e.g., `"loopx": "not-a-range"`). Run a loop that re-enters the workflow multiple times. Assert that the invalid-semver warning appears exactly once on stderr. This is the invalid-semver counterpart to T-VER-07a (invalid JSON). *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-07c**: Runtime `package.json` failure warning follows "first entry only" dedupe for unreadable workflow `package.json`. Create a workflow with an unreadable `package.json` (e.g., mode 000). Run a loop that re-enters the workflow multiple times (e.g., via loop reset). Assert that the unreadable-file warning appears exactly once on stderr, not on each re-entry. This is the unreadable-file counterpart to T-VER-07a (invalid JSON) and T-VER-07b (invalid semver). **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-07d**: Cross-workflow `package.json` failure warning via goto. Create two workflows: `.loopx/clean/index.sh` (no `package.json` or a valid one with no loopx declaration) and `.loopx/broken/index.sh` with a `package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Set up a loop where `clean:index` emits a goto to `broken:index`, and `broken:index` completes without goto (triggering loop reset). Run for multiple iterations. Assert: (a) the invalid-JSON warning for `broken` is emitted exactly once on stderr (on first entry via goto), (b) no warning is emitted for `clean`, and (c) execution continues normally (the invalid `package.json` does not block the goto transition). This covers the failure-warning path when a workflow is first entered cross-workflow — T-VER-07a covers re-entry deduplication within a single workflow, and T-VER-04 covers version-mismatch warnings on cross-workflow goto, but neither covers `package.json` failure warnings on cross-workflow first entry. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-07e**: Cross-workflow `package.json` failure warning via goto — unreadable variant. Same structure as T-VER-07d: create `.loopx/clean/index.sh` (no `package.json` or a valid one with no loopx declaration) and `.loopx/broken/index.sh` with an unreadable `package.json` (mode 000). Set up a loop where `clean:index` gotos `broken:index`, and `broken:index` completes without goto (triggering loop reset). Run for multiple iterations. Assert: (a) the unreadable-file warning for `broken` is emitted exactly once on stderr (on first entry via goto), (b) no warning is emitted for `clean`, and (c) execution continues normally. This is the unreadable-file counterpart to T-VER-07d (invalid JSON) — T-VER-07c covers re-entry dedupe for unreadable files within a single workflow, but not the cross-workflow first-entry path. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-07f**: Cross-workflow `package.json` failure warning via goto — invalid semver range variant. Same structure as T-VER-07d: create `.loopx/clean/index.sh` (no `package.json` or a valid one with no loopx declaration) and `.loopx/broken/index.sh` with a `package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }` (valid JSON but invalid semver range). Set up a loop where `clean:index` gotos `broken:index`, and `broken:index` completes without goto (triggering loop reset). Run for multiple iterations. Assert: (a) the invalid-semver warning for `broken` is emitted exactly once on stderr (on first entry via goto), (b) no warning is emitted for `clean`, and (c) execution continues normally. This is the invalid-semver counterpart to T-VER-07d (invalid JSON) and T-VER-07e (unreadable). *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-08**: Workflow `package.json` invalid JSON → warning, execution continues. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-09**: Workflow `package.json` invalid semver range → warning, execution continues. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-10**: `dependencies` range wins over `devDependencies` when both are present. Set up a workflow `package.json` with `dependencies.loopx` having a satisfied range and `devDependencies.loopx` having an unsatisfied range → no version mismatch warning on stderr. Reverse the ranges (`dependencies.loopx` unsatisfied, `devDependencies.loopx` satisfied) → version mismatch warning on stderr, execution continues. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-10a**: Runtime: `dependencies.loopx` has an invalid semver range (e.g., `"not-a-range"`), `devDependencies.loopx` has a valid but unsatisfied range (e.g., `">=999.0.0"`). Assert: (a) stderr contains a warning about the invalid semver range in `dependencies`, (b) stderr does NOT contain a version mismatch warning (the version check is skipped, not failed), and (c) execution continues. The `dependencies` field takes precedence — when it is present but invalid, loopx warns and skips version checking entirely. It must not fall back to `devDependencies.loopx`. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-10b**: Runtime: `dependencies.loopx` has a valid, satisfied range, `devDependencies.loopx` has an invalid semver range (e.g., `"not-a-range"`). Assert: (a) no version mismatch warning on stderr, (b) no invalid-semver warning on stderr, and (c) execution continues normally. When `dependencies.loopx` is present, `devDependencies.loopx` is ignored entirely — it is not read or validated, even if malformed. T-VER-10 proves precedence with two valid ranges; T-VER-10a proves no fallback when `dependencies` is invalid. This test closes the converse gap: `dependencies` is valid and satisfied, so `devDependencies` must be invisible regardless of its content. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-11**: `optionalDependencies` ignored at workflow level. Workflow `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `optionalDependencies` with an unsatisfied range → no version warning at runtime. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-11a**: Runtime: `optionalDependencies.loopx` with an invalid semver range (e.g., `"not-a-range"`) is ignored. Workflow `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `optionalDependencies` with an invalid semver range — no `dependencies.loopx` or `devDependencies.loopx` present. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) no version mismatch warning on stderr, and (c) no invalid-semver or `package.json` warning on stderr. T-VER-11 covers a valid-but-unsatisfied `optionalDependencies.loopx`; this extends coverage to the malformed case, proving the field is fully invisible at the workflow level — it is not read or validated, even when malformed. An implementation that read `optionalDependencies.loopx` only to emit invalid-semver warnings would fail this test. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-11b**: Runtime: `peerDependencies.loopx` is ignored at the workflow level. Workflow `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `peerDependencies` with a valid but unsatisfied range (e.g., `">=999.0.0"`) — no `dependencies.loopx`, `devDependencies.loopx`, or `optionalDependencies.loopx` present. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` and run `loopx run -n 1 ralph`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) no version mismatch warning on stderr, and (c) no `package.json`-related warning on stderr. Per SPEC 3.2, workflow-level version checking reads only `dependencies` and `devDependencies` (with `optionalDependencies` explicitly ignored at the workflow level). T-VER-11 / T-VER-11a prove `optionalDependencies` is ignored at runtime; this test proves `peerDependencies` is also outside the checked set — the field is fully invisible at the workflow level and must not trigger a mismatch warning. **Classification:** derived-spec coverage, not core ADR-0003 acceptance coverage. SPEC 3.2 enumerates the workflow-level checked fields explicitly (`dependencies`, `devDependencies`; with `optionalDependencies` explicitly excluded) but does not explicitly discuss `peerDependencies`; this test validates an exclusion that follows from the enumerated-list semantics rather than from a direct ADR-0003 statement. Keep as a useful boundary test, but do not gate ADR-0003 acceptance on it. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-11c**: Runtime: `optionalDependencies.loopx` does not rescue an unsatisfied `dependencies.loopx`. Workflow `package.json` declares `loopx` in BOTH `dependencies` (with an unsatisfied range, e.g., `">=999.0.0"`) AND `optionalDependencies` (with a satisfied range, e.g., `"*"` or the running version's exact value) — no `devDependencies.loopx`. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` and run `loopx run -n 1 ralph`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, and (b) stderr contains a version mismatch warning for `ralph`. Because `optionalDependencies` is intentionally not checked at the workflow level (Spec 3.2), its satisfied range must not suppress the `dependencies` mismatch warning. T-VER-11 / T-VER-11a prove `optionalDependencies` alone is ignored at runtime, and T-VER-14a pins down the mixed case for `devDependencies` + `optionalDependencies`; this test closes the symmetric gap for `dependencies` + `optionalDependencies`, covering the highest-precedence workflow-level version-check field (Spec 3.2: `dependencies` wins over `devDependencies`) in the mixed-field configuration. An implementation that wrongly merged `optionalDependencies` into the workflow-level check would suppress the mismatch warning and fail this test. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-12**: Install-time version checking: `dependencies` range wins over `devDependencies` when both are present in a workflow's `package.json`. Set up `dependencies.loopx` with a satisfied range and `devDependencies.loopx` with an unsatisfied range → install succeeds (no version mismatch error). Reverse the ranges → install fails. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-12a**: Install-time: `dependencies.loopx` has an invalid semver range, `devDependencies.loopx` has a valid but unsatisfied range. Assert: (a) stderr contains a warning about the invalid semver range in `dependencies`, (b) install succeeds (the version check is skipped, not failed — invalid semver does not block install per Spec 3.2), and (c) no version mismatch error is reported. The `dependencies` field takes precedence — when it is present but invalid, the version check is skipped entirely. It must not fall back to `devDependencies.loopx`. This is the install-time counterpart to T-VER-10a. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-12b**: Install-time: `dependencies.loopx` has a valid, satisfied range, `devDependencies.loopx` has an invalid semver range (e.g., `"not-a-range"`). Assert: (a) install succeeds, (b) no invalid-semver warning on stderr, and (c) no version mismatch error. When `dependencies.loopx` is present, `devDependencies.loopx` is ignored entirely at install time — it is not read or validated, even if malformed. This is the install-time counterpart to T-VER-10b. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-13**: Install-time version checking: `optionalDependencies.loopx` is ignored at the workflow level. Workflow `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `optionalDependencies` with an unsatisfied range → install succeeds (no version check performed). *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-13a**: Install-time: `optionalDependencies.loopx` with an invalid semver range (e.g., `"not-a-range"`) is ignored. A workflow source's `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `optionalDependencies` with an invalid semver range — no `dependencies.loopx` or `devDependencies.loopx` present. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the workflow is installed, (c) no version mismatch error, and (d) no invalid-semver or `package.json` warning on stderr. This is the install-time counterpart to T-VER-11a, extending T-VER-13 (valid-but-unsatisfied) to the malformed case. Proves `optionalDependencies.loopx` is fully invisible at the workflow level at install time as well. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-13b**: Install-time: `peerDependencies.loopx` is ignored at the workflow level. A workflow source's `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `peerDependencies` with a valid but unsatisfied range (e.g., `">=999.0.0"`) — no `dependencies.loopx`, `devDependencies.loopx`, or `optionalDependencies.loopx` present. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the workflow is installed, (c) no version mismatch error, and (d) no `package.json`-related warning on stderr. Per SPEC 3.2, install-time version checking uses the same rules as runtime — only `dependencies` and `devDependencies` are read. T-VER-13 / T-VER-13a prove `optionalDependencies` is ignored at install time; this is the `peerDependencies` counterpart and the install-time mirror of T-VER-11b, locking down that the excluded-dependency-field set is the same at install time as at runtime. **Classification:** derived-spec coverage, not core ADR-0003 acceptance coverage. SPEC 3.2 enumerates the workflow-level checked fields explicitly (`dependencies`, `devDependencies`; with `optionalDependencies` explicitly excluded) but does not explicitly discuss `peerDependencies`; this test validates an exclusion that follows from the enumerated-list semantics rather than from a direct ADR-0003 statement. Keep as a useful boundary test, but do not gate ADR-0003 acceptance on it. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-13c**: Install-time: `optionalDependencies.loopx` does not rescue an unsatisfied `dependencies.loopx`. Workflow source's `package.json` declares `loopx` in BOTH `dependencies` (with an unsatisfied range, e.g., `">=999.0.0"`) AND `optionalDependencies` (with a satisfied range, e.g., `"*"` or the running version's exact value) — no `devDependencies.loopx`. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with a version mismatch error, and (b) the workflow is not installed. With `-y`, the install succeeds (override). This is the install-time counterpart to T-VER-11c — the "ignore `optionalDependencies` at the workflow level" rule applies identically at install time (Spec 3.2 and 10.6), and a satisfied `optionalDependencies.loopx` must not suppress the install-blocking mismatch detected via `dependencies.loopx`. T-VER-13 / T-VER-13a prove `optionalDependencies` alone is ignored at install time, and T-VER-15a pins down the mixed case for `devDependencies` + `optionalDependencies` at install time; this test closes the symmetric gap for `dependencies` + `optionalDependencies` at install time, covering the highest-precedence workflow-level version-check field (Spec 3.2: `dependencies` wins over `devDependencies`) in the mixed-field configuration. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-14**: Runtime version checking: `devDependencies.loopx` only (no `dependencies.loopx`). Workflow `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `devDependencies` with an unsatisfied range → warning on stderr, execution continues. This proves the `devDependencies`-only path works independently of the `dependencies`-over-`devDependencies` precedence rule tested in T-VER-10. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-14a**: Runtime: `optionalDependencies.loopx` does not rescue an unsatisfied `devDependencies.loopx`. Workflow `package.json` declares `loopx` in BOTH `devDependencies` (with an unsatisfied range, e.g., `">=999.0.0"`) AND `optionalDependencies` (with a satisfied range, e.g., `"*"` or the running version's exact value) — no `dependencies.loopx`. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` and run `loopx run -n 1 ralph`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, and (b) stderr contains a version mismatch warning for `ralph`. Because `optionalDependencies` is intentionally not checked at the workflow level (Spec 3.2), its satisfied range must not suppress the `devDependencies` mismatch warning. T-VER-11 / T-VER-11a prove `optionalDependencies` alone is ignored, and T-VER-14 proves `devDependencies`-only unsatisfied warns; this test pins down the mixed case where a satisfied `optionalDependencies` could appear to "rescue" the check if an implementation wrongly merged fields. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-15**: Install-time version checking: `devDependencies.loopx` only (no `dependencies.loopx`). Workflow `package.json` declares `loopx` only in `devDependencies` with an unsatisfied range → install refused with version mismatch error. This proves the `devDependencies`-only install path works independently of the precedence rule tested in T-VER-12. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-15a**: Install-time: `optionalDependencies.loopx` does not rescue an unsatisfied `devDependencies.loopx`. Workflow source's `package.json` declares `loopx` in BOTH `devDependencies` (with an unsatisfied range, e.g., `">=999.0.0"`) AND `optionalDependencies` (with a satisfied range, e.g., `"*"` or the running version's exact value) — no `dependencies.loopx`. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with a version mismatch error, and (b) the workflow is not installed. With `-y`, the install succeeds (override). This is the install-time counterpart to T-VER-14a — the "ignore `optionalDependencies` at the workflow level" rule applies identically at install time (Spec 3.2 and 10.6), and a satisfied `optionalDependencies.loopx` must not suppress the install-blocking mismatch detected via `devDependencies.loopx`. T-VER-13 / T-VER-13a prove `optionalDependencies` alone is ignored at install time, and T-VER-15 proves `devDependencies`-only unsatisfied blocks install; this test pins down the mixed case. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-16**: Runtime: workflow has a valid `package.json` with no `loopx` declared in any dependency field (e.g., `{ "name": "my-workflow", "version": "1.0.0" }`) → no version check is performed, no warning emitted. Execution proceeds normally. This explicitly tests the "valid JSON, no `loopx` dependency declared → no version check" rule from Spec 3.2. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-17**: Install-time: workflow source has a valid `package.json` with no `loopx` declared in any dependency field → no version check is performed, install succeeds without version-related errors or warnings. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-18**: Unentered sibling workflows are not version-checked. Create `.loopx/good/index.sh` (the starting workflow, no `package.json`) and `.loopx/sibling/index.sh` with a `package.json` declaring a loopx range NOT satisfied by the running version. Run `loopx run -n 1 good` (the starting workflow completes without ever entering `sibling`). Assert: (a) exit code 0, and (b) no version mismatch warning on stderr for `sibling`. Version checks are entry-scoped — only workflows actually entered during the loop have their `package.json` checked. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-18a**: Unentered sibling workflow with broken `package.json` emits no warning. Create `.loopx/good/index.sh` (the starting workflow, no `package.json`) and `.loopx/sibling/index.sh` with a `package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{{{INVALID`). Run `loopx run -n 1 good`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, and (b) stderr contains no `package.json`-related warnings (no JSON parse warning, no version warning).
