T-VER-18 covers an unentered sibling with an unsatisfied range; this test extends coverage to the `package.json` failure-warning path (invalid JSON), proving that `package.json` failure warnings are also entry-scoped — the sibling's `package.json` is never read because the sibling workflow is never entered. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-19**: `loopx run -h` does not perform workflow version or `package.json` checks. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with a `package.json` declaring a loopx range NOT satisfied by the running version. Run `loopx run -h`. Assert: (a) help output is displayed, (b) exit code 0, and (c) stderr contains no version mismatch warnings. Version checking is entry-scoped — `run -h` performs discovery and validation (names, collisions) but does not enter any workflow, so version checks do not run. *(Spec 3.2, 11.2)*
- **T-VER-19a**: `loopx run -h` does not read workflow `package.json` — unreadable file variant. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with a `package.json` set to mode 000 (unreadable). Run `loopx run -h`. Assert: (a) help output is displayed, (b) exit code 0, and (c) stderr contains no `package.json`-related read warnings. An implementation that wrongly reads workflow `package.json` during help would emit a read-failure warning; this test catches that. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 3.2, 11.2)*
- **T-VER-19b**: `loopx run -h` does not read workflow `package.json` — invalid JSON variant. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with a `package.json` containing `{{{INVALID`. Run `loopx run -h`. Assert: (a) help output is displayed, (b) exit code 0, and (c) stderr contains no JSON parse warnings. An implementation that wrongly reads workflow `package.json` during help would emit a parse-failure warning. *(Spec 3.2, 11.2)*
- **T-VER-19c**: `loopx run -h` does not read workflow `package.json` — invalid semver variant. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with a `package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }`. Run `loopx run -h`. Assert: (a) help output is displayed, (b) exit code 0, and (c) stderr contains no semver/version warnings. An implementation that wrongly reads workflow `package.json` during help would emit an invalid-semver warning. *(Spec 3.2, 11.2)*
- **T-VER-20**: Workflow `package.json` is not re-read after first entry (mutation test). Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with a `package.json` declaring a loopx range SATISFIED by the running version. Set up a multi-iteration loop where the script mutates its own `package.json` to an UNSATISFIED range after the first iteration (e.g., rewrites the loopx version field to `">=999.0.0"`), then re-enters the workflow (via loop reset). Assert: no version mismatch warning appears on any iteration, proving the file was not re-read after first entry. This goes beyond T-VER-03 (which proves the warning is not repeated) by proving the file itself is not re-checked — if the implementation re-read `package.json` on re-entry, the mutated range would trigger a new warning. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-20a**: Workflow `package.json` is not re-read after first entry — absent-then-broken mutation. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with no `package.json` in the workflow directory at loop start. Set up a multi-iteration loop where the script creates `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`) after its first iteration, then re-enters the workflow via loop reset. Assert: no `package.json` failure warning (invalid-JSON parse warning) appears on stderr on later iterations, proving the file itself is not re-read after first entry. T-VER-20 proves "not re-read" for the satisfied-then-unsatisfied version-range mutation path; this test proves "not re-read" for the absent-then-broken `package.json` failure path — a distinct code path where the initial first-entry read found no file at all, so an implementation could plausibly retry the read on re-entry and emit a new parse warning. This closes the `package.json`-failure branch of the Spec 3.2 "subsequent entries do not re-read `package.json` or repeat warnings" rule. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-21**: Workflow with no `package.json` runs with no version-check warning. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with no `package.json` in the workflow directory. Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) stderr contains no version-related warnings or `package.json`-related warnings. This locks down the "normal case" from Spec 3.2: absent `package.json` means no version check is performed and no warnings are emitted. An implementation that wrongly warns on missing `package.json` would fail this test. *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-22**: Workflow with no `package.json` installs with no version-related warning. Set up a single-workflow install source with no `package.json`. Run `loopx install <source>`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) stderr contains no version-related warnings or `package.json`-related warnings, (c) the workflow is installed in `.loopx/`. This is the install-time counterpart to T-VER-21. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-23**: A stray `.loopx/package.json` is ignored for runtime version checking. Create `.loopx/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }` (an unsatisfied range). Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` with no workflow-level `package.json`. Run `loopx run -n 1 ralph`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, and (b) no version mismatch warning on stderr. The `.loopx/package.json` file is not a recognized manifest — version authority lives only in the project root `package.json` (for delegation) and each workflow's own `package.json` (for runtime/install-time validation). *(Spec 3.2)*
- **T-VER-23a**: A pre-existing stray `.loopx/package.json` is ignored at install time. In the target project, create `.loopx/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }` (an unsatisfied range) **before** running install. Then run `loopx install <single-workflow-source>` where the source has no `package.json`. Assert: (a) exit code 0, (b) the workflow is installed at `.loopx/<name>/`, (c) the stray `.loopx/package.json` is preserved unchanged, and (d) no version mismatch or `package.json` warnings on stderr. The `.loopx/package.json` is not a recognized manifest at install time either — install only reads and validates each workflow's own `package.json`. This is the install-time counterpart to T-VER-23 (runtime). T-INST-97b proves install does not *create* `.loopx/package.json`; this test proves install does not *read* a pre-existing one. *(Spec 3.2, 10.6)*
- **T-VER-24**: No version/package warning when the starting target cannot be entered. Create `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (valid workflow with no `index` script) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }` (an unsatisfied range). Run `loopx run ralph`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with an error about missing default entry point (`index`), and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings. Target resolution (Spec 7.1 step 3) fails before workflow-entry version checking (step 5) is reached — the workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2)*
- **T-VER-24a**: No `package.json` failure warning when the starting target cannot be entered — broken JSON variant. Create `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (valid workflow with no `index` script) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing `{{{INVALID`. Run `loopx run ralph`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with an error about missing default entry point, and (b) stderr contains no JSON parse warnings. This extends T-VER-24 from the unsatisfied-range path to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure path. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2)*
- **T-VER-24b**: No version/package warning when an explicit `workflow:script` start target names a missing script — unsatisfied range variant. Create `.loopx/ralph/index.sh` (valid workflow, `index` present) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }` (an unsatisfied range). Run `loopx run ralph:missing` (explicit target where `missing` is not a script in `ralph`). Assert: (a) exit code 1 with an error about the missing script `missing` in workflow `ralph`, and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings for `ralph`. Target resolution fails before workflow-entry version checking runs — the workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. This is the explicit-`workflow:script`-start counterpart to T-VER-24 (bare target missing default entry) and T-VER-25 (goto target missing script). ADR-0003 made explicit `workflow:script` start targets first-class, so the ordering rule that target resolution precedes version checking must hold for them too. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-24c**: No `package.json` failure warning when an explicit `workflow:script` start target names a missing script — broken JSON variant. Same setup as T-VER-24b but `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains `{{{INVALID` (broken JSON) instead of an unsatisfied range. Run `loopx run ralph:missing`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with missing-script error for `missing` in `ralph`, and (b) stderr contains no JSON parse warnings for `ralph`. This extends T-VER-24b from the unsatisfied-range path to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure path, mirroring the T-VER-24 → T-VER-24a split for the bare-target missing-default-entry case and the T-VER-25 → T-VER-25a split for the goto-target-missing-script case. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-24d**: No version/package warning when an explicit `:index` start target names a non-existent `index` in a workflow without one — unsatisfied range variant. Create `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (valid workflow with no `index.*` script) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }` (an unsatisfied range). Run `loopx run ralph:index`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with an error about the missing script `index` in workflow `ralph`, and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings for `ralph`. Target resolution fails before workflow-entry version checking runs — the workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. This is the **combined** case that T-VER-24 (bare target, missing default entry), T-VER-24b (explicit `workflow:missing` target), and T-CLI-109a / T-API-20j2 / T-API-45a (plain error shape for `workflow:index` with no index) do not jointly cover: the explicit `:index` target on a workflow that has no index AND a workflow-level version declaration. ADR-0003 makes `index` special only when the script portion is omitted, so the explicit `:index` path must enforce the same "target resolution precedes version checking" ordering as any other missing script. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-24e**: No `package.json` failure warning when an explicit `:index` start target names a non-existent `index` in a workflow without one — broken JSON variant. Same setup as T-VER-24d but `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains `{{{INVALID` (broken JSON) instead of an unsatisfied range. Run `loopx run ralph:index`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with an error about the missing script `index` in workflow `ralph`, and (b) stderr contains no JSON parse warnings for `ralph`. This extends T-VER-24d from the unsatisfied-range path to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure path, mirroring the T-VER-24 → T-VER-24a and T-VER-24b → T-VER-24c splits. Together T-VER-24d/24e close the combined-case gap across both `package.json` failure branches for the explicit-`:index`-on-no-index-workflow path. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-25**: No version/package warning when a goto target script does not exist. Create `.loopx/start/index.sh` that outputs `{ "goto": "other:missing" }`. Create `.loopx/other/index.sh` (valid workflow) with `.loopx/other/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }` (an unsatisfied range). Run `loopx run -n 2 start`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with an error about missing script `missing` in workflow `other`, and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings for `other`. Goto target resolution (Spec 7.1 step 11.d) fails before the first-entry version check (step 11.e) — the target workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2)*
- **T-VER-25a**: No `package.json` failure warning when a goto target script does not exist — broken JSON variant. Same setup as T-VER-25 but `.loopx/other/package.json` contains `{{{INVALID` instead of an unsatisfied range. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with missing-script error, and (b) no JSON parse warnings on stderr for `other`. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2)*
- **T-VER-25b**: No version/package warning when a goto emits `workflow:index` but the target workflow has no `index` — unsatisfied range variant. Create `.loopx/start/index.sh` that outputs `{ "goto": "other:index" }`. Create `.loopx/other/check.sh` (valid workflow with no `index.*` script) and `.loopx/other/package.json` containing `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": ">=999.0.0" } }` (an unsatisfied range). Run `loopx run -n 2 start`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with an error about the missing script `index` in workflow `other`, and (b) stderr contains no version mismatch or `package.json`-related warnings for `other`. Goto target resolution fails before the first-entry version check — the target workflow is never entered, so its `package.json` is never read. This is the **combined** case that T-LOOP-31c (generic missing `other:index` goto error shape) and T-VER-25 / T-VER-25a (generic missing goto script `other:missing` with unsatisfied range / broken JSON) do not jointly cover: the specific `:index` goto target on a workflow that has no index AND a workflow-level version declaration. ADR-0003 makes `index` special only when the script portion is omitted, and that rule must hold on the cross-workflow goto path as well — so the qualified `workflow:index` goto target into a no-index workflow must follow the ordinary missing-script ordering rule, never entering the workflow and never emitting version/package warnings for it. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-25c**: No `package.json` failure warning when a goto emits `workflow:index` but the target workflow has no `index` — broken JSON variant. Same setup as T-VER-25b but `.loopx/other/package.json` contains `{{{INVALID` (broken JSON) instead of an unsatisfied range. Run `loopx run -n 2 start`. Assert: (a) exit code 1 with an error about the missing script `index` in workflow `other`, and (b) stderr contains no JSON parse warnings for `other`. This extends T-VER-25b from the unsatisfied-range path to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure path, mirroring the T-VER-25 → T-VER-25a split. Together T-VER-25b/25c close the combined-case gap across both `package.json` failure branches for the goto-`workflow:index`-into-no-index-workflow path. *(Spec 7.1, 3.2, 2.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-26**: Runtime version check fires on explicit script entry into a no-index workflow. Create `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (no `index` script) with a `package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range. `loopx run -n 1 ralph:check` → (a) warning on stderr about version mismatch, (b) exit code 0, (c) `check.sh` executed (marker file written). This combines no-index (T-CLI-110, T-DISC-19) with version checking (T-VER-02) — both are individually covered, but the combination tests that version checking still runs when entry is via an explicit script in a workflow without a default entry point. *(Spec 3.2, 4.1, 2.1)*
- **T-VER-26a**: Runtime `package.json` failure warning on explicit-script entry into a no-index workflow — invalid JSON variant. Create `.loopx/ralph/check.sh` (no `index` script) and `.loopx/ralph/package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). `loopx run -n 1 ralph:check` → (a) warning on stderr about the invalid `package.json`, (b) exit code 0, (c) `check.sh` executed (marker file written). Extends T-VER-26 (unsatisfied range on explicit entry into a no-index workflow) to the invalid-JSON `package.json` failure path. T-VER-08 covers invalid JSON on normal (bare) workflow entry; this test pins down that the same warning fires when entering via an explicit `workflow:script` target in a workflow without a default entry point. This is the normal-execution counterpart to the explicit-target `-n 0` coverage in T-CLI-119i. *(Spec 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-26b**: Runtime `package.json` failure warning on explicit-script entry into a no-index workflow — invalid semver range variant. Same structure as T-VER-26a, but `.loopx/ralph/package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }` (valid JSON, invalid semver range). Assert: (a) warning on stderr about the invalid semver range, (b) exit code 0, (c) `check.sh` executed. Invalid-semver counterpart to T-VER-26a; normal-execution counterpart to T-CLI-119j. T-VER-09 covers invalid semver on normal (bare) workflow entry. *(Spec 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-26c**: Runtime `package.json` failure warning on explicit-script entry into a no-index workflow — unreadable variant. Same structure as T-VER-26a, but `.loopx/ralph/package.json` is unreadable (e.g., mode 000). Assert: (a) warning on stderr about the unreadable `package.json`, (b) exit code 0, (c) `check.sh` executed. Unreadable-file counterpart to T-VER-26a and T-VER-26b; normal-execution counterpart to T-CLI-119k. T-VER-07 covers unreadable on normal (bare) workflow entry. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 3.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-27**: Cross-workflow first-entry version warning for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto. Create two workflows: `.loopx/alpha/index.sh` (no `package.json`, emits `goto:"beta:check"`) and `.loopx/beta/check.sh` (no `index` script) with `package.json` declaring an unsatisfied loopx range. `loopx run -n 2 alpha`. Assert: (a) `beta:check` executes (marker file), (b) stderr contains a version mismatch warning for `beta` on first entry, and (c) no warning for `alpha`. This combines cross-workflow goto into a no-index workflow (T-LOOP-30a) with version checking (T-VER-04) — both covered separately, but the combination tests that the first-entry version check fires when the transition target is an explicit script in a workflow that has no default entry point. *(Spec 3.2, 2.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-27a**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto — invalid JSON variant. Create two workflows: `.loopx/clean/index.sh` (no `package.json` or a valid one with no loopx declaration, emits `goto:"broken:check"`) and `.loopx/broken/check.sh` (no `index` script) with `package.json` containing invalid JSON (e.g., `{broken`). Set up a loop where `clean:index` gotos `broken:check`, and `broken:check` completes without goto (triggering loop reset). Run for multiple iterations (e.g., `-n 4`). Assert: (a) `broken:check` executes (marker file), (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-JSON warning for `broken` (emitted on first entry via goto), (c) no warning is emitted for `clean`, and (d) execution continues normally. T-VER-07d covers cross-workflow goto into `broken:index` (index present); T-VER-27 covers cross-workflow goto into a no-index workflow with version mismatch; this test is the combination — cross-workflow goto into a no-index workflow (entered via explicit `workflow:script` qualified goto) with an invalid-JSON `package.json`. ADR-0003 made explicit `workflow:script` entry into no-index workflows a first-class path, so `package.json` failure warnings must fire on this path too. *(Spec 3.2, 2.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-27b**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto — unreadable variant. Same structure as T-VER-27a, but `.loopx/broken/package.json` is set to mode 000 (unreadable) instead of containing invalid JSON. Assert: (a) `broken:check` executes (marker file), (b) stderr contains exactly one unreadable-file warning for `broken` (emitted on first entry via goto), (c) no warning for `clean`, and (d) execution continues normally. Unreadable-file counterpart to T-VER-27a (invalid JSON) — T-VER-07e covers the same `package.json` failure mode on cross-workflow goto into a workflow *with* an `index` script; this test covers the no-index path. **Conditional on `process.getuid() !== 0`.** *(Spec 3.2, 2.2, 4.1)*
- **T-VER-27c**: Cross-workflow first-entry `package.json` failure warning for a no-index workflow entered via qualified goto — invalid semver range variant. Same structure as T-VER-27a, but `.loopx/broken/package.json` contains `{ "dependencies": { "loopx": "not-a-range!!!" } }` (valid JSON but invalid semver range) instead of invalid JSON. Assert: (a) `broken:check` executes (marker file), (b) stderr contains exactly one invalid-semver warning for `broken` (emitted on first entry via goto), (c) no warning for `clean`, and (d) execution continues normally. Invalid-semver counterpart to T-VER-27a (invalid JSON) and T-VER-27b (unreadable) — T-VER-07f covers the same `package.json` failure mode on cross-workflow goto into a workflow *with* an `index` script; this test covers the no-index path. Together, T-VER-27a/27b/27c prove that all three `package.json` failure-warning branches fire on cross-workflow first entry into a no-index workflow via qualified goto, not just the version-mismatch branch (T-VER-27). *(Spec 3.2, 2.2, 4.1)*

### 4.14 Exit Codes (Cross-Cutting)

**Spec refs:** 12

- **T-EXIT-01**: Clean exit via `stop: true` → code 0. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-02**: Clean exit via `-n` limit reached → code 0. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-03**: Clean exit via `-n 0` → code 0. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-04**: Successful subcommand (`loopx version`) → code 0. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-05**: Script exits non-zero → code 1. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-06**: Validation failure (name collision) → code 1. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-07**: Invalid goto target → code 1. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-08**: Missing workflow → code 1. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-09**: Missing `.loopx/` directory → code 1. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-10**: Usage error (invalid `-n`) → code 1. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-11**: Missing `-e` file → code 1. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-12**: SIGINT → code 130. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-13**: SIGTERM → code 143. *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-14**: `loopx run` with no target → code 1 (usage error). *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-15**: `loopx ralph` (unrecognized subcommand) → code 1 (usage error). *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-16**: `loopx --unknown` → code 1 (usage error). *(Spec 12)*
- **T-EXIT-17**: Invalid target string (e.g., `":script"`) → code 1. *(Spec 12)*

---

## 5. Fuzz Testing

Fuzz tests use `fast-check` for property-based testing. They are designed to find edge cases that manual test enumeration misses.

### 5.1 Structured Output Fuzzer

**File:** `tests/fuzz/output-parsing.fuzz.test.ts`

**Approach:** Generate random strings and feed them as the stdout of a script in a workflow. Verify invariants hold for all inputs.

#### Generators

| Generator | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `arbitraryJSON` | Random valid JSON values (objects, arrays, strings, numbers, booleans, null) |
| `arbitraryString` | Random strings including unicode, control characters, empty, very long |
| `arbitraryOutputObject` | Random objects with `result`, `goto`, `stop` fields of various types |
| `arbitraryMalformedJSON` | Strings that look like JSON but are malformed |

#### Properties

- **F-PARSE-01: No crashes.** For any string written to stdout, loopx does not crash. Exits with code 0 or code 1. Never any other exit code for non-signal cases.
- **F-PARSE-02: Deterministic parsing.** Same stdout → same behavior.
- **F-PARSE-03: Type safety of parsed output.** `result` is always string, `goto` is always string, `stop` is always `true`.
- **F-PARSE-04: Raw fallback consistency.** Non-structured stdout → entire stdout becomes `result`.
- **F-PARSE-05: Non-ASCII safe.** UTF-8 with NUL bytes, control characters, high Unicode does not cause crashes.

**Iterations:** At least 1000 at unit-parser level (via `parseOutput` seam), 50–100 at E2E level.

### 5.2 Env File Fuzzer

**File:** `tests/fuzz/env-parsing.fuzz.test.ts`

#### Properties

- **F-ENV-01: No crashes.**
- **F-ENV-02: Deterministic parsing.**
- **F-ENV-03: Keys and values are strings.**
- **F-ENV-04: Last-wins for duplicates.**
- **F-ENV-05: Comment lines never produce variables.**

**Iterations:** At least 1000 at unit-parser level (via `parseEnvFile` seam), 50–100 at E2E level.

---

## 6. Supplementary Unit Tests

### 6.1 Output Parsing Unit Tests

**File:** `tests/unit/parse-output.test.ts`

Uses the `parseOutput` internal seam (section 1.4). Tests the parser function directly with valid JSON objects, type coercion cases, edge cases, non-object JSON values, and malformed JSON.

### 6.2 Env Parsing Unit Tests

**File:** `tests/unit/parse-env.test.ts`

Uses the `parseEnvFile` internal seam (section 1.4). Tests standard KEY=VALUE pairs, comments, blank lines, quoted values, duplicate keys, and edge cases.

### 6.3 Source Detection Unit Tests

**File:** `tests/unit/source-detection.test.ts`

Test the source classification logic (section 10.1) in isolation:

- `org/repo` → git (github)
- Various URLs → correct source type (`"git"` or `"tarball"`)
- URLs that would be single-file → throws (single-file URL install removed)
- Edge cases: URLs with ports, auth, paths, query strings

### 6.4 Compile-Time Type Tests

**File:** `tests/unit/types.test.ts`

**Required execution method:** Vitest typecheck mode, `tsc --noEmit`, or `tsd`.

- **T-TYPE-01**: `import type { Output, RunOptions } from "loopx"` compiles without error. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-TYPE-02**: `Output` has optional `result?: string`, `goto?: string`, `stop?: boolean` fields. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-TYPE-03**: `RunOptions` has optional `maxIterations?: number`, `envFile?: string`, `signal?: AbortSignal`, `cwd?: string`, and `env?: Record<string, string>` fields. Assert that `RunOptions` shape matches the Spec 9.5 definition exactly: each field is optional and has the specified type. A `RunOptions` value with only `env: { FOO: "bar" }` must type-check; a value with `env: { FOO: 42 }` must be a static type error (value is not a string); a value with `env: "not-an-object"` must be a static type error. *(Spec 9.5)*
- **T-TYPE-04**: `run()` returns `AsyncGenerator<Output>`. *(Spec 9.1, 9.5)*
- **T-TYPE-05**: `runPromise()` returns `Promise<Output[]>`. *(Spec 9.2, 9.5)*
- **T-TYPE-06**: `run()` and `runPromise()` accept an optional `RunOptions` second argument. *(Spec 9.1, 9.2, 9.5)*
- **T-TYPE-07**: `run()` and `runPromise()` require `target` as the first argument (`string`). Omitting `target` is a static type error. *(Spec 9.1, 9.2, 9.5)*

---

## 7. Edge Cases & Boundary Tests

- **T-EDGE-01**: Very long result string (~1 MB). Handled without truncation or hang. *(Spec 2.3)*
- **T-EDGE-02**: Result containing JSON-special characters. Correct serialization/deserialization. *(Spec 2.3)*
- **T-EDGE-03**: Script that writes stdout in multiple `write()` calls. Full output captured. *(Spec 2.3)*
- **T-EDGE-04**: Script that writes to both stdout and stderr. No interleaving issues. *(Spec 6.2, 6.3)*
- **T-EDGE-05**: Unicode in result values and env values preserved. Unicode in workflow/script names rejected (ASCII-only pattern). *(Spec 2.3, 5.3, 8.1)*
- **T-EDGE-06**: Deeply nested goto chain (A → B → C → ... → Z) including cross-workflow hops. Correct execution order and iteration counting. *(Spec 7.1)*
- **T-EDGE-07**: Script that produces output on stdout but also reads from stdin when no input is available. No deadlock. *(Spec 6.7)*
- **T-EDGE-11**: `-n` with very large value (e.g., `999999`). No integer overflow. *(Spec 4.2)*
- **T-EDGE-12**: Empty `.loopx/` directory (exists but no workflows). `loopx run ralph` → error. `loopx run -h` → run help with no workflows listed. *(Spec 4.1, 11.2)*
- **T-EDGE-14**: Env file with no newline at end of file. Last line still parsed. *(Spec 8.1)*
- **T-EDGE-15**: Env file that is completely empty (0 bytes). No error, no variables loaded. *(Spec 8.1)*

---

## 8. CI Configuration

### 8.1 Runtime Matrix

| Runtime | Versions |
|---------|----------|
| Node.js | 20.6 (minimum), latest LTS, latest current |
| Bun | 1.0 (minimum), latest |

### 8.2 Pipeline Stages

1. **Build**: Compile/bundle loopx.
2. **Phase 0 (Harness)**: Run `tests/harness/`. Fail the pipeline if any fail.
3. **Typecheck**: Run `tsc --noEmit` or `vitest typecheck` on `tests/unit/types.test.ts`.
4. **Unit Tests**: Run `tests/unit/`.
5. **E2E Tests**: Run `tests/e2e/`. Parameterized over runtime matrix.
6. **Fuzz Tests**: Run `tests/fuzz/` with CI-appropriate iteration count (e.g., 5000).
7. **Stub Validation** (optional, periodic): Run spec tests against stub binary.

### 8.3 Timeouts

| Suite | Timeout per test |
|-------|-----------------|
| Harness | 10s |
| Unit | 5s |
| E2E | 30s |
| E2E (signals) | 60s |
| Fuzz | 120s |

### 8.4 Parallelism

- Vitest runs test files in parallel by default. Each test file uses isolated temp directories.
- Signal tests should run serially within their file.
- Install tests that start local servers should share a single server instance per file.

---

## 9. Pending Spec Decisions

All previously identified spec problems (SP-15 through SP-31) have been resolved.

**Currently pending:**
- SP-32 (SSH/SCP URL classification — SPEC.md section 10.1 does not mention SSH or SCP-style URLs. No tests added until resolved.)
